# 16 тАФ Dispatcher Backlog

Working backlog for items extracted from `input/input_raw.md`. Each row
points to the originating line range so context is recoverable.

**Convention:** items are dispatched in rounds; each round runs as one
or more parallel sub-agents on the
`claude/implement-input-raw-changes-2WiOF` branch (or worktree of it).
Status legend:

- `queued` тАФ vetted, waiting for dispatch slot
- `in-progress` тАФ agent is working (note round + agent ID/branch)
- `done` тАФ landed in this branch (commit hash)
- `blocked` тАФ needs user input (note reason)
- `parked` тАФ out of scope for this branch (e.g. dataship work, infra)

## Scope filter

`input_raw.md` mixes work for at least three projects:

1. `dlr-shepard/shepard` (this repo, Java/Quarkus backend + Nuxt 3 / Vue 3 /
   Vuetify 3 frontend + client libs) тАФ **in scope**. (Earlier rounds said
   "Angular"; corrected by the `aidocs/33` agent which verified against
   `frontend/package.json:24,45-46`.)
2. `dlr-shepard/shepard-dataship` (separate Python client; M1тАУM9 milestones
   on lines 975тАУ1214 reference `src/ui/*.py`, `src/worker.py`, etc.) тАФ
   **out of scope here**, parked.
3. Program-level work (HMC, federation, project website, AAS) тАФ **parked**,
   not implementable from this repo.

## Backlog (this repo only)

| PM1a | `PluginManifest` SPI + `PluginRegistry` (`@ApplicationScoped`, observes `StartupEvent` post-migrations) + `backend/plugins/` drop-in directory + Dockerfile mount-point + flip UH1a from source-stitched to drop-in JAR (the first real plugin under the new shape). | user direction 2026-05-13, ADR-0023 | M | **shipped** | This PR. | PM1b2 | `JarSignatureVerifier` for untrusted JARs (four `shepard.plugins.signing.*` config keys, default `required=false`); semver-range enforcement of `shepardCompatibility()` (incompatible plugins land in `FAILED` state with `plugin.compatibility.failed` / `plugin.compatibility.unparseable` failureMessages; `shepard.plugins.compatibility.strict=true` default + operator-override valve); `DEGRADED` lifecycle state + `PluginEntry.markDegraded()` lifecycle hook (forward placeholder for PM1b3 тАФ child-classloader CDI integration deferred to PM1b3 per `aidocs/69`). `VersionRange` parser extended to accept the npm/Composer-style operator-comma syntax (`>=5.2.0,<6`) every existing plugin manifest already uses. | тАФ | M | **shipped** | This PR. Backend: new `de.dlr.shepard.plugin.{JarSignatureVerifier, JarSignatureException}` (`@ApplicationScoped`; JDK's `JarFile(verify=true)` + `KeyStore.getInstance("JKS"/"PKCS12")` for trust-anchor loading; fail-soft on malformed truststore); `PluginRegistry.enforceCompatibility()` runs between discovery + dependency-resolution so compat failures pre-empt dependent's `plugin.dependency.missing` (more accurate root-cause reporting); `PluginRegistry.verifyJarSignature()` + `applySignatureOutcome()` hook into `loadJarPlugin()` so failed-signature entries land in `FAILED` with operator visibility in `GET /v2/admin/plugins`. `PluginState` grows `DEGRADED`. `PluginEntry.markDegraded()` added. Five new config keys (`shepard.plugins.signing.required` / `.trust-anchors` / `.truststore.path` / `.truststore.password` / `shepard.plugins.compatibility.strict`) all default-safe. Trackers (`aidocs/16` PM1 umbrella тЖТ PM1b2 shipped + PM1b3 queued; `aidocs/34` PM1b2 AWARE row; `aidocs/44` plugin-runtime-hardening row; `aidocs/63 ADR-0023` forward-work тАФ JarSignatureVerifier + semver-compat enforcement ticked, child-classloader CDI integration deferred to PM1b3) + reference docs (`docs/reference/plugins.md` ┬з"Signing + compatibility enforcement" with the operator runbook + `jarsigner` workflow) + new design doc `aidocs/platform/69-runtime-plugin-cdi.md` for the deferred PM1b3 slice all updated in this PR. `PluginEntryIO.state` schema description extended to mention `DEGRADED`. **No new endpoints** тАФ state flows through existing `GET /v2/admin/plugins`. **No Cypher migration** тАФ runtime-config-only changes. |
| PM1b3 | True runtime CDI integration тАФ a vendor drops `shepard-plugin-foo-x.y.z.jar` into `/deployments/plugins/` at runtime and its REST endpoints + admin CLI subcommand come up **without** declaring the plugin in the backend's `with-plugins` Maven profile. Option B (per the `aidocs/69` analysis): extend `PluginContext` with `registerHttpRoute(pathPattern, handler)` so plugins ship Vert.x handlers instead of `@Path` resources (side-steps Quarkus's build-time CDI scanning); wire `PluginRegistry` to a singleton `PluginRouter` that manages the live Vert.x route table. PM1b2's `DEGRADED` state becomes the auto-detection signal: a JAR-walk plugin without a matching `quarkus.index-dependency.*` config key lands DEGRADED with `plugin.runtime.no-cdi-scan` and the failureMessage points at the runbook. Ship a vendor-style example plugin (`plugins/example-video/`) that's NOT in the `with-plugins` profile, demonstrating the drop-in path end-to-end. | `aidocs/69 ┬з4`, ADR-0023 forward-work | M-L | queued | Quarkus's build-time CDI scanner doesn't expose a runtime bean-addition API (verified against Quarkus 3.27.x source); the structurally correct fix is to give plugins a non-CDI HTTP-handler shape. See `aidocs/69` for the full reasoning + the Option A (per-plugin Quarkus extension) vs Option B (Vert.x router) trade-off. |

### Newly surfaced (second-pass analysis of `input_raw.md` lines 1840тАУ8409)

These come from a re-read of regions the first scan missed. `R7` deduplicates with existing `L1`. `R2` (RO-Crate) is **already implemented** in this repo (`ExportConstants.ROCRATE_METADATA`); only the per-payload selection enhancement remains. Most others are blocked on user/maintainer decisions.

| ID | Item | input_raw refs | Size | Status | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| R1 | Databus + MOSS federation layer (`shepard-plugin-databus`) | 8380 | M | **design done** | `aidocs/77`. Full design: `:DatabusConfig` admin entity, admin REST + CLI parity, researcher-facing `POST /v2/collections/{appId}/publish/databus`, PROV-O Turtle generation, `shepard` MOSS module definition (SHACL + indexer). MB1aтАУMB1g phasing. Gated on PROV1a (`:Activity` capture, `aidocs/55`) and the MOSS module YAML landing in the DLR-internal Databus instance. |
| R2 | Per-payload selective RO-Crate export (refinement of existing export) | 8381 | SтАУM | **Phase 1 done** | Round 6, commit `be0eb26` (cherry-picked). Existing exporter lives in `backend/src/main/java/de/dlr/shepard/context/export/` (`ExportService` is the walker entry point, `ExportBuilder` wraps `edu.kit.datamanager.ro_crate.RoCrate.RoCrateBuilder`). Phase 1 adds an optional `ExportSelection` body on a **new** sibling `POST /collections/{collectionId}/export` (the existing GET is preserved unchanged for byte-identical legacy behaviour). Selection has two sections: `payloads` (`include` allow-list of kinds + `excludeIds` deny-list) and `metadata` booleans (permissions / annotations / labJournal / versions / subscriptions). The selection actually applied is recorded as a JSON block on the root data entity in `ro-crate-metadata.json` so consumers can tell what was excluded. 18 tests pass (5 new selection-service + 2 new manifest-injection + 11 pre-existing). **Important:** the exporter today does **not** yet emit `permissions / versions / subscriptions / annotations` documents тАФ the booleans are wired and recorded but bundling those metadata kinds is deferred to **R2d**. |
| R2b | File- and column-level selection on payloads (per-FileReference oid include list; per-TimeseriesReference column / time-window picks) | тАФ | M | done | Round 6, commit `60a3ea1`. Adds `payloads.perPayload: Map<entityId, PerPayloadSelection>` and `payloads.strictPerPayload: boolean`. `PerPayloadSelection` has optional `fileOids`, `columns`, `timeRange{start,end}` тАФ kind-applicability is silent (wrong-kind entries ignored). Existing per-OID file-fetch service reused; existing `fieldFilterSet` parameter on `TimeseriesReferenceService.exportReferencedTimeseriesByShepardId` covers per-column projection; a new 14-arg overload accepts `startNanosOverride` / `endNanosOverride` for time-window without mutating the reference. Stale OIDs / unknown columns silently skipped + recorded in a new `selection.warnings[]` array on the manifest's root selection block; `strictPerPayload=true` flips that to 400. 11 new tests pass (43/43 export-package). P17b lint stays green. |
| R2c | Per-payload metadata-field redaction (e.g. include the annotation but redact its label) | тАФ | M | done | Round 6, commit `f993e8b`. Adds `metadata.redactFields: Set<RedactableField>` to `ExportSelection`. **Closed enum** of 6 fields, each verified against the actual IO type before shipping (one stop-and-report adjustment): `PERMISSION_USERNAME` (replaces `owner` + `reader[]` + `writer[]` + `manager[]`), `PERMISSION_GROUP_IDS` (empties `readerGroupIds` / `writerGroupIds` тАФ renamed from proposed `тАж_GROUP_NAME` because `PermissionsIO` carries group ids only), `ANNOTATION_LABEL` (replaces `propertyName` тАФ proposed `label` doesn't exist; IRI left intact as stable id), `ANNOTATION_VALUE` (replaces `valueName` тАФ proposed `value` doesn't exist), `VERSION_AUTHOR` (replaces `createdBy` тАФ no `author` field), `LAB_JOURNAL_CONTENT` (replaces `journalContent`). Mutation is direct setter on the Lombok `@Data` IO types before serialisation. Manifest selection block records the **set** but not the replacement values (no leak vector). 11 new tests pass; 54/54 export-package total. |
| R2d | Emit permissions / versions / subscriptions / semantic-annotations documents from the exporter (the metadata booleans from R2 Phase 1 are wired but the exporter currently doesn't bundle these doc kinds) | тАФ | M | **mostly done** | Round 6, commit `d5fa03c`. **3 of 4 kinds wired:** `permissions` (via `PermissionsService.getPermissionsOfEntityOptional`), `versions` (via `VersionService.getAllVersions`; collection-only тАФ only Collections are versioned), `annotations` (via `BasicEntity.getAnnotations()`). Defaults remain `false` so today's behaviour is unchanged. 14 new tests pass on merged branch (10 service-level in `ExportMetadataBundleTest`, 4 builder-level in `ExportBuilderSelectionTest`). **`subscriptions` deferred** тАФ see **R2d2** below. |
| R2d2 | Emit per-entity subscriptions in the RO-Crate export тАФ needs a URL-pattern тЖТ entity-URL matcher because subscriptions in shepard are URL-pattern-based, not per-entity-attached | тАФ | M | done | Round 6, commit `967fbf5`. New `SubscriptionMatcher` extracted from `SubscriptionFilter` (pure refactor; `SubscriptionFilterTest` 7/7 pass); new `EntityUrlSynthesiser` produces canonical paths for Collection / DataObject / BasicReference / LabJournalEntry using the same `Constants.*` tokens the JAX-RS resources use. Walker hook calls `subscriptionService.getMatchingSubscriptionsForUrl(url, method)` and writes `<id>-subscriptions.json` per entity. **Documented trade-off:** subscription patterns are full-URL regexes (scheme + host); export only knows the path, so authors of host-anchored patterns may need a `.*` prefix to also match exports. 7 new tests pass; 43+ on merged branch. |

### Permission-system evolutions (from `aidocs/24`, 2026-05-05)

| ID | Item | Size | Status | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| F1 | Declarative `@Authz(action, resource)` annotation seam replacing the path-segment switch in `PermissionsService.isAllowed` | M | queued | **Same proposal as P5.** Designed so a future `PolicyDecisionPoint` (OPA / Cedar) is a drop-in (~┬╜-day add). Unblocks the path-segment-switch problem that L2c also needs to solve. |
| F2 | Group / sharing model: `Group` Neo4j node with `(User)-[:member_of]->(Group)-[:has_permissions]->(Permissions)-[:has_permissions]->(Entity)` | L | queued | Major gap for a research-data platform. Includes manager-groups + grant inheritance. |
| F3 | Permission audit log (Postgres table) for grants/revokes | SтАУM | **тЬУ shipped** | `V1.10.0__add_permission_audit_log_table.sql` тАФ `permission_audit_log` table (BIGSERIAL PK, TIMESTAMPTZ, entity_app_id, entity_kind, actor_username, action, detail_json). `PermissionAuditLogService` (ApplicationScoped, AgroalDataSource, fire-and-forget). Hooked into all three write paths in `PermissionsService`: `createPermissions` тЖТ GRANT, `updatePermissionsByNeo4jId` тЖТ UPDATE (before/after JSON), `deletePermissions` тЖТ REVOKE. `GET /v2/admin/permission-audit/log` (`@RolesAllowed("instance-admin")`, params: entityAppId, actor, from, to ISO-8601, page/size). 13 new unit tests. |
| F4 | Versioned cache invalidation key: `(entityId, AccessType, userSub, jwtIat)` | S | **тЬУ shipped** | Changed `isAccessTypeAllowedForUser` signature from 3-arg to 4-arg; 4th arg `jwtIat` is the JWT `iat` claim (seconds-since-epoch, default `0L` when no JWT or no iat). `JWTPrincipal` gained an `iat` field; `JWTFilter.parsePrincipalFromAccessToken()` extracts `body.getIssuedAt()`. Services with `AuthenticationContext` pass `currentIat()` (reads `authenticationContext.getPrincipal().getIat()`); REST resources and the cache warmer without live-request context pass `0L`. `CompositeCacheKey` now 4-tuple. 4 new `PermissionsServiceIatCacheKeyTest` tests. |
| F5 | Explicit fail-closed invariant when Neo4j is degraded | S | **тЬУ shipped** | Added `dbHealthRegistry.isCurrentlyDown(DatabaseKind.NEO4J)` guard at the top of `PermissionsService.isAllowed()`: returns `false` immediately when Neo4j is DOWN without calling the DAO. Null-safe (guards against `@InjectMocks` test environments). 3 new `PermissionsServiceNeo4jGuardTest` tests covering: DOWN returns false without DAO call; UP does not short-circuit; guard is independent of username. |
| F6 | Design F1's seam so a future OPA / Cedar `PolicyDecisionPoint` is a drop-in | XS (within F1) | **тЬУ shipped (2026-05-26)** | **Verdict from `aidocs/24`:** No to OPA/Cedar adoption now (overkill for a single Quarkus service with small graph-shaped policy); yes to making the seam future-proof at half-day cost. Shipped: `PolicyDecisionPoint` interface (`auth/permission/services/PolicyDecisionPoint.java`); `GraphPolicyDecisionPoint` `@ApplicationScoped` CDI bean delegates to `PermissionsService.isAccessTypeAllowedForUser` (fast path via `EntityIdResolver`) and `isAccessAllowedForDataObjectAppId` (DataObject fallback). Class-level Javadoc added to `PermissionsService`. 3 new `GraphPolicyDecisionPointTest` cases (allowed, denied, DataObject fallback). F1 wires `@Authz` annotation that calls this PDP. |
| F7 | Row-level security in TimescaleDB / PostGIS тАФ denormalise ACLs into the data DBs | L | parked тАФ conditions for unparking listed in `aidocs/24` | **Verdict:** No for v1. Backend is the only enforcement point; replicating ACLs into Postgres adds a second source of truth with no current threat-model justification. Conditions for a flip: more than one client bypasses the backend, or read fanout becomes the dominant cost. |
| F8 | Configurable OIDC roles-claim path (`shepard.oidc.roles-claim-path`, default `realm_access.roles`); `JWTFilter` walks the dot-path so non-Keycloak IdPs (Pocket ID, Authentik, Azure AD) can carry roles in their native claim shape | XS-S | **done** | Bundled with **A0** (`2901834`). `shepard.instance-admin.role` (default empty = no IdP-side admin) names the role-string within the claim that maps to `instance-admin`. CONFIG-status row in `aidocs/34`. |

## Open user decisions (blocking some items)

1. **Leaked JWTs** at `aidocs/input/input_raw.md:222` and `:360` (issuers
   `bt-au-cube2.intra.dlr.de`, `bt-au-cube3.intra.dlr.de`, sub `kreb_fl`).
   Already on `origin`. Need: rotate tokens, decide whether to redact in
   the file, and whether to rewrite history.
2. ~~**API versioning (P4)** is breaking тАФ confirm strategy
   (`/shepard/api/v1` prefix, dual-serve, deprecation window) before
   dispatching.~~ тАФ **resolved**: shipped non-breaking. Upstream
   `/shepard/api/...` stays byte-frozen via explicit class-level
   `@Path("/shepard/api/...")` prefix; new fork-additive endpoints land
   under `/v2/` (per `CLAUDE.md` API-version policy). User-facing URLs
   unchanged.
3. **Templates system (L3)** is large and design-heavy тАФ needs a written
   design before implementation.
4. **Neo4J ID migration (L2)** is large and touches a lot of code тАФ needs
   a written design before implementation.
5. **Admin role mechanism (A0)** тАФ A3b discovered there is no admin auth
   in shepard today. JWT roles are always `new String[0]`, so
   `@RolesAllowed("admin")` denies everyone. Three paths offered:
   (a) full admin-role mechanism populating roles from OIDC claims
   (~50 lines + config), (b) dev-profile-only exposure of admin
   endpoints, (c) scope-shift admin endpoints to `/temp/admin/*` with
   the same auth as the existing `/temp/migrations/*` carve-out and
   harden later. Affects A3b, P3c.
6. **R-series items (R1тАУR9)** from the second-pass input analysis are
   mostly blocked on design / framework / asset decisions тАФ see
   "Newly surfaced" table.

### Round 4 тАФ 2026-05-05 (analysis layer)

While Round 3 implementation agents ran, four parallel **analysis-only**
agents produced strategic / design docs requested by the maintainer:

| Doc | Purpose | Status | Commit |
|---|---|---|---|
| `aidocs/platform/19-architecture-feedback.md` | Critical review of post-Round-3 architecture | done | `879ffc0` |
| `aidocs/platform/20-epic-roadmap.md` | 14-epic catalogue with Mermaid dependency graph + 2-track 6-month plan | done | `fc4ae3b` |
| `aidocs/archive/21-user-interest-gauge.md` | Demand signals for HDF5/HSDS, tabular, KG interfaces + survey plan | done | `362712e` |
| `aidocs/ops/22-admin-cli-draft.md` | Candidate functions for a future `shepard-admin` CLI | done | `452eded` |

**Key findings from these docs that should drive Round 4 priorities:**

- **`aidocs/19` flags two security fragilities at the top:**
  - **C3 fallback** at `PermissionsService.java:262+` тАФ when the
    permissions node is missing, the fallback grants Reader+Writer+Manager.
    This is a full-access backdoor catalogued in
    `aidocs/archive/07-security-issues.md` C3 тАФ **not new, but not yet fixed**.
  - **C5 Cypher injection** at `Neo4jQueryBuilder.java:198-244` тАФ
    string-concatenated query construction; cross-cuts every search
    endpoint and gates `aidocs/semantics/13-search-improvements.md`.
  - Plus **A0** (admin role) тАФ already in our backlog.
- **`aidocs/20` recommends two parallel tracks:**
  - **Foundations track:** E1 (foundations: A0 + observability + P4 + L6 + S1) тЖТ E5 (streaming + ID alignment) тЖТ E11 (permissions + admin CLI) тЖТ E2 (unified search v2).
  - **User-value track:** E12 (UX & ecosystem) тЖТ E6 (annotation generalisation) тЖТ E9 (spatial graduate/deprecate) тЖТ E4 (triplestore + SPARQL).
  - Three "could start tomorrow" epics: **E1, E5, E12**.
  - Three "blocked on user decision" epics: **E14** (Neo4j ID migration owner), **E9** (spatial graduate vs deprecate), **E4** (default ontology + reasoning profile + n10s deployment).
- **`aidocs/21` ranks the three candidate development directions:**
  - **KG interfaces:** strongest evidence (4 open GitLab issues, partial `SparqlConnector` already, two independent user groups). Ready to act once #274 unblocks.
  - **HDF5/HSDS:** low-medium; one named asker, no GitLab issue, TimescaleDB satisfies the temporal subset. **Maintainer-confirmed hard constraint (2026-05-05):** any HDF5 surface must be compatible with the existing Python ecosystem (`h5py` / `PyTables` / `pandas.read_hdf`) тАФ `h5pyd` over HSDS is the canonical access path; "download original file" is the fallback. Recorded in epic E7 (`aidocs/platform/20-epic-roadmap.md:309-329`) and ┬з3.6 of `aidocs/archive/21-user-interest-gauge.md`.
  - **Tabular/relational:** thin; the ask hides two distinct products (interface vs storage). Defer until separated.

| PERF2b | Recommender тАФ `scripts/perf/recommend.py` reads `last-run.json` + Prometheus instant queries тЖТ 3-5 ranked suggestions | user request 2026-05-12, `aidocs/59 ┬з4` | M | **тЬУ shipped** | `scripts/perf/recommend.py`. stdlib-only Python 3.9+. Six rules: `search_threshold_breach` (k6 p95 > 3000ms тЖТ Neo4j page-cache), `collections_threshold_breach` (k6 p95 > 800ms тЖТ perms-cache), `jvm_heap_too_small` (heap > 85% тЖТ -Xmx), `gc_pauses_high` (GC max > 200ms тЖТ G1GC), `permissions_cache_cold` (hit rate < 60% тЖТ cache size + TTL), `mongo_latency_high` (avg cmd > 50ms тЖТ pool size). Prometheus queries for JVM heap, GC pause, perms-cache hit ratio, Mongo latency; falls back gracefully when Prometheus is unreachable. `--json` for machine-readable output; `--output FILE`; `--dry-run` uses canned data. Exit 0 = healthy, exit 1 = suggestions found (CI-friendly), exit 2 = error. |

The cipher format includes a `gcm1:` prefix marker so a future cipher upgrade can recognise the legacy shape. **Versioned PIDs (KIP1h respect)**: `DataciteMinter` reads `MintRequest.versionNumber()` directly (KIP1h made it a first-class field), encodes as `version: "v<n>"` in the DataCite request body, and adds `relatedIdentifiers: [{ relationType: IsNewVersionOf, ... }]` for n > 1 тАФ plus a back-fill `PUT /dois/<previous>` that stamps the inverse `HasVersion` so the chain renders both ways in DataCite Commons. Previous-PID lookup is delegated to a `PreviousPublicationResolver` interface that defaults to a no-op (test-friendly; production wires it to the in-core `PublicationDAO` via the manifest hook). **Network hardening**: 10s connect + 30s request timeout on the JDK `HttpClient`; one retry on 5xx / network exception with 1s backoff; `MinterException` on second failure (caught by core `PublishService` тЖТ 500 `publish.minter.failed`). 4xx is final (no retry). **Resource-type mapping**: shepard's `digitalObjectType` (Dataset / Collection / Software / Text / Image) maps onto DataCite's `resourceTypeGeneral` vocabulary with `Dataset` as the safe default. **Event mapping**: DataCite `event` field set from `defaultState` тАФ `draft`/`registered`/`findable` тЖТ `draft`/`register`/`publish`. Migration: `V33__Add_appId_constraint_DataciteMinterConfig.cypher` (V31 + V32 are taken by KIP1h backfill + PM1e PluginRuntimeOverride). Password is NOT a deploy-time key (security posture; gitleaks would flag it). Default `api-base-url=https://api.test.datacite.org` (Fabrica test environment). ### DB-OPT тАФ 2026-05-23 (database optimisation against real-world data тАФ POST-IMPORT)

User directive 2026-05-23: *"after import we should do the database optimisation case we have real word data"*. The MFFD ingest is about to populate the multi-substrate stack with the first **real-world-scale** dataset (тЙИ8k DataObjects + their reference graph + tapelaying TS + bridgewelding TS). That's the perfect baseline for benchmark-driven optimisation. Sequencing: import lands тЖТ snapshot the post-import state тЖТ run the DB-OPT pass against real data тЖТ ship the wins. Builds on `### DB тАФ 2026-05-22` inventory + anti-pattern hunt; this section is the **action layer**.

| ID | Slice | Size | Status | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|

Output: `aidocs/agent-findings/db-baseline-post-mffd.md`. This is the reference point every optimisation is measured against. | S | **done** (doc `db-baseline-post-mffd.md`, 2026-05-26) | Blocks DB-OPT2..5. Unknown field тЖТ 400 before any DB hit. New `X-Shepard-Payload-Diet` response header surfaces the active mode. Diagnostic: `examples/mffd-showcase/scripts/diagnostics/measure-payload-diet.sh`. See `aidocs/34` DB-OPT5, `aidocs/44` row, `docs/reference/data-objects.md`. ### BATCH-API тАФ 2026-05-23 (bulk endpoints for metadata-heavy passes)

User directive 2026-05-23 after v16 deploy block landed: *"backlog batch API"*. v16's Pass 1 + Pass 2 issue tens of thousands of individual POST/PATCH calls (one per source DO) тАФ the metadata work that's cheap individually but expensive in aggregate. v16's 3-pass design is mainly bottlenecked here, not at the per-DO file/TS/SD write level.

A batch API on the dest reduces N round-trips to N/B (B = batch size, e.g. 100). For an MFFD-scale ingest with ~30K source DOs this is the difference between 30K HTTP calls and 300 тАФ likely **10-30├Ч speedup on Pass 1 + Pass 2** combined.

| ID | Slice | Size | Status | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| BATCH-API-1 | **Design + spec** тАФ endpoints under `/v2/` (the fork's development surface): `POST /v2/collections/{appId}/data-objects:batch` (bulk create, body = array of DataObjectIO with name/desc/attrs/parentAppId/predecessorAppIds, transactional or best-effort per `?mode=`); `PATCH /v2/collections/{appId}/data-objects:batch` (bulk update); same shape for `/v2/structured-data-containers/{appId}/payloads:batch` (bulk SD writes for tight ref groups). Body cap configurable (e.g. 1000 items / 10MB whichever smaller). Response: per-item `{index, id, appId, status, error?}`. | M | queued | OpenAPI spec lives in `backend/src/main/java/de/dlr/shepard/v2/.../resources/`. |
| BATCH-API-2 | **Backend implementation** тАФ Quarkus REST resource + service. Transaction shape per `?mode=`: `mode=atomic` rollback on any failure; `mode=besteffort` partial success returns per-item status (default). Reuses existing OGM + persistence logic; just amortizes session+transaction cost across N items. Optimistic-locking for PATCH (revision check per item). Permission check applies per item. | L | queued | Pairs with existing `DataObjectService.create/update` тАФ wraps in a `@Transactional` outer + per-item loop. |
| BATCH-API-3 | **Importer adoption** тАФ v16.5 importer uses batch endpoints when available. Pass 1: chunk all_src into batches of 100, POST `/v2/data-objects/batch`; map src_do_id тЖТ dest_appId from response array; resolve ogm id via GET for Pass 2/3 compatibility. Pass 2 stays per-DO PATCH (no batch PATCH yet). Auto-fallback to per-DO on 404. `--use-batch-api`/`--no-batch-api` flags. Telemetry: `batch_pass1_start`, `batch_pass1_chunk_success`, `batch_pass1_complete`. | M | **done** | Shipped in `mffd-import-v15.py` v16.5 (commit on main). BATCH-API-5 tests in `tests/test_v16_batch.py` (7 tests). |
| BATCH-API-4 | **Per-substrate batch primitives audit** тАФ see if Mongo `bulkWrite`, PostgreSQL `INSERT INTO ... VALUES (...), (...), ...`, TimescaleDB `COPY`, Neo4j `UNWIND` are being used optimally underneath BATCH-API-2's per-item loop. Eke out the last 2-3├Ч by collapsing the inner loop into a single substrate-native bulk op. | L | **done** (2026-05-27) | Findings: `aidocs/agent-findings/batch-api-audit-2026-05-27.md`. Key findings: (1) MongoDB has zero `insertMany`/`bulkWrite` calls тАФ highest headroom substrate; (2) Neo4j DO batch endpoint is sequential OGM loop тАФ UNWIND write path not wired (pattern proven in DAO reads); (3) BulkTrace* IO classes are dead code (`/channels/bulk` path in javadoc, no `@Path` wires it); (4) No batch presigned URLs; (5) No batch annotation create. Priority queue in findings doc. New backlog: DEADCODE-BULKTRACE (see below). |
| BATCH-API-5 | **Tests** тАФ `DataObjectBatchV2RestTest.java`: added 4 tests (atomic-mode `@Disabled` placeholder, oversized-batch-returns-400 documents actual behavior vs spec's 413, duplicate-names-no-constraint, all-failed-still-returns-207). Importer: `tests/test_v16_batch.py` (7 tests) covering chunking 250тЖТ3├Ч(100+100+50), fallback on 404, happy path, partial failure, resume skip, `--no-batch-api`, `_batch_supported=False` pre-set. | M | **done** | Shipped. Backend: 19 tests (1 `@Disabled`), 0 failures. Python: 7 tests, 0 failures. |

**Acceptance**: re-running a 30K-DO MFFD import with BATCH-API in place completes Pass 1 + Pass 2 in <5 min (vs ~50 min today). Pass 3 unchanged (workers=4 worker bound stays the bottleneck for payload-heavy work).

| ID | Slice | Size | Status | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| DEADCODE-BULKTRACE | **Remove orphaned BulkTrace IO classes** тАФ `BulkTraceRequestIO`, `BulkTraceResultIO`, `BulkTraceChannelIO` all carry javadoc referencing `POST /v2/timeseries-containers/{id}/channels/bulk` but no `@Path` annotation wires this path. The shipped bulk read endpoint is `/channels/data/bulk` using `BulkChannelDataRequestIO`. Delete or wire. Confirmed by `grep -rn 'channels/bulk' backend/src/main/java/` returning only javadoc strings. | XS | **done** (2026-05-27) | All three files deleted; dead imports removed from `TimeseriesContainerChannelsRest.java`. Surfaced by BATCH-API-4 audit (2026-05-27). |

### V16-PRESERVE-HIERARCHY тАФ 2026-05-23 (replace v15's flat shape with full source-DO tree replication)

User directive 2026-05-23 after v15 hit steady-state ingest: *"so under one DO many DOs could be and then another... DOs to the bottom тАФ along the way references ... is the script doing this"* + decision **B** when offered the trade-off. v15 flattens cube3's hierarchical DO tree (Step тЖТ Layer тЖТ Ply Group тЖТ Track) into a single step DO with thousands of refs whose names encode the source-DO identity. v16 ships the proper-fidelity design: replicate the source tree as actual dest DOs with parent/child + predecessor/successor edges + per-DO attributes.

**Fidelity gaps v15 has that v16 closes**:

- Source DO tree тЖТ flattened to single step DO (loses Layer / Ply Group / Track structure)
- Per-source-DO attributes тЖТ only step DO carries attrs (loses `layer_index`, `ply_orientation`, `track_idx`, `material_batch`, etc.)
- Per-source-DO predecessor/successor edges тЖТ not replicated (Track NтЖТN+1 chain lost)
- Per-source-DO timestamps тЖТ only step DO carries import-time stamp

**What stays from v15**:

- Predefined SD containers (645000 + 645003) тАФ these are SHARED across all leaf DOs of a step. Each leaf's structuredDataReference points at the shared container with its own oids list.
- TS container per step (e.g., 653673) тАФ same shared-container pattern.
- File container per source DO тАФ each source file lands as 1 file ref on the leaf dest DO that owned it in source.
- AUTH PROBE (v15.17), ENV-ALIAS (v15.17), uv-PEP-723 runner (v15.16), exit-0 break (v1.1), MFFD_SELFUPDATE / MFFD_CREATE_SEMANTIC_REPOS env opt-outs (v15.19) тАФ all carry forward unchanged.

| ID | Slice | Size | Status | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| V16-IMPL-1 | **Recursive source traversal** тАФ `iter_data_objects` extends to either (a) return all DOs incl. nested + script reconstructs tree via parentId, OR (b) recurse children explicitly. (a) is fewer cube3 round-trips; prefer it. Returned SourceDO must carry `parentId`, `childrenIds`, `predecessorIds`, `successorIds`, full `attributes`. | M | queued | Audit v5 `/collections/{c}/dataObjects` endpoint тАФ does it return all-depth or top-level-only? If top-level: need `/dataObjects/{d}/children` traversal. |
| V16-IMPL-2 | **Dest tree creation** тАФ for each source DO, create a dest DO whose parent is the dest-side mirror of the source's parent (step DO at the root). Two-pass: first pass creates all dest DOs without edges; second pass wires parent/child + predecessor/successor edges using a source-id тЖТ dest-id map. State file extends to map `src_do.do_id тЖТ dest_do_id` for resume safety. | L | queued | The two-pass is necessary because predecessor edges may forward-reference DOs not yet created. |
| V16-IMPL-3 | **Per-DO attribute copy** тАФ copy ALL source DO attributes verbatim plus standard `source_*` markers (per v15.10). No attribute is privileged; every key the source carries lands on dest. Critical for `layer_index`, `ply_orientation`, etc. which are the queryable identity of each Track. | S | **done (2026-05-27)** | `_SHEPARD_INTERNAL_ATTRS` frozenset filters out `appId`/`shepardId`/`createdBy`/`createdAt`/`updatedBy`/`updatedAt`/`deleted`. `_build_do_attrs()` copies remaining attrs + appends all four `source_*` markers. `self._source_version` cached from `_stamp_source_instance_attrs` so `/versionz` is fetched once, not per-DO. `_import_one_do` uses `_build_do_attrs`. Step DOs remain synthetic (no source attrs); that distinction is documented in the code. |
| V16-IMPL-4 | **Reference placement at the correct depth** тАФ file/TS/SD references land on the LEAF dest DO that carried the source ref, NOT on the step DO. Step DO becomes a pure parent container. State file granularity = per-source-DO-id ├Ч per-ref-kind ├Ч per-ref-id. | M | queued | The big behaviour change. v15's `dest_do_id = step_dest_do_id` becomes `dest_do_id = src_to_dest_map[src_do.do_id]`. |
| V16-IMPL-5 | **Resume safety** тАФ state file's `do_done`/`file_done`/`ts_done`/`structured_done` keys all key by SOURCE DO ID (not name). `dest_id_map` persisted to state so a resumed run knows the dest-side mapping. Idempotent: re-running over a half-done state yields zero duplicate dest DOs. | M | queued | Critical тАФ re-runs are the norm during ingest tuning. |
| V16-IMPL-6 | **Bridgewelding parallel paths** тАФ source has multiple `Execution YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM:SS` DOs under Bridgewelding, plus `Process Data N`, `AF_9` etc. These are sibling at the same depth (children of Bridgewelding step). v16 preserves them all as sibling dest DOs. | S | **done (2026-05-27)** | Verified: `walk_source_tree` yields every `do-NNNNN.json` sorted by filename; each sibling gets a distinct `stable_hash()` (keyed by `do_id:name`), no `already_done` collision. `do_id_map` keyed by source `do_id` тАФ no overwrite. `ThreadPoolExecutor` fans out one future per SourceDataObject so siblings run concurrently. Comment added to `_import_one_do` confirming the analysis and scoping the V16-IMPL-2 caveat (child-before-parent in single pass). |
| V16-IMPL-7 | **Test fixtures + unit tests** тАФ recursion correctness, two-pass edge wiring, resume safety, dest_id_map persistence. `tests/test_v16_hierarchy.py`. | M | queued | Before live deploy. |
| V16-IMPL-8 | **Deploy + re-run** тАФ wipe dest MFFD-Dropbox 652941 (already wiped per this row's prompt), launch v16 from clean state. ETA roughly same as v15 (cube3 source-pull is the bottleneck, not the dest writes). | S | blocked-on-1..7 | Cube redeploy + tmux launch using existing runbook. |

**Acceptance**: at completion, MFFD-Dropbox contains a tree of dest DOs matching cube3's source tree тАФ step DOs at the root, Layer / Ply Group / Track / Execution DOs nested below, leaf-DO references attached at the correct depth, predecessor/successor edges between sibling DOs preserved. UI shows the AFP digital thread structurally, not just as a flat ref-list.

### TSDB-DELETE-LIMIT тАФ 2026-05-23 (TimescaleDB DML decompression limit blocks TS container delete)

Surfaced during the MFFD-tapelaying triage (2026-05-23 ~13:36 UTC). `DELETE /shepard/api/timeseriesContainers/{id}` returns HTTP 500 for any TS container whose FK-cascade chain touches >100K rows in compressed chunks. The backend code is innocent тАФ TimescaleDB substrate config knob `timescaledb.max_tuples_decompressed_per_dml_transaction = 100000` (default) is the gate.

Stacktrace from backend log (ref `10295074-4c77-4319-92c7-406efac48288`):
```
JDBC exception executing SQL [ERROR: tuple decompression limit exceeded by operation
  Detail: current limit: 100000, tuples decompressed: 3487063
  Hint: Consider increasing timescaledb.max_tuples_decompressed_per_dml_transaction or set to 0 (unlimited).
  Where: SQL statement "DELETE FROM ONLY \"_timescaledb_internal\".\"_hyper_1_38_chunk\" WHERE $1 OPERATOR(pg_catalog.=) \"timeseries_id\""]
[delete from timeseries te1_0 where te1_0.container_id=?]
```

| ID | Slice | Size | Status | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| TSDB-DDL-1 | **Raise the decompression limit in the TimescaleDB container env.** Three placement options: (a) `ALTER SYSTEM SET timescaledb.max_tuples_decompressed_per_dml_transaction = 0` baked into a migration; (b) `command:` arg on the `timescaledb` service in `infrastructure/docker-compose.yml` (`-c timescaledb.max_tuples_decompressed_per_dml_transaction=0`); (c) `SET timescaledb.max_tuples_decompressed_per_dml_transaction = 0` per-session in the Hibernate / JDBC connection-pool initializer. Recommendation: **(b)** тАФ declarative, visible to operators in compose. `0` = unlimited; safe because Shepard's typical delete is admin-initiated. | S | **done** | Pairs with `feedback_db_audit_includes_stack.md` (compose env / driver knobs are in scope for DB-audit). Sister issue: explicit FK cascade trigger could be replaced by `drop_chunks()` for whole-container deletes тАФ see TSDB-DDL-2. |
| TSDB-DDL-2 | **Chunk-aware container delete path** тАФ for `DELETE /timeseriesContainers/{id}`, the right substrate primitive is `SELECT drop_chunks('timeseries_data_points', older_than => now())` scoped to `timeseries_id IN (SELECT id FROM timeseries WHERE container_id = ?)`, NOT row-by-row DELETE. Drops compressed chunks without decompression. Order-of-magnitude faster + bypasses the decompression-limit issue entirely. Replace the JPA cascade for whole-container TS deletes. | M | queued | This is the structural fix. TSDB-DDL-1 is the immediate unblock. |
| TSDB-DDL-3 | **Apply retroactively: today's TS-tapelaying consolidation** тАФ once TSDB-DDL-1 ships, the deferred 589657 + 599903 delete (528098 is strict superset, zero data loss) should succeed via the existing REST DELETE endpoint. Acceptance test for TSDB-DDL-1. | S | queued | Cross-references PRE-MUT-SNAP5 (which would gate this through a snapshot pair when that mechanism ships). |

### PRE-MUT-SNAP тАФ 2026-05-23 (pre-mutation snapshot mechanism тАФ gate on every cleanup / purge / migration)

User directive 2026-05-23, during the MFFD TS-tapelaying-duplicate triage: *"thats why we need provenance .. and snapshots on mutations"*. The trigger was a sloppy "duplicate-looking" call on 3 TS containers (528098/589657/599903) where a row-level spot-check turned out to be required to confirm safe-to-delete; the REST DELETE 500'd before any harm was done, but the **structural fix is to gate every mutation behind a snapshot pair**, not rely on backend failure as the safety net.

Builds on `project_snapshot_boundaries.md` (existing memory: "every larger transformation gets a snapshot pair") + `feedback_referenced_data_infinite_retention.md` (referenced data has infinite retention; only orphans are deletion-eligible) тАФ this section ships the mechanism so those rules are enforced, not just documented.

| ID | Slice | Size | Status | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| PRE-MUT-SNAP1 | **Pre-mutation snapshot contract** тАФ design doc `aidocs/ops/<NN>-pre-mutation-snapshots.md`. Defines: every mutation pathway (cleanup / purge / migration / storage rebalance / FS1e move / SM1 orphan-collect) MUST take a pre-mutation snapshot of the affected scope BEFORE the first destructive operation. Scope = the substrate slice that would be mutated (e.g. `timeseries_data_points WHERE container_id IN (...)` + the corresponding Neo4j subgraph + Mongo collections + Garage objects). Snapshot artefact = a `:Snapshot` DataObject in a dedicated `snapshots-system` collection with PROV-O attribution of WHO triggered it + WHAT it covers + the artefact hash. Snapshots are retained for a configurable grace window (default: 90 days). | M | queued | Companion to `project_snapshot_boundaries.md`. Cite `feedback_referenced_data_infinite_retention.md` as the kill-switch criterion. |
| PRE-MUT-SNAP2 | **Substrate-native snapshot primitives** тАФ implement the per-substrate snapshot operations the contract requires. TimescaleDB: `INSERT INTO snapshots.<table>_snap SELECT * FROM <table> WHERE <scope>`. Neo4j: `apoc.export.cypher.query(scope-cypher, file, {format:'plain'})` to a snapshot artefact. Mongo: `db.<coll>.aggregate([{$match: scope}, {$out: 'snapshots.<coll>_<session>'}])`. Garage: `garage bucket snapshot` (if available) or `garage block download` + tar. Each primitive returns a `SnapshotResult{substrate, scope, rowCount, sizeBytes, artefactUri, sha256, durationMs}`. | M | queued | Lives in backend (Java) `de.dlr.shepard.ops.SnapshotService` + a Quarkus REST surface `POST /v2/admin/snapshots`. |
| PRE-MUT-SNAP3 | **Gate every mutation pathway** тАФ wire SnapshotService into every existing cleanup / migration / purge entry point: the orphan-wipe scripts under `examples/mffd-showcase/scripts/`, the SM1 `purgeOrphans` operation (task #74), the FS1e migration runner, the `mffd-completeness-check.py` consolidation suggestion (when it gets that), and the `shepard-admin <feature> set-*` commands that touch data. Gate behaviour: `--no-snapshot` flag REQUIRED to skip; default = take snapshot, refuse to proceed if snapshot fails. | L | queued | Touches тЙе5 entry points. Land incrementally per pathway тАФ don't block ship of the mechanism on full coverage. |
| PRE-MUT-SNAP4 | **Rollback runbook** тАФ `docs/admin/runbooks/rollback-from-snapshot.md`. Single-page operator procedure: given a snapshot id, restore the affected scope. Per the `feedback_admin_runbooks_pattern.md` contract: numbered steps, host indicator per step, expected stdout, end-state verification (a fresh `SELECT COUNT(*)` matching the pre-snapshot count). Includes the cross-substrate restore order (Neo4j тЖТ TimescaleDB тЖТ Mongo тЖТ Garage) so referential integrity holds. | M | queued | Pairs with `feedback_admin_runbooks_pattern.md` (runbook contract) + `ADMIN-RUNBOOKS-LIBRARY` (the systematic library this row contributes to). |
| PRE-MUT-SNAP5 | **Apply retroactively: today's TS-tapelaying triage** тАФ once the mechanism ships, the deferred MFFD-tapelaying consolidation (528098 keep, 589657 + 599903 delete) goes through the new path: snapshot first, then DELETE. Closes the loop on the situation that motivated the row. | S | queued | This is the **acceptance test**: if PRE-MUT-SNAP1..4 are right, this consolidation should be a two-line operator script. |

| DB-AP1 | **Anti-pattern hunt** тАФ find every site that violates a known good practice. Candidates: string-concat'd Cypher (C5/C5b killed them but regressions grow back), N+1 query patterns (Neo4j AND Postgres), missing indices on hot-path foreign keys, GridFS used for files when Garage S3 is active, missing `ON DELETE CASCADE` on Postgres FKs where the parent is mutable, missing constraints on `:HasAppId` Neo4j labels, Mongo collections without TTL where the data is ephemeral. | DB-AP2 | **Cross-cutting findings** тАФ patterns that span substrates. E.g. dual-source-of-truth (same field written to Neo4j AND Postgres), substrate-mismatch (timeseries lives in Timescale but the Neo4j `:Timeseries` label still carries denormalised metadata that can drift), schema-evolution gaps (migration added the field but the IO class doesn't surface it). Highest-value findings per SSOT discipline (`feedback_shacl_single_source_of_truth.md`). | M | queued | DB-AP1 enables DB-AP2 тАФ run AP1 first per substrate, then AP2 reads the union. |
| DB-DOC1 | Roll the catalogues into operator-facing docs: `docs/reference/database-overview.md` (one-screen "what data lives where") + `docs/help/troubleshooting-databases.md` (operator-readable common issues + fixes). | S | **done** | Shipped. `docs/reference/database-overview.md` + `docs/help/troubleshooting-databases.md` + `docs/admin/index.md` links. |

| IMPORT-Q7-FIX | **Code-fix shipped 2026-05-28** for task #145 / Q7. Two compounding bugs in `download_file_ref`: (1) **forgotten-oid** тАФ the worker fan-out at L4170 called `download_file_ref(src_coll_id, do_id, fref_id, tmp_file, fref.size)` with 5 positional args, dropping `oid=fref.oid`. Per v5.4.0 `FileReferenceRest.getFiles`, the bare `/payload` endpoint returns a JSON array of `ShepardFile` metadata, NOT bytes тАФ so the importer wrote JSON-as-binary and uploaded it to dest. Fix: keyword-pass `oid=fref.oid, corr=corr_id` from the worker; post-stream byte-count guard in `download_file_ref`; unlink partial files; emit `file_truncated` / `file_unverified` diag events (IMPORT-DBG1 surface). Regression test: `examples/mffd-showcase/scripts/test_fileref_truncation.py` (10 cases, all pass; truncation cases verified to FAIL pre-fix). Validation deferred to next v16 import (no live cube JWT + 2026-05-28 full-reset wiped 661923). | M | **done** | Branch `145-fileref-truncation-fix`. Findings: `aidocs/agent-findings/q7-fileref-parser-bug-2026-05-28.md`. |

### IOT1 тАФ 2026-05-23 (map IoT data to proper ontologies)

User directive 2026-05-23: *"map iot to proper ontologies"*. The home-showcase MQTT collector + future industrial IoT integrations (OPC UA on the cube + MFFD shop floor sensors + LUMEN engine DAQ) all produce telemetry that's currently typed at the wire level (channel name) but not semantically (what KIND of sensor, what KIND of measurement). Map onto established IoT vocabularies.

| ID | Slice | Size | Status | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| IOT1 | Add IoT-anchor ontology bundles to the N1c2 preseed manifest: **W3C SOSA/SSN** (Semantic Sensor Network тАФ `sosa:Sensor`, `sosa:Observation`, `sosa:Platform`, `sosa:FeatureOfInterest`, `sosa:ObservableProperty`), **W3C iot-lite**, **QUDT** (units of measurement, already partly used via m4i). | M | done (2026-05-30) | SOSA/SSN + QUDT already satisfied by N1k (2026-05-27); only iot-lite remained. `iot-lite.ttl` stub + manifest entry (sha256: `38ea224bтАж`) added; nineteen bundles total. Cite `aidocs/semantics/95 ┬зSHACL` + `feedback_ontology_first.md`. SHA-256-pinned TTL stubs + canonical URL + fetchOnSeed flag (same N1e/N1c pattern as the m4i bundle). |
| IOT2 | Shape recipe `IoTObservationShape` тАФ every imported timeseries channel maps to one `sosa:Sensor` + a chain of `sosa:Observation`s. Channel name тЖТ `sosa:observes` тЖТ `sosa:ObservableProperty`. Captures the home-showcase MQTT topology + the MFFD AFP telemetry. | M | queued | Pairs with M4I-c (m4i DataObject shape) тАФ the IoT layer is the timeseries-axis projection of the same semantic discipline. |
| IOT3 | `shepard-plugin-iot-bridge` тАФ declarative bridge from MQTT / OPC UA / Modbus / Kafka topics into `sosa:Observation` writes. Plugin-first per CLAUDE.md heuristic. Sidecars declared per PM1f (mosquitto, opcua-asyncio, etc.). | L | queued | Extends home-showcase collector pattern. Operator config: topic тЖТ channel + sensor-IRI mapping. Probably the largest of these. |
| IOT4 | AI-assisted IoT-channel-to-ontology mapper (paired with shepard-plugin-ai). Given a list of channel names, propose `sosa:Sensor` typings + `sosa:ObservableProperty` mappings; human accepts/rejects per `project_ai_human_collab_provenance.md` acceptance ladder. | M | queued | User noted "mai be needs ai ... dont know" тАФ AI-assisted, NOT AI-decided. Mode: ЁЯдЭ collaborative. |

### IMPORT-W тАФ 2026-05-22 (smart warmup with fail-fast diagnostics)

User directives 2026-05-22: *"script should be smart and have a warmaup / probing phase everything works (write access to v5 is enabled for testing)"* + *"unexpected replies lead to abort and actionable diagnostic report"*. Spec source: `backend/src/test/resources/fixtures/v5/openapi-5.4.0.json` (v5.4.0, 282 KB, 90 paths). See `feedback_warmup_fail_fast_diagnostic.md` in agent memory.

| ID | Slice | Size | Status | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| IMPORT-W1 | v15.2 тАФ smart warmup phase that exercises read + write + wire-shape sanity against source + destination. Probes every payload kind the run will touch (file, TS, structured, semantic annotation), writes throwaway probes, reads them back, deletes them, and cross-checks response shape against `fixtures/v5/openapi-5.4.0.json` for the source side. v5 source has write access enabled for testing per user 2026-05-22. | M | **done** | Shipped 2026-05-22 in `examples/mffd-showcase/scripts/_smart_warmup.py` (~860 LOC). New `--smart-warmup` flag (default on) + `--legacy-warmup` opt-out. Probes auth тЖТ reads тЖТ source-write+cleanup тЖТ dest-write+cleanup тЖТ Garage. 22 new tests; total suite at 140. See `aidocs/agent-findings/v15.2-implementation.md`. |
| IMPORT-W2 | Unexpected-reply abort + structured diagnostic report. On any non-2xx or wire-shape drift during warmup or main loop: stop, emit a structured diagnostic block (verb + url + expected schema + got + where to look + what to try next), exit with a distinct integer per failure class (auth=2, source-unreachable=3, garage-down=4, operator-interrupt=5, wire-shape-drift=6, write-permission-denied=7). Used by IMPORT-W1 warmup + by `V1WireFidelityIT` Java side via a parallel implementation. | S | **done** | Shipped 2026-05-22 as `compare_against_openapi()` in `_smart_warmup.py` (not a separate `tools/` file тАФ co-located with the only Python consumer). Resolves `$ref` + `allOf`, walks one level of `properties` + `required`, returns `ShapeDiff(ok, skipped, missing_required_fields, extra_unknown_fields, type_mismatches)`. Skipped gracefully when the spec lacks the endpoint. 3/3 probed endpoints in the v5.4.0 spec have schema coverage. JVM-side parallel implementation for `V1WireFidelityIT` DEFERRED тАФ separate slice. |

### P1 тАФ 2026-05-16 (parallel DB connectivity)

| ID | Slice | Status | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|
| P1 | Parallel startup DB warm + parallel recovery | done | New `DbConnectivityWarmer` (`@ApplicationScoped`, `@Observes StartupEvent`) fires one `Thread.ofVirtual()` per required `DbPinger` in parallel тАФ total startup wait is now `max(latencies)` not `sum(latencies)`. Bounded by `shepard.migrations.connection-wait-timeout` (reused from `MigrationsRunner`; no new config key). `DbRecoveryScheduler.attemptRecovery()` now collects stale pingers then probes each in its own virtual thread (`CompletableFuture.allOf` blocks the tick). Both use `RequestContextController.activate/deactivate` per thread so JPA `EntityManager` injections in `TimescalePinger` / `PostGisPinger` work correctly off the caller thread. Per-DB `DbHealthState` independently tracks each outcome. 7 new unit tests in `DbConnectivityWarmerTest` (including timing proof: 3 ├Ч 300 ms pingers finish in < 950 ms wall-clock); 2 new tests added to `DbRecoverySchedulerTest`. |

### VIS тАФ 2026-05-22 (visualization plugin family)

Survey: `aidocs/agent-findings/vis-plugin-survey.md`. Broadens the Trace3D seed
(`aidocs/agent-findings/trace3d-spike.md`, task #142) into a coherent plugin
family covering 3D paths/traces, vector fields/CFD, voxel/volumetric (REM/EM/╬╝CT),
and surface meshes. **Extended 2026-05-22** with categories 5 (CAD data) and
6 (FEM result files) per
`aidocs/agent-findings/vis-plugin-survey-addendum-cad-fem.md` тАФ
7 categories total, 5 plugins + 2 sidecars. All rows queued; pick-up order:
VIS-S1 тЖТ VIS-T1 тЖТ VIS-V1 тЖТ VIS-X1 тЖТ **VIS-C1 тЖТ VIS-F1** тЖТ VIS-S2 тЖТ VIS-S3
(stretch).

**Critical context for VIS-T1:** `@tresjs/nuxt` repo was archived Feb 1, 2026.
`@tresjs/core` itself (v5.8.1, May 2026) is still actively maintained. Use core
directly via an in-plugin `useTres()` composable; do NOT depend on the archived
Nuxt module. This is a correction to `aidocs/agent-findings/trace3d-spike.md`
which assumed `@tresjs/nuxt` was available тАФ see survey ┬з1.2 for the rationale.

| ID | Slice | Size | Status | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| VIS-S1 | Shared cross-cutting platform piece: `POST /v2/shapes/render` `ViewRecipeRenderer` SPI dispatcher (in-tree, plugin authors register a renderer keyed by SHACL shape IRI from the template body's `viewRecipeShape` field). Garage signed-URL minter helper (`SignedUrlIssuer`) + presigned-URL access-control filter SPLIT OUT to a follow-up (VIS-S1b) тАФ the dispatcher alone unblocks VIS-T1 sprint-2, the URL minter is wanted by VIS-V1 / VIS-X1 but not Trace3D. | M | **shipped 2026-05-28 (VIS-S1a тАФ SPI dispatcher only; VIS-S1b URL minter still queued)** | In-tree, not a plugin. **Predecessor for all VIS-* plugins.** SPI shape `de.dlr.shepard.spi.view.{ViewRecipeRenderer, ViewRecipeRendererRegistry, RenderRequest, RenderResponse, RenderException}` тАФ ServiceLoader-loaded POJO impls mirroring the `PayloadKind` P-series pattern; fail-fast at startup on duplicate shape IRI; renderer-thrown `RenderException` тЖТ HTTP 422 (RFC 7807); unexpected `RuntimeException` тЖТ HTTP 500; no renderer registered тЖТ in-tree TPL2b `DECLARED`-status fallback (wire shape preserved for clients whose plugin isn't installed). 32 unit tests (14 registry + 18 dispatcher). | RDK-PARSE-1 | **`RdkTextScrapeParser` tier-1 тАФ readable strings out of `MFZ.rdk`**. New module `plugins/fileformat-robotics/` (declared as a `FileParserPlugin` per `aidocs/integrations/110-file-format-parser-plugin.md ┬з3`). Decompresses the `.rdk` zlib payload (4-byte custom magic header skipped), walks `[uint32 LE byte-length][UTF-16LE bytes]` records, and classifies each via predicate-specific regex; emits eight SemanticAnnotations on the parent FileReference under `urn:shepard:rdk:*`: `appVersion`, `platform`, `programSource`, `cadRef[]`, `stepRef[]`, `apiEndpoint`, `robotController`, `companionSpatialAnalyzer` (the last when a `<base>.xit`/`.xit64` sibling exists in the same FileContainer). | S | **done 2026-05-28** | MAJOR | user request 2026-05-28 | `plugins/fileformat-robotics/` standalone Maven module + three-audience docs trio. 17 JUnit tests green, including `RdkTextScrapeParserMFZFixtureTest` against the real 12.1 MB `examples/mffd-showcase/raw-data/mffd-data/cell/MFZ.rdk` тАФ reproduces aidocs/110 ┬з4.3 expected output verbatim. Aggregator wire-up filed as **RDK-WIRE-AGGREGATOR-1** (same `OTVIS-WIRE-AGGREGATOR-1`-class Jandex blocker). Namespace decision documented in `RdkAnnotations` javadoc: `urn:shepard:rdk:*` supersedes the `chameo:*` / `m4i:*` sketch in aidocs/110 ┬з4.3 тАФ the doc is `stage: concept` and updated in this PR. Note: walker is single-pass structured-string extraction over zlib-decompressed UTF-16LE length-prefix records тАФ literal printable-ASCII run extraction discarded after empirical eval (754K raw runs vs. 72 structured records on `MFZ.rdk`); chose option (a) (regex-per-predicate) over option (b) (multi-pass classifier) for tier-1. |

| URDF-WEBVIEW-1 | **in progress (this PR тАФ phase 1: in-tree renderer adapter, plugin extraction deferred).** **`shepard-plugin-vis-urdf` тАФ URDF browser viewer + animator + Foxglove iframe fallback.** **URDF is Shepard's lingua franca for robot kinematics** тАФ ROS RViz, Isaac, MuJoCo, Foxglove, Gazebo all consume it. Plugin ships: (a) `UrdfViewShape` SHACL allow-list extension; (b) `UrdfResolver` returns signed Garage URL for `.urdf` + mesh assets; (c) `UrdfView.vue` using `urdf-loader` (gkjohnson, MIT, npm `urdf-loader`) тАФ Three.js-based, mounts into the shared `<TresCanvas>` from `vis-trace3d`; supports STL/Collada/glTF meshes; (d) **`UrdfAnimator.vue` тАФ trajectory playback**: takes a `:DigitalTwinScene` URDF + a `TimeseriesReference` carrying joint-angle channels (one channel per movable joint, `urn:shepard:urdf:joint` annotation maps channel тЖТ joint name; preselection rule applies), drives `urdf-loader`'s per-joint setters against a time cursor. Conversion: `RdkToUrdfExporter` sidecar wraps RoboDK Python API тЖТ URDF via `robolink.Item.UpdateRobotURDF()` (cell-level info lost; document the lossy boundary in `plugins/vis-urdf/docs/reference.md`). ### TOOLS-NAV-* / SCENEGRAPH-NAV-* тАФ top-nav reachability reconciliation (2026-05-30)

Reconciler walked the deployed UI on 2026-05-30 and found exactly one strict
violation of the CLAUDE.md "every shipped feature reachable from the top-nav
before beta" rule: **SCENEGRAPH-REST-1-UI** was 4 clicks from any page
(avatar тЖТ /me тЖТ Semantic tile тЖТ Scene graphs). The cheapest structural fix
is a top-level `Tools` menu that aggregates six research-tooling routes тАФ
which simultaneously lifts five other surfaces from 4-click to 1-click depth.

| ID | Item | Size | Status | Severity | Notes |

### M4I тАФ 2026-05-23 (metadata4ing deepening)

User directive 2026-05-23: *"how to deepen metadata4ing (m4i) integration"*.
Design lands at `aidocs/semantics/94-metadata4ing-integration-design.md`.
**Critical finding** surfaced during research: the current
`ProvJsonLdRenderer` emits **non-canonical predicates**
(`m4i:hasMethod` / `m4i:hasInput` / `m4i:hasOutput`) that do
not exist in canonical m4i 1.4.0 тАФ see M4I-b. Latest m4i
version is **1.4.0 (2025-12-08)**; the shipped bundle pins it
already, no version bump needed.

| ID | Slice | Size | Status | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| M4I-a | Promote `metadata4ing.ttl` stub тЖТ fetch canonical TTL on first seed via existing `canonicalUrl` + `fetchOnSeed` flag (NASA Thesaurus N1e pattern). Stub stays in JAR as offline fallback. Acceptance: тЙе 100 m4i `:Resource` rows in n10s after fresh start. | S (1 d) | **тЬУ shipped (2026-05-26)** | `aidocs/semantics/94 ┬з4.1`. `fetchUrl: "https://w3id.org/nfdi4ing/metadata4ing/1.4.0/"` + `fetchFormat: "Turtle"` added to `ontologies-manifest.json` metadata4ing entry. w3id.org permanent URL 303-redirects to `nfdi4ing.pages.rwth-aachen.de` (~202 KB canonical TTL; тЙе 150 terms). Stub unchanged (SHA-256 pin intact) as offline fallback. New test `realManifest_metadata4ing_hasFetchUrl_andTurtleFormat` added to `OntologySeedServiceTest`. |
| M4I-b | **CRITICAL bug-shaped fix.** Rewrite m4i branch of `ProvJsonLdRenderer.render(...)` to emit canonical predicates: `m4i:hasMethod` тЖТ **`m4i:realizesMethod`**; `m4i:hasInput` тЖТ **`obo:RO_0002233`** (OBO Relations Ontology, already preseeded via ONT1a); `m4i:hasOutput` тЖТ **`obo:RO_0002234`**. Extend `@context` with `"obo"` prefix when profile=m4i. Add `m4i:investigates` from activity to investigated entity on read actions. | S | **done (2026-05-26)** | `aidocs/semantics/94 ┬з4.2`. Verified against canonical OWL at `https://nfdi4ing.pages.rwth-aachen.de/metadata4ing/metadata4ing/` on 2026-05-23. Both code paths fixed (`renderActivityAsM4iNode` + `render(activities, m4i)`). `obo:` prefix added to `@context` when profile=m4i. 8 new canonical-predicate tests added; 5 existing tests updated to assert new predicates. SHACL self-test deferred to M4I-c. AWARE in `aidocs/34` flagged BREAKING for any m4i consumer that depended on the old non-canonical names (low real-world risk; no known consumer; discipline is the point). |
| M4I-c | `m4i:DataObjectShape` SHACL contract + `M4iDataObjectRenderer` + content-neg `Accept: application/ld+json; profile=metadata4ing` on `GET /v2/data-objects/{appId}` (mirrors PROV1h on `/v2/provenance/*`). Mandatory triples: `m4i:InvestigatedObject` type, `dcterms:identifier`, `dcterms:title`, `schema:dateCreated`. ### DOC-STAGE тАФ 2026-05-23 (doc-lifecycle taxonomy + tagging)

Cross-cutting documentation hygiene. The lifecycle taxonomy lives at
`aidocs/00-doc-stages.md`; the grouped index at
`aidocs/01-doc-stage-index.md` (auto-generated). CLAUDE.md carries the
"Always: tag every aidocs doc with a lifecycle stage" rule.

| DOC-STAGE1 | Taxonomy doc (`aidocs/00-doc-stages.md`) + generator (`scripts/regenerate-doc-stage-index.py`) + tagger (`scripts/tag-aidocs-stages.py`) + retro-tag pass over ~210 `aidocs/**/*.md` files + CLAUDE.md rule + this backlog section + memory rule. Zero UNTAGGED leftovers; histogram printed at commit time. | M | done (this PR) | All `aidocs/**/*.md` carry YAML `stage:` front-matter. Retro-tags use existing `**Status.** тАж` lines + path heuristics; owner can refine any best-guess `fragment` defaults in follow-on. |
| DOC-STAGE2 | Pre-commit hook + CI step that runs `python3 scripts/regenerate-doc-stage-index.py --check` and fails on drift; same hook fails when a new `aidocs/**/*.md` lands without a `stage:` field. ### SWEEP тАФ 2026-05-23 (deferred items surfaced from repo grep)

Sweep result from a cross-cutting `grep -E 'TODO|FIXME|deferred|follow-up|out of scope|queued'` pass across `backend/`, `frontend/`, `plugins/`, `examples/`, `docs/`, `aidocs/agent-findings/`, `aidocs/{platform,integrations,ops,semantics,strategy,ux,workflows,reference}/*.md`, `.github/workflows/`, `Makefile`, and `backend/pom.xml`. 320 existing row IDs were extracted from this file and used as a dedup filter тАФ every row below is **not** already on the backlog. Full inventory + source citations: `aidocs/agent-findings/repo-task-sweep-2026-05-23.md`.

Rationale: per `feedback_backlog_for_later.md` ("things-for-later go on a maintained backlog, not in prose docs") and `feedback_backlog_consult_context.md` (every row cites its source). The risk being closed is the slow rot where a `TODO(IMP1)` in `ImportV2Rest.java` or a "this is a follow-up" footnote in a design doc never becomes a row, and the deferral is forgotten.

Skew: 5 CRITICAL, 49 MAJOR, 17 MINOR, 14 NICE-to-have. Highest-priority item to ship: **`MFG5`** тАФ enforce DataObject `status` as a closed enum at the persistence boundary. Quoting `aidocs/agent-findings/manufacturing-quality.md ┬з11.2`: *"the single largest gap between Shepard's current design and aerospace quality record requirements"* тАФ one backend PR, no migration on shipped data beyond a value-set check.

| MFFD-IMPORT-PERF1 | **Real worker fan-out for `run_source_mode_workers`.** Extract the per-DO loop body (`mffd-import-v15.py` L2495..2598) into a callable `_process_one_source_do(...)` and submit one future per source DO. Bound at 4 concurrent cube3 GETs + 4 dest POSTs per `aidocs/93 ┬з5`. Today the wrapper is a fake fan-out тАФ it spawns the pool, runs `lambda: True` probes, then calls `run_source_mode` SEQUENTIALLY (`mffd-import-v15.py` L2983..2999). `--workers N` does nothing for throughput. | M | **done (v15.8)** | MAJOR | `aidocs/agent-findings/mffd-import-slowness-diagnose-2026-05-23.md ┬з5 Hypothesis #1` | Shipped 2026-05-23 in v15.8 (manifest published to FileContainer 473932). Per-DO body extracted into `_process_one_source_do(src_do, do_bar)` closure inside `run_source_mode`. Driver submits one future per source DO via `ThreadPoolExecutor(max_workers=workers)` with `as_completed`-based drain + refill keeping the pool saturated. `tqdm.update(1)` happens only in the driver thread. `ImportState` gains `_lock: RLock` covering all read+write ops. `existing_names` hoisted to per-step snapshot (no N parallel calls for the same dest list). `run_source_mode_workers` simplified to a thin forwarder; tests in `tests/test_worker_pool.py` updated. |

| STAGE1 | **Per-user data dump / staging area** тАФ every authenticated user gets a personal staging space (a private, draft-shaped Collection or a sibling concept) where they can drop files, archives, raw exports, or scratch data without committing to a curated Collection yet. AI analysis plugins (FVF on micrographs, anomaly detection on TS, m4i auto-extraction on PDFs, channel-unit inference) fire against staged data automatically when an AI capability is registered. The user reviews results, then **promotes** items into shared Collections тАФ staged items either move (one-shot) or remain as the read-only origin with provenance edges. The microsections-showcase is the canonical use case: researcher drops `Schliffbilder.7z`, FVF analysis runs per TIF, user accepts results into a sample-series Collection. Pairs with task #26 (ingest data from git) + AI1t (PDF auto-annotation) + AI1v (channel-unit inference) + J2 (JupyterHub plugin); all of those become "things that run inside the staging area" rather than separate top-level integrations. Operator-visible bits: `:UserStagingArea` Neo4j entity (one per `:User`); `GET /v2/me/staging` returns the area; `POST /v2/me/staging/files` uploads; `POST /v2/me/staging/promote` moves items into a Collection with PROV-O `wasDerivedFrom`. ### GH-INFRA тАФ 2026-05-23 (GitHub features integration)

Full survey: `aidocs/strategy/83-github-features-leverage.md`. The
guiding rule (also pinned in `feedback_github_features.md`): default is
"don't add a new GitHub feature unless solo-dev cost is near zero AND
external-contributor / security-posture value is high"; `aidocs/16`
stays SSOT тАФ Issues are NOT a backlog mirror.

Decision matrix per feature lives in the survey doc above.

| ID | Slice | Size | Status | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| GH-INFRA1 | Templates + CODEOWNERS + Dependabot + canonical labels + release-notes scaffolding + PR template mirroring CLAUDE.md "Always:" rules + CONTRIBUTING.md "Filing issues" / "PR discipline" sections + the survey doc + this row. Pure config-as-code; no API calls; no live changes to the GitHub repo until merged + the operator actions below are taken. | M | done | Shipped 2026-05-23 on the worktree branch in one commit. Files: `.github/release.yml`, `.github/workflows/release-notes.yml`, `.github/workflows/sync-labels.yml`, `.github/ISSUE_TEMPLATE/{config,bug-report,feature-request,docs-improvement,security-finding}.yml`, `.github/pull_request_template.md`, `.github/CODEOWNERS`, `.github/dependabot.yml`, `.github/labels.yml`, `docs/ops/cut-a-release.md`, `docs/ops/github-projects-board-setup.md`, `aidocs/strategy/83-github-features-leverage.md`, CONTRIBUTING.md additions. |
| GH-INFRA2 | Manually create the Projects v2 board following `docs/ops/github-projects-board-setup.md`. Operator-only; no code. Sets up columns (Backlog / In Progress / In Review / Blocked / Done), custom fields (Severity / Area / Effort / Stage / Aidocs ID), auto-add-to-project rule, and 5 saved views. | S | queued | Manual one-time setup. Picking up after GH-INFRA1 merges to main. |
| GH-INFRA3 | Cut `v6.0.0-rc.1` once the MFFD real-data import lands and aidocs/34 has the corresponding row. First release that uses `.github/workflows/release-notes.yml`. | S | queued | Gated on MFFD import landing. Follows `docs/ops/cut-a-release.md`. |
| GH-INFRA4 | aidocs/16 тЖФ GitHub Issues sync tooling. **Gated on external-contribution velocity** тАФ don't build until 5+ external contributors are filing issues per month. The duplicate-bookkeeping cost only pays back when there's real bilateral flow. | M | blocked | Blocking condition: external-contributor velocity threshold not yet met. Re-evaluate quarterly. |
| GH-INFRA5 | GitHub Environments for `nuclide.systems` and `DLR boxes` with required-reviewer deploy gates. Replaces the implicit "I just ran `make redeploy` in tmux" deploy step with a Github-tracked, audit-trailed deploy. | M | queued | Lower priority than GH-INFRA2/3. Pairs with the deploy-after-feature rule from `feedback_deploy_after_visible_features.md`. |

### GH-PM тАФ 2026-05-23 (GitHub project-management policies)

Full policy: `aidocs/strategy/85-github-project-management-policies.md`.
The shape: `aidocs/16` is the SSOT backlog; GitHub Issues are the narrow
4-gate subset (external-pickup / security / repro-bug / agent in-flight);
sync direction is one-way (aidocs/16 тЖТ Issue); the unified state machine
maps doc front-matter тЖФ aidocs/16 Status тЖФ GH `status:*` / `stage:*`
labels тЖФ Projects v2 columns byte-for-byte (see `aidocs/00-doc-stages.md`).
Releases cut on coherent-feature-set boundary with the ┬з5 pre-flight
checklist. The end-state test is `scripts/trace-feature.sh <ID>` тАФ nine
surfaces resolved per feature.

| ID | Slice | Size | Status | Notes |

### OBS тАФ 2026-05-23 (recursive self-observability)

The principle is documented in `feedback_shepard_measures_itself.md`:
Shepard's own ingest-rate metrics live INSIDE Shepard's TimeseriesContainer
substrate, not in a parallel observability stack. The MFFD-Dropbox import
session was the first concrete instance тАФ the chart updates by the same
TS chart UI a researcher already uses.

| ID | Slice | Size | Status | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| OBS-MFFD1 | `scripts/mffd-import-stats-collector.py` polls `/v2/collections/{appId}/data-objects` every 5 min, walks per-DO refs for file/TS/SD counters, runs `docker exec shepard-garage /garage bucket info shepard-files` for the object-store size, and POSTs 11 channels per tick to `TimeseriesContainer` 590324 linked to `DataObject` 590344 in the MFFD-Dropbox collection. Bootstrap is idempotent; the `TimeseriesReference` is lazily created after the first tick materialises channels (the v5 `Bug A` minItems:1 constraint, learned from v15.2). Ships a systemd timer pair (`infrastructure/systemd/mffd-import-stats-collector.{service,timer}`) so operators can replace the ad-hoc background process. Plottable via the existing TS chart UI тАФ no new frontend code. | S | done | Shipped 2026-05-23 (this commit). Files: `scripts/mffd-import-stats-collector.py`, `infrastructure/systemd/mffd-import-stats-collector.{service,timer}`, `docs/help/observing-an-import.md`, this row, `aidocs/data/00-model-inventory.md ┬з8` row, `feedback_shepard_measures_itself.md`. Verified: first tick at 23:07:24Z wrote 11/11 channels (`DO=8, files=0, garage=160300 B`); second tick at 23:08:19Z saw `TSrefs=1, channels=11` confirming the lazy reference creation. |
| OBS-MFFD2 | Generalise the collector to ANY import job: lift the MFFD-specific name-pattern table into a per-collection config + accept any collection-appId. Land as `scripts/import-stats-collector.py` (drop the `mffd-` prefix) plus an admin UI for picking which collections to instrument. | M | queued | Promotes the recursive-observability pattern to a first-class tool. Pairs with the `OBS-MFFD3` admin dashboard. |
| OBS-MFFD3 | Dashboard view summarising all in-flight imports: list every `ImportStats-*` DataObject across all collections + a `dos_total` sparkline + a delta-since-last-tick. Plugs into the existing Collections list or lands as `/v2/admin/imports`. | M | queued | "What's actually being ingested right now?" admin view. Dep on `OBS-MFFD2`. Pairs with the `GH-INFRA3` release gate. |

### DOCS-3A тАФ 2026-05-23 (three-audience docs: admin + user + plugin)

The rule is documented in `feedback_three_audience_docs.md`: three sharply
distinct audiences (admin, user, plugin) with the same-PR maintenance shape,
served from BOTH the Pages site AND Shepard's in-app `/help` route. The user
+ plugin audiences already have policies in CLAUDE.md; the admin audience
needs explicit consolidation.

| AGENT-WT1 | Standing tier-1 agent-dispatch protocol: when 2+ agents may touch overlapping aidocs paths (esp. parallel persona-audits or design-doc edits), use `EnterWorktree` for true isolation. Today's batch (LOGSTORE/PROMPT/ADMIN-STALE-CH/ONT-AI-MAP persona audits, dispatched in parallel) landed 3 deliverables under one commit because agents staged concurrently in the main worktree. Content correct, commit-message scope misleading. **Action:** update agent prompt templates to require `EnterWorktree` for tier-1 parallel dispatches; document in `feedback_autonomous_mode_protocol.md`. **Structural fix (2026-05-27):** agents launched with `isolation: worktree` get separate working trees тАФ but if the agent then writes to absolute `/opt/shepard/...` paths rather than paths relative to its worktree root, the writes bypass worktree isolation and land directly in the main tree, defeating the purpose. Agent prompt templates must warn: use relative paths within the worktree, OR stage + commit before reporting. | PROV-USER-ENRICH | **Wire `X-Source-User-*` headers тЖТ `:MirroredUser` in `ProvenanceCaptureFilter`.** SHIPPED 2026-05-26 (#234). When the MFFD v15+ importer forwards `X-Source-User-{Username,DisplayName,Email,Instance}` headers, `ProvenanceCaptureFilter` now (a) upserts a `:MirroredUser` node via `MirroredUserDAO.createOrUpdateBySourceKey`, (b) caches the result for 5 min in new `@ApplicationScoped` `MirroredUserEnrichmentCache` to avoid per-request DB round-trips, (c) stamps the resolved appId as `mirroredUserAppId` on the `:Activity` node via new 11-param `ProvenanceService.record(...)` overload, (d) backfills blank `firstName`/`lastName`/`email` on the local `:User` node from the display-name header. All prov enrichment is best-effort (WARN-logged, never fails the request). New: `auth/users/services/MirroredUserEnrichmentCache.java`; extended: `Activity.mirroredUserAppId` property, `ProvenanceService` 11-param overload, `ProvenanceCaptureFilter`. Tests: `provenance/filters/MirroredUserLookupTest.java` (11 cases). | M | **done (2026-05-26, #234)** | Source: 2026-05-23. Pairs with PROV-USER-MIRROR-ENDPOINT (#229), MFFD-IMPORT-USER-CAPTURE (header-forward v15.9). |

| WIZARD-JSON-INTERPRETABLE | **Process wizards emit a JSON manifest of every action taken.** User-flagged 2026-05-23 *"make process wizards jason interpretable - whatever that means"*. Today's UI wizards (Create-from-template, ImportManifest helper, AnomalyDetection setup, future spatial-region annotator) capture user intent in form-state, translate it into REST writes (POST Collection / POST DataObject / POST Annotation / link refs / set attrs), and produce no durable per-action record other than the resulting Shepard entities + the PROV1a `:Activity` audit trail. The gap: an external agent (Claude / MCP / another Shepard instance / a downstream automation) can't re-read what the wizard *intended* тАФ only what it *produced*. **Spec:** every wizard run emits a `wizard-run.json` artifact attached to the resulting top-level entity as a FileReference (`name="wizard-manifest.json"`, attribute `kind:wizard-manifest`). Manifest shape: `{wizard_id, wizard_version, user, started_at, finished_at, form_inputs: {...verbatim form state...}, computed_decisions: [{predicate, value, source: "user|default|inferred"}], created_entities: [{type, appId, summary}], skipped: [{type, reason}], next_actions_suggested: [...]}`. Consumers: (a) MCP tools can read the manifest to answer "how was this Collection set up?" without reverse-engineering from the graph; (b) replay automation can re-run the same wizard with the same form state on another instance for templating; (c) provenance-export (RO-Crate / BagIt) carries the manifest as a first-class artifact; (d) AI assistants get a clean view of "the user clicked through this flow" without parsing the activity log. **Pairs with:** task #20 (Create-from-template тАФ entry point already shipped), task #42 (template UX), task #51 (containerless basic mode), Importer's AgentContextIO / ImportManifestIO patterns from v15 (the wizard manifest is the UI-side dual of the importer-side manifest). | M | queued | Design decision needed: does the wizard manifest live as a FileReference on the entity (durable, queryable) or as a separate `:WizardRun` Neo4j node linked to the entity (graph-traversable)? Recommend file-attached: easier to round-trip, cheaper to read. Effort sized for one canonical wizard (Create-from-template) as proof-of-concept; subsequent wizards follow the same shape. |

Look for: hot-path query patterns that need indexes (Neo4j label-property indexes, Mongo compound indexes, Timescale chunk pruning); Cypher patterns that don't scale (cartesian joins, expanding-bag traversals); SD container collection proliferation in Mongo (one Mongo collection per SD container тАФ at MFFD volume that's potentially 1000+ collections); Garage object naming + bucket layout under real load; PGтЖФNeo4j duplication seams (where the same fact lives in both); SHACL-shape vs runtime-query mismatch (cf. `feedback_shacl_single_source_of_truth.md`); TS chunk + retention policy fit for MFFD cadence; permission lookup cost at depth. Output: `aidocs/agent-findings/db-audit-post-mffd-real-data.md` + per-substrate sub-findings. Pairs with `feedback_db_review_all_stores.md`. | L | queued | Dependency: v15.13 ingest complete + verdict PASS/PARTIAL accepted. Use the live data тАФ no fixtures, no synthetic seeds. Cross-cutting findings (touch all six substrates) are the highest-value output. |
| MFFD-IMPORT-BUG-E | **v15.12 тАФ fix SD payload BSON-array reject (root cause of 100% StepMetaProcessExecution failure rate).** SHIPPED 2026-05-23 in v15.12. Backend `StructuredDataService.java:53` calls `Document.parse(payload.getPayload())` which MongoDB's BSON model rejects with `readStartDocument...not when CurrentBSONType is ARRAY` when the inner JSON has an array at root. The v15.9-v15.11 importer was hitting this on every `StepMetaProcessExecution` SD upload because that payload IS a list. **Fix:** `upload_structured_payload()` wraps non-dict payloads in `{"items": [...], "_wrapped": "v15.12-bug-e"}` before `_json.dumps()`. Readers consuming MFFD SD payloads must unwrap the single `items` key when `_wrapped` marker present. Diagnosed via destination backend log grep (`f1a0a74d-7436-41a7-8dc6-9d13dc2d883e` reference) тЖТ exact exception type тЖТ traced to `StructuredDataService.java:53` `Document.parse()` call. **Sibling:** MFFD-IMPORT-COMPLETENESS-CHECK (post-migration verifier so we can confirm the wrap actually landed everything). **Operator action needed:** redrive the SD references already created with empty payloads (ID range 632242..current тЖТ all bridgewelding SDs that hit 500 since import started). Either DELETE + recreate or POST again to same /payload (since prior call never landed). Per-DO recovery scriptable from the source 5-tuple (collection + DO + container name тЖТ original SD payload). | S | done (v15.12, 2026-05-23) | Wrap fix + version canary + py_compile gate тЬУ. Cube hot-patch + main commit + manifest publish pending. Backend-side alternative (detect array-root + wrap before Document.parse) tracked as MFFD-SD-BACKEND-WRAP-FALLBACK. |

Per-DO row: existence-in-dest + per-kind ref counts (files / TS / SD / fileBundle / video / image / anomaly / semantic / children) + blocking kinds. | MFFD-IMPORT-DIAG | **v15.11 тАФ structured diagnostic instrumentation for self-diagnosable failures.** SHIPPED 2026-05-23 in v15.11. Adds `DiagSink` class emitting one JSON line per event to stderr (atomic via single `os.write(2, ...)` under module-level lock, тЙд4096 bytes = Linux PIPE_BUF), tee'd into the existing log file and mirrored into the existing `Telemetry` channel (best-effort, never breaks emit). New `--diag-mode={quiet,normal,verbose,http-trace}` flag (default `normal`; env `MFFD_DIAG_MODE`). 18 event kinds (startup, warmup_step, source_user_resolved, iter_start/end, do_start/skip/done/error, http_request/response, worker_pool, jwt_status, manifest_poll, state_save, telemetry_flush, summary, shutdown). Auto-classified diagnostic hints from a pure-function `classify_error(status, body)` тЖТ 9 hint codes (jwt-expired-or-rotated, permission-denied, not-found, conflict, rate-limited, bean-validation, client-error, server-side, timeout-or-network) with human-readable actions. Per-DO correlation id (`<step>:<src_do_id>`) ties every related event together. Non-2xx http responses ALWAYS emit regardless of mode тАФ failure signal must not be filterable. Credential masking (`mask_credential` тЖТ `sha256:<first-12-hex>`) with explicit plaintext-leak guard test. Shutdown event carries the final 60s rolling-window summary. 36 new pytest cases in `tests/test_diag.py` (wire shape, 8-thread atomic-write concurrency, mode gating, all 9 error classes, JWT decode well-formed + malformed, credential mask + leak guard, summary aggregation, payload truncation, PIPE_BUF overflow marker, telemetry-mirror best-effort, version constant). Pattern card: `aidocs/integrations/95 ┬зPattern 19`. Closes the "2 AM debugging requires code spelunking" failure mode by making logs alone sufficient to diagnose any of: wire-shape errors, 401/403/404/409/429, rate limits, worker deadlock, JWT expiry, lock contention, state-file inconsistency, source-side missing content, Quarkus bean-validation violations. | M | done (v15.11, 2026-05-23) | DiagSink тЬУ + 18 event kinds тЬУ + classifier тЬУ + masking тЬУ + atomic-write concurrency test тЬУ.
