| UX-REVERT-MUTATIONS | **First-class "undo" for data mutations тАФ user-facing revert of changes / mutation passes.** Companion to the Goldilocks-shaping principle (`project_mffd_dest_backfill_pass.md`, `project_dataset_forging.md`): if mutations are iterative ("juuuuuuuust right"), then UNDO must be first-class. Every mutation that lands via the v2 API is recorded as a typed `:Activity` (PROV-O) with input/output state references; the UI exposes a "history" panel per DataObject / Collection / Container showing N most recent mutations with one-click "revert this change" (returns to the pre-mutation state) and bulk "revert N passes" (back to S(N-k)). Plays nice with the snapshot chain S0тЖТS1тЖТ...тЖТSn that the back-fill pattern produces. Pairs with PV1a payload version history (already shipped тАФ extends from "file payload versions" to "attribute + reference + structure mutations"). Probably needs a v2 endpoint `POST /v2/{resource}/{appId}/revert?to=activityAppId` + `GET /v2/{resource}/{appId}/mutations` (list). | L | queued | Source: 2026-05-23 user flag ("for backlog, easy way to revert changes / mutations for users"). Companion to MFFD-IMPORTER-DATASET-CAPTURE + the dest backfill pattern. Critical for trusting AI-driven mutation passes тАФ user can experiment + back out safely. EN 9100 audit angle: the revert trail IS the audit trail. |

**ЁЯЫИ Clarification 2026-05-23 (user flag "none are for direct reuse - informational only"):** The UNAS code-drop projects are **informational only** тАФ patterns + design references + field-confirmation that ZLP needs the integration shape. Do NOT propose direct code-reuse / dependency adoption from these zips. They inform the *shape* of what to build, not the *substrate* to build on. Treat the listed projects as "see how others solved this" rather than "import this library." Reuse-before-reimplement still applies тАФ but the reuse decision goes through fresh upstream OSS evaluation, not the UNAS snapshot.

| PERM-SYSTEM-REVIEW | **Permission system review тАФ consistency, inheritance, ACL vs RBAC vs alternatives.** Today's Shepard permissions are a per-entity ACL bolted on: each entity (Collection, FileContainer, DataObject, ...) carries `{owner, permissionType: Private\|Public, reader[], writer[], readerGroupIds[], writerGroupIds[], manager[]}`. **Live failure modes observed 2026-05-23** (RoboDK dropbox setup): (a) FileContainer created via REST defaults to `Private` despite being inside a `Public` Collection тАФ no inheritance; (b) DataObject has no per-entity permissions endpoint (`GET /collections/{id}/dataObjects/{did}/permissions` 404) so write authorization is unclear / inconsistent with FileContainer pattern; (c) `createFileReference` fails opaquely when either DO or FC denies write тАФ error toast literally reads "Error while createFileReference:" with empty message after colon (the UX-FRIENDLY-ERRORS symptom); (d) ~~per task #148, DataObject creation doesn't seed a Permissions record at all, causing 403 cascades~~ **CORRECTED 2026-05-24** (see `aidocs/agent-findings/bug-148-do-perms-seeded-2026-05-24.md`): DataObjects are **designed** to not seed own Permissions; access inherits from parent Collection via `PermissionsService.isAccessAllowedForDataObjectAppId` (lines 291-329 of `PermissionsService.java`). Live verified all 17,149 DOs lack `:Permissions` and all writes succeed via the parent-Collection walk (HTTP 200/201, zero 403s). The RoboDK 403 cascades trace to sub-bullet (a) тАФ FileContainer not inheriting parent Collection's `Public` setting тАФ not anything DO-related. **BUG-148 / task #148 тЖТ close as works-as-designed.** **Design question to resolve**: (1) **Pure ACL** (current shape, fix inheritance + add DO endpoint) тАФ minimal change, retains owner-centric model, but every entity carries its own list; doesn't scale to project-level orgs. (2) **RBAC** (roles: viewer, contributor, curator, admin; scoped to Collection) тАФ projects assign roles, members inherit. Clean for institutional use; loses fine-grained per-DO override. (3) **RBAC + ABAC overrides (PBAC, policy-based)** тАФ RBAC as default, per-entity policy lets `embargo_until: 2027-01-01` or `accessRights: restricted access` short-circuit role grants. Best fit for FAIR + EN 9100 needs (embargo, license-gated access, NCR-confidentiality), but complex. (4) **Capability-based / Macaroons** тАФ bearer tokens carry scoped capabilities (read coll-X-until-2027 + write fc-626776). Composable, delegatable, but breaks the "user-in-list" UI assumption. **Recommendation to investigate** (audit before implementation): RBAC core + ABAC overlay (option 3). Default role grants from Collection; per-entity policies layer on license / embargo / access-rights from LIC1. Pairs with TPL10 DQR (DataQualityRequirement) which can carry policy. The 5 acceptance lenses: (A) auditor-ready audit trail per access decision (PROV1a captures the decision; the role + policy at decision time); (B) onboarding a new contributor takes тЙд 2 clicks (assign role, done); (C) embargo enforcement is a property not a one-off ACL entry; (D) inheritance: child inherits parent unless explicitly overridden; (E) all four UI badges (ЁЯМР Public / ЁЯСБ Restricted / ЁЯФТ Closed / тП▒ Embargoed) compute deterministically from role+policy without per-entity ACL lookup. Audit deliverable: `aidocs/platform/<n>-permission-system-review.md` with reuse survey (existing FAIR-aware ACL libraries: Keycloak Authorization, OPA, Cedar (AWS, Apache-2.0) тАФ Cedar particularly notable as it's purpose-built for ABAC-on-RBAC), prior art (CKAN dataset access, Coscine + RWTH; Dataverse role assignments; openBIS spaces+projects), and decision matrix. | L | queued | Source: 2026-05-23 user flag with screenshot evidence ("permission system review for more consistency - inheritance, discuss ACL or RBAC or alternatives") + live failure on RoboDK FC. Pairs with #148 (Permissions bug) + UX-FRIENDLY-ERRORS (the opaque error) + LIC1 (license field needs policy enforcement) + TPL10 (DQR). GH #1557. |

| BUG-UI-FILEREF-EMPTY-OIDS | тЬУ shipped (eba9be1a9) тАФ **UI bug: createFileReference POSTs with empty `fileOids` array.** Fixed in `fix(frontend): file upload тАФ await createFileReference + surface empty-oids honestly`. Guards in both `useCreateFileReference.ts:20-30` and `DataObjectFileUploadDialog.vue:113-123`. Live repro 2026-05-23: user opens DataObject тЖТ "Add data reference" тЖТ picks a 12.1 MB .rdk file тЖТ picks existing FileContainer тЖТ clicks Upload тЖТ 400 `fileOids must not be empty`. The 2-step backend flow is: (a) POST file content to `/shepard/api/fileContainers/{cid}/payload` returning fileOid, (b) POST `{name, fileContainerId, fileOids: [oid]}` to `/collections/{cid}/dataObjects/{did}/fileReferences`. Either step (a) is failing silently and step (b) fires anyway, OR step (b) doesn't await the step (a) Promise. Frontend file: search `frontend/components/dialog/AddDataReferenceDialog.vue` or similar; also `frontend/composables/api/useFileReferences.ts`. Likely fix: chain `await uploadToContainer(file) тЖТ const oid = response.oid тЖТ createFileReference({fileOids: [oid]})`. UX-FRIENDLY-ERRORS would surface this honestly (the error toast literally truncates to "Error while createFileReference:"). | M | queued | Source: 2026-05-23 screenshot evidence + curl-traced 400 reproduction. Workaround: 2-step curl-upload (literal command in commit body). Pairs with UX-FRIENDLY-ERRORS + #135 file upload progress + PERM-SYSTEM-REVIEW (this is the kind of failure mode the permission audit must include). |

| BUG-148-DESIGN-ASSERT-TEST | **Lock the DataObject-permissions inheritance contract into a regression-anti-test.** BUG-148 (2026-05-24) was a misdiagnosis ("DO creation should seed a Permissions record"); the real design is that DOs inherit from parent Collection via `PermissionsService.isAccessAllowedForDataObjectAppId` (lines 291-329) and the 3-arg fallback overload (lines 276-289). | V14-WHERE-CLAUSE-TIGHTEN | **V14 orphan-permissions backfill WHERE clause is too broad.** `V14__Backfill_orphan_permissions.cypher` line 44-45 matches `(e:BasicEntity) WHERE NOT (e)-[:has_permissions]->(:Permissions)` тАФ but DataObject + BasicReference ARE BasicEntity nodes designed to have NO direct Permissions (they inherit from parent Collection). V90__Tighten_orphan_permissions_backfill.cypher removes any such incorrectly-attached Permissions (legacyBackfill='A0-V14') from DataObject/BasicReference nodes, then DETACH DELETEs the orphaned Permissions node if no other incoming edges remain. | LOG-AS-PROV-ARTEFACT | **Shepard logs (processed) as PROV-O artefact describing mutations.** Distinct from LOG-ENHANCEMENT but compose-able with it: every Shepard log record that describes a mutation (POST/PUT/PATCH/DELETE) becomes a typed `:Activity` in the prov substrate тАФ `prov:wasAttributedTo` (user), `prov:used` (input refs), `prov:generated` (output refs), `prov:atTime` (timestamp), `shepard:operation` (verb+path), `shepard:resultStatus` (http). Processing pipeline: VictoriaLogs sidecar ingests raw logs тЖТ a normaliser (plugin? sidecar? in-tree filter?) extracts mutation events тЖТ writes :Activity nodes to Neo4j. **Recursion**: every Shepard mutation thus gets two trails тАФ the raw log (operational) and the typed prov node (semantic). Activity diff = log diff projected through PROV-O. The case-study value: a queryable "what actually changed and why" surface that survives long after the log retention window. Pairs with PROV1a (ProvenanceCaptureFilter тАФ already captures mutations, but as filter-time records, not log-processed) тАФ open question: dual-write vs. consolidate to one path. | L | queued | Source: 2026-05-23 user flag ("shepard logs (maybe processed) as prov artefact describing mutations"). | MOBILE-PWA | **Shepard frontend as a Progressive Web App (PWA) for mobile.** Researchers + auditors increasingly check Shepard from phones / tablets тАФ esp. on the shop floor (per the manufacturing-quality persona's ruggedized terminal requirement). | AAS-CODE-EXTRACTION | **Extract in-tree AAS code into `shepard-plugin-aas` proper.** Today AAS lives partly in `plugins/aas/` and partly in-tree (per task #82 + AAS1 row showing `AAS1a done; rest queued`). | HTML-TO-MD-MIGRATION | **Migrate all rendered fields from HTML to Markdown тАФ combined with block-editor (editor.js / BlockNote) research.** User flags 2026-05-23: ("move from html rendering to markdown in all fields /migrate") + ("combine with editor js research"). The migration target is not "markdown text in a textarea" but a **shape-driven block editor** where each block is a typed Shepard individual, serialised to markdown for storage. **Phase A тАФ data migration**: (a) inventory HTML-bearing fields backend (`description`, `notes`, attributes, lab-journal entries, ref comments) + frontend (`v-html`, contenteditable, rich-text); (b) HTML тЖТ markdown via `turndown` on read OR one-shot Cypher/SQL; (c) markdown sanitiser tests (XSS, scripts, styles, malicious links); (d) export round-trip test. **Phase B тАФ block editor**: (e) pick base тАФ **editor.js** (MIT, flexible blocks) vs **BlockNote** (MIT, Notion-flavour UX) тАФ full reuse-survey per `feedback_reuse_before_reimplement.md`; (f) each block type maps to a typed Shepard individual (heading / paragraph / table тЖТ existing TableContainer / code / image тЖТ file-reference / ts-chart тЖТ embedded TS view / shepard-ref тЖТ any artefact); (g) mode A form-shapes from SHACL templates + mode B free-text; (h) per-block `fair2r:modeOfProduction` + author + timestamp attribution; (i) lossless markdown round-trip; (j) admin-configurable block-type registry. Subsumes `project_block_editor.md`. Migration mode: backward-read тЖТ forward-write тЖТ drop HTML. | L | queued | Source: 2026-05-23 user flags. Pairs with PV1a (markdown diffs cleanly), UX-FRIENDLY-ERRORS, LABJOURNAL-SCIENTIFIC-TWITTER (the labjournal IS the canonical consumer of the new block editor). |

| LABJOURNAL-SCIENTIFIC-TWITTER | **Lab journal as scientific twitter тАФ direct references to Shepard artefacts of all types; render specifics supplied by plugins; AI agents can join the convo.** User flags 2026-05-23: ("labjournal should be a scientific twitter with direct references to shepard artifacts (of all types - specifics should be supplied by plugins responsible)") + ("maybe even agents ca join the convo"). The shape: every lab-journal entry is a short post (twitter-style, but no length limit) authored by either a human OR an AI agent (both with f(ai)┬▓r attribution). Entries can **directly reference** any Shepard artefact тАФ DataObject, Collection, FileReference, TimeseriesReference, StructuredDataReference, GitReference, AAS submodel, ImageBundle frame, anything a plugin contributes as a `PayloadKind`. The **render specifics for each reference type come from the plugin responsible** for that PayloadKind (per the PayloadKind SPI тАФ image plugin renders thumbnail-with-link, TS plugin renders live-sparkline-snippet, GitReference renders commit-shape, etc.) тАФ labjournal core knows nothing about how to render a TS chart; it asks the TS plugin. **Threading**: entries can reply to other entries (twitter-style); branch into discussion sub-threads; pin pinnable posts; mention users (`@kreb_fl`) + agents (`@claude-opus-4-7`). **Agent participation**: AI agents post into the labjournal under their model identity with mandatory `ЁЯдЦ Posted by` transparency line (per `feedback_role_agents_file_issues.md` extended pattern); the agent's reasoning per post is captured + cite-able. **Agent capabilities in-thread** (per user flag 2026-05-23 "assisting in research questions - ordering thoughts - reformatting extracting semantic anchors"): (1) **research-question assistance** тАФ agent surfaces related artefacts, related literature (via paper-search MCP), open-question gaps; (2) **thought-ordering** тАФ agent suggests reorderings of a chain of posts, identifies missing transitions, surfaces implicit assumptions; (3) **reformatting** тАФ agent polishes markdown formatting, suggests block-type replacements (e.g. "this list reads better as a table"), maintains house-style; (4) **semantic-anchor extraction** тАФ agent reads free-text posts and proposes typed annotations from the active ontology (CHAMEO / Material OWL / m4i / domain-vocabulary), surfacing them as user-acceptable suggestions per the f(ai)┬▓r five-rung acceptance ladder. Each agent suggestion lands as a NEW post in the thread (not an inline edit) тАФ preserving the conversational shape + the human's final-decision authority. **Composition**: built on top of HTML-TO-MD-MIGRATION's block editor тАФ each post IS a block-editor document with first-class artefact-reference blocks. Replaces the existing lab-journal entry shape (which is plain markdown today per J1 chain). | XL | queued | Source: 2026-05-23 user flags. Pairs with HTML-TO-MD-MIGRATION (block editor substrate), TPL9 (f(ai)┬▓r AI provenance), PERSONA-ISSUES-FROM-AUDIT (the AI-can-post-with-transparency pattern), J1d (lab-journal entry history panel + diff viewer тАФ the new shape needs new viewers), NTF1 (notifications: who got mentioned). Cross-references `project_block_editor.md` (Twitter-hybrid attribution per block тАФ already in memory; this row makes it concrete for labjournal). |

a specific predicate-level integration gap between f(ai)┬▓r (this fork's
PROV-O extension; `noheton/f-ai-r`) and the RDA FAIR4ML schema.org
extension (`w3id.org/fair4ml`). Sequence them after PROMPT1 (the
PromptLog substrate is the canonical f(ai)┬▓r consumer in the fork).

Conclusion: f(ai)┬▓r and FAIR4ML are complementary along orthogonal axes (authoring vs distribution); the thesis posture is A+B (gap-filling + lifecycle-stage complementarity), not C (competition). | S | **feature-defined 2026-05-23** | Source doc landed. | UI-011e | **`# DOs` column shows 0 everywhere on `/collections` list.** Surfaced by UX Scrutinizer 2026-05-24. **Root cause turned out to be different from the task hypothesis:** `GET /v2/collections` (CollectionV2Rest тЖТ CollectionDAO) already returns correct counts on live (LUMEN=17, MFFD-Dropbox=8514, Home=3). The frontend `/collections` page does NOT call that endpoint тАФ it calls `SearchApi.searchCollections` тЖТ `POST /shepard/api/search/collections` тЖТ `SearchDAO.findCollections`, whose `emitCollectionReturnPart` used `Neighborhood.ESSENTIAL` (= `path=(c)-[*0..1]->(n) WHERE n:Permission OR n:User`). ESSENTIAL never walks DataObjects, so `CollectionIO.dataObjectIds[]` came back empty on every search result. Fix: flip the collection projection to `Neighborhood.EVERYTHING` (depth 1) тАФ the same neighborhood `CollectionDAO.findAllCollectionsByShepardId` already uses successfully in production. Container / User / UserGroup `emit*ReturnPart` helpers stay on ESSENTIAL (their cells don't expose nested-entity counts). | S | тЬЕ **shipped** (worktree UI-011e) | UI-011 follow-up; ships before UI-011a..d because it's broken not deferred. On every Phase-2/3/5 workflow during cold load the UI flashed a red error toast claiming data was unavailable тАФ actually `handleError()` was emitting on `AbortError` (route changed mid-flight) and on `401 Unauthorized` (which the auth-refresh middleware silently handles). ## CRIT-2026-05-24-* тАФ Critical operational risks

| ID | description | effort | status | notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| ~~CRIT-LOMBOK-APT~~ | **RETRACTED 2026-05-24** тАФ false alarm caused by local working-directory pollution. Three pre-existing dirty mods to `Collection.java` / `DataObjectIO.java` / `SparqlQueryValidator.java` were carried in canonical `/opt/shepard` since session start; the dirty WD made Lombok APT fail. Agent worktrees (`git worktree add` тЖТ clean HEAD checkout) build fine тАФ verified by reproducing `mvn clean compile -DskipTests` in `/opt/shepard/.claude/worktrees/agent-*/backend` тЖТ green. Three subsequent worktree-isolated agents (UI-011e, OPS-MIGRATION-HEALTHCHECK, RDM-001) all built + deployed + smoked 25/25 from canonical-main-equivalent state. The PROV-resolver agent's report was accurate-for-their-moment but conflated transient cherry-pick state with a main-branch bug. | XS | тЬЕ **resolved (false alarm)** | Lesson kept as CRIT-SMOKE-NOT-CATCHING-BUILD-BREAK below. Operator note: the three dirty session-original files are still in `/opt/shepard` WD; `git stash` or `git checkout HEAD -- <files>` to restore main if not actively worked on. |
| CRIT-SMOKE-NOT-CATCHING-BUILD-BREAK | **Smoke endpoint passes against a stale running image even when a fresh `mvn clean compile` is broken.** This is how CRIT-LOMBOK-APT hid for a full session. Fix: chain `make build-backend` as a hard prerequisite of `make smoke` (or add a `make smoke-with-build` target that's the default), so a broken main can't deploy "successfully". | S | тЬЕ **shipped** 2026-05-24 | OPS hygiene bundle. `smoke: build-backend` now in `Makefile`. Self-test caught a probe-injected error AND surfaced a real `TargetEntityResolver.resolve(String)` duplicate-method break sitting on main тАФ filed as `CRIT-MAIN-BROKEN-TARGETENTITYRESOLVER-DUPLICATE` below. See `aidocs/agent-findings/ops-hygiene-bundle-2026-05-24.md`. |
| CRIT-WORKTREE-DOCKER-CACHE | **`make redeploy-frontend` reports success but ships a STALE image from agent worktrees.** Surfaced by UX-Pattern-D agent 2026-05-24: their first `make redeploy-frontend` returned green smoke 25/25 but the live frontend still served the old code. Recovery required `rm -rf .output .nuxt && npm run build && docker build && docker compose up -d --force-recreate frontend`. Suspected: docker layer cache + Nuxt `.output` cache + dev-mode hot-swap container retention combine to mask the staleness. The authoritative live-deploy verify command is `docker exec infrastructure-frontend-1 grep -l <new-testid> /app/server/chunks/build/*.mjs` тАФ chain into `make smoke` or a new `make verify-frontend-deploy` target so it can't repeat. Same family as CRIT-SMOKE-NOT-CATCHING-BUILD-BREAK above (smoke probes running image not fresh code). | M | тЬЕ **shipped** 2026-05-24 | OPS hygiene bundle. Resolved as a sibling of MK-REDEPLOY-FORCE-RECREATE тАФ `--force-recreate <service>` now folded into every `redeploy*` Makefile target, which closes the docker-cache trap. `verify-frontend-deploy` sentinel-check target deliberately deferred per the OPS-bundle task brief ("--force-recreate alone closes 80%"). |

## SM1a тАФ User-configurable orphan-data retention per container (DEFAULT 1 YEAR)

| ID | description | effort | status | notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| SM1a | **Per-container user-configurable retention for non-referenced data, default 1 year, with notification warnings.** Researcher decides on a per-container basis (or accepts the instance-admin default) how long non-referenced data lives before deletion. The `INTEGRITY RULE` from `feedback_referenced_data_infinite_retention.md` still holds тАФ referenced data is never deleted. Only data with `refs=0 AND payload>0 AND not in active job state` is subject to the retention clock. **Default 1 year** (revises the prior SM1 design memory which had `infinite grace`; rationale: most operators don't actually want indefinite orphan accumulation; explicit-opt-in for "infinite" is the safer default-OFF posture). **Per-container fields** on TS / File / SD containers: `orphan_retention_days: int` (NULL = use instance default, 0 = delete-on-next-sweep, -1 = infinite), `orphan_retention_owner_notified_at: timestamp?`. **Notification cadence**: nag at 30d / 7d / 1d before deletion (NTF1 dep), one final "deleted N items" on actual deletion. **UI**: a Retention card on each container detail page with the current setting + a select with explicit options (Infinite / 1 year / 90 days / 30 days / Delete-on-orphan); plus an instance-admin landing tile to set the instance default. **Audit**: every retention-driven deletion lands in `:Activity` with `:RetentionSweep` source kind. **Acceptance**: a researcher can opt into infinite, accept the 1-year default, or tighten to 30d; gets the nag notifications; sees deletions in the activity trail. | L | queued | Revises `project_storage_management.md` default (infinite тЖТ 1 year). Depends on: NTF1 (notifications, in design), `:Activity` source-kind extension. Frontend + backend + Cypher migration (per-container retention fields) + scheduled-job (sweep). Update aidocs/34 + 44 + model-inventory. **Operator-facing default change тАФ document loudly in v6.x release notes.** |
| SM1a-RUNBOOK | **Operator runbook for retention policy** тАФ `docs/admin/runbooks/orphan-retention-policy.md`. Covers: where to set the instance default, what the per-container override does, how the nag cadence fires, how to recover a container from delete-on-next-sweep state in the brief window before it fires, audit-trail query (`MATCH (a:Activity {sourceKind: 'RetentionSweep'})`), and how to opt out entirely (set instance default to infinite). Sibling to `docs/admin/runbooks/restore-tsdb-container-neo4j-shadow.md`. | S | done (2026-05-27) | Runbook written as `stage: feature-defined` with `[FUTURE]` tags throughout тАФ SM1a is designed but not yet shipped. Audit-trail Cypher includes both pre-SM1a fallback (`summary CONTAINS 'RetentionSweep'`) and full post-SM1a query (`sourceKind = 'RetentionSweep'`). |

## PROV-2026-05-24-* тАФ Provenance trail completeness gaps

Source: `aidocs/agent-findings/rdm-004-provenance-empty-fix-2026-05-24.md` (closes RDM-2026-05-24-004). Root-cause analysis showed the LUMEN DO Provenance panel renders an empty list because 99.93 % of recorded Activities have `targetKind=NULL`/`targetAppId=NULL` тАФ the capture filter's path resolver fails on subresource paths and on v1 numeric-id paths. The empty-state copy fix (Bucket D) shipped in the same PR; the structural pieces are tracked below.

| ID | Item | effort | status | notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| PROV-EMPTY-STATE-COPY | **`DataObjectProvLog.vue` empty state now distinguishes "no events recorded" from "filter hid everything".** Adds an optional `hint` prop on `EmptyListIcon` and two computed branches (extracted to `frontend/utils/provenanceEmptyState.ts` for testability). Closes the trust-killer signal: a researcher landing on a DO with zero activities now reads a precise explanation of capture scope instead of a suspect empty panel. | XS | тЬЕ **shipped** 2026-05-24 | Frontend-only, <50 LOC. Vitest passes. See findings doc above. |
| PROV-RESOLVER-PATHWALK | **`TargetEntityResolver` walks the path right-to-left for the deepest `(kind, id)` pair instead of insisting on the tail.** Subresource creates now attach to the newly-minted entity, not its parent. Pre-fix: `POST /v2/collections/<COLL-uuid>/dataobjects` recorded the Collection UUID with kind `DataObject` (wrong target). Post-fix: walks right-to-left for `(knownPlural, idLike)` pairs; unknown plurals no longer fall back to title-casing тАФ verb-shaped segments like `payload`/`diff`/`detect-anomalies` can't pollute `targetKind` any more. Pure refactor split: `PathTargetParser` (static parser) + `TargetEntityResolver` (CDI bean wiring the parser to numeric lookup). | M | тЬЕ **shipped** 2026-05-24 | Closes RDM-2026-05-24-004 bucket B. Same PR as PROV-V1-NUMERIC-LOOKUP. See `aidocs/agent-findings/prov-resolver-fix-2026-05-24.md`. |
| PROV-V1-NUMERIC-LOOKUP | **Capture-time resolution of `/shepard/api/...` numeric IDs тЖТ appIds via a generic `EntityAppIdLookup` helper.** Single parameterised Cypher (`MATCH (n:<Label>) WHERE n.shepardId=$id ...`) over the static label allow-list; deviates from the brief's per-DAO method shape because all targets share `AbstractEntity` (carries `appId`) + `VersionableEntity` (carries `shepardId`), so one helper covers every kind with zero entity-file edits. On miss the Activity lands with `targetKind` set + `targetAppId=null` тАФ capture is never blocked. The optional backfill is split off as `PROV-BACKFILL-MIGRATION`. | L | тЬЕ **shipped** 2026-05-24 | Closes RDM-2026-05-24-004 bucket C. Same PR as PROV-RESOLVER-PATHWALK. See findings doc. |
| PROV-BACKFILL-MIGRATION | **One-off backfill of the ~280 K orphaned `:Activity` rows whose `targetKind=NULL`.** Implementation should re-use the production `PathTargetParser` from Java (not re-implement string parsing in Cypher), call `EntityAppIdLookup` for each parsed `(kind, numericId)` pair, and write the result back via `apoc.periodic.iterate` (batched, idempotent). Acceptance: post-migration `MATCH (a:Activity) WHERE a.targetKind IS NULL RETURN count(a)` drops by тЙе 250 K. Optional rollback `V**_R__backfill_activity_targets.cypher` clears the back-filled fields. Split from PROV-V1-NUMERIC-LOOKUP to keep this PR shippable; only recovers historic seed traffic. | M | queued | Not blocking; the resolver fix already prevents the bug recurring for new writes. |
| PROV-CAPTURE-READS-DECISION | **Decide whether `shepard.provenance.capture-reads` flips from `false` to `true` for `/v2/...` paths.** Current default is off per `aidocs/55 ┬з4` (read-volume bounding); the f(ai)┬▓r promise of "every interaction is observable" implies on. Sizing exercise: count GETs/day on MFFD-Dropbox, multiply by `retention-days=730`, check Neo4j page-cache + disk delta. If green, flip the default for `/v2/` paths only (v1 stays off to keep upstream-compat ops cost predictable). Pairs with PROV-RESOLVER-PATHWALK + PROV-V1-NUMERIC-LOOKUP тАФ flipping reads without resolver fixes just multiplies the NULL-target row count. | S (design) + M (impl) | queued | Design call. Subsumes the f(ai)┬▓r AI-collaboration provenance line in `aidocs/55 ┬з4` and the RDM-004 Bucket A verdict. |
| RDM-002-E2E-FIX | **RDM-002 Playwright e2e fails on live despite code shipped + smoke green.** All 5 tests in `e2e/tests/rdm-002-orcid-on-profile.spec.ts` failed on `expect(getByTestId("profile-identity-section")).toBeVisible()` post-deploy `4ef13776`. Source has the test-id; `useRouteFragment` is hash-based and `/me#profile` matches `UserFragments.PROFILE`. Likely a race: spec asserts before the SSR-hydrated `routeFragment` ref updates. Add `await page.waitForSelector('[data-testid="profile-identity-section"]', { timeout: 5000 })` or `await page.waitForLoadState('networkidle')` before the assertion. | XS | тЬЕ **done 2026-05-26** | RDM-002 follow-up. | BUG-LJ-V1-COLL-ID | **`GET /v2/collections/{appId}/lab-journal-entries` returns 500 on any collection with entries** (LUMEN exposes it; MFFD-Dropbox hid it with empty list). Surfaced by RDM-005 widget agent 2026-05-24. **Brief's hypothesis was wrong by primary evidence**: not a v1-numeric-id тЖТ appId resolver gap тАФ LUMEN's Collection node already has `appId=019e30b0-...` populated and `EntityIdResolver.resolveLong` succeeds; the resolver is irrelevant to this bug. **Actual root cause**: `CollectionLabJournalEntriesDAO`'s `RETURN DISTINCT lje` projection did not hydrate the INCOMING `has_labjournalentry` edge back to DataObject, so `LabJournalEntry.getDataObject()` came back null on every entry and `LabJournalEntryIO`'s constructor NPEd on `dataObject.getShepardId()`. **Fix**: DAO Cypher now projects a depth-1 neighbourhood path (`MATCH path=(lje)-[*0..1]-(n) ... RETURN lje, nodes(path), relationships(path)`) тАФ the canonical `CypherQueryHelper.getReturnPart` pattern тАФ so the OGM hydrates both directions. Resource adds a defensive orphan-skip + WARN log as belt-and-braces. Unrelated to PROV-V1-NUMERIC-LOOKUP. | S | тЬЕ **shipped** 2026-05-24 | See `aidocs/agent-findings/bug-lj-v1-coll-id-fix-2026-05-24.md`. Live verification post-deploy. |
| OGM-HYDRATION-AUDIT | **Audit every `findByQuery` callsite in v2 DAOs for the `RETURN <entity>`-only pattern that triggered BUG-LJ-V1-COLL-ID** тАФ any place returning just the leaf node without a `nodes(path), relationships(path)` projection silently drops INCOMING relationships, and the bug only surfaces when the IO/service touches those fields. The canonical safe pattern is `CypherQueryHelper.getReturnPart(entity)`. Sweep should catch other UI-XXX bulk endpoints landed in 2026-05 that may carry the same defect (e.g., new collection-walk DAOs in `de.dlr.shepard.v2.*.daos`). | S | тЬЕ **done (2026-05-27)** | Audit complete. v2 DAO sweep: `aidocs/agent-findings/ogm-hydration-audit-2026-05-24.md`. Service-layer sweep: `aidocs/agent-findings/ogm-hydration-service-layer-2026-05-27.md`. `DataObjectDAO.findByAppId` fix already applied (line 426: `session.load(DataObject.class, stub.getId(), DEPTH_ENTITY)`). Safety comment added to `LabJournalEntryService.getCollectionId()` documenting why `findByNeo4jId` is safe and what pattern would reintroduce BUG-LJ-V1. |
| MK-REDEPLOY-FORCE-RECREATE | **`make redeploy-frontend` ships stale image because `docker compose up -d --no-build` reuses the existing container even after `image-frontend` rebuilt.** Surfaced independently by Pattern-D agent + UX-bundle agent 2026-05-24. ## MONGO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-* тАФ MongoDB substrate audit (live shepard)

Filed 2026-05-24 by the **MongoDB substrate audit agent** running against
live `infrastructure-mongodb-1` (MongoDB 8.0.4). Findings file:
`aidocs/agent-findings/mongodb-substrate-audit-2026-05-24.md`. Pairs with
sibling agent #209's file-routing investigation; both feed
`MFFD-DB-AUDIT-REAL-DATA`.

| ID | Description | Size | Status | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| MONGO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-001 | **N+1 in `StructuredDataSearchService.findMatchingReferences:76-95`** тАФ one Mongo round-trip per reachable reference. Confirms long-standing SD1 backlog row with live evidence. Fix: either ship SD1 (deprecate Mongo SD query path тЖТ Postgres), or batch the per-container `find()` calls into a single `$or` / `$in` over the union of reachable containers. **MAJOR**. | M | queued | Cite to SD1. Audit row is the perf-evidence partner. |
| MONGO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-002 | **One Mongo collection per FileContainer + StructuredDataContainer** (`FileService.createFileContainer`, `StructuredDataService.createStructuredDataContainer`). Proven not to scale: BUG-F surfaced 4 197 SD collections at MFFD volume. Mongo-side cleanup ran post-redrive but **Neo4j carries 4 197 `:StructuredDataContainer{deleted: TRUE}` tombstones with no Mongo counterpart** (verified 2026-05-24 sample of 5 mongoIds: all GONE from Mongo). Long-term fix is structural (SD1 тЖТ Postgres for SD; FS1 family already in flight for files). Short-term fix: GC the Neo4j tombstones. **MAJOR**. | M | queued | Pairs with SD-WIPE-AND-REGET + SM1 retention. |
| MONGO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-003 | **JSON-string concatenation to build Mongo query** in `StructuredDataSearchService:91` (`mongoQuery += ", " + mongoSearchQuery + "}"` тЖТ `Document.parse(mongoQuery)`). Same shape as the C5/C5b Cypher string-build pattern that was explicitly killed in this fork. Should use `com.mongodb.client.model.Filters` DSL. Lower exploit ceiling than the Cypher case (Mongo `$where` is not used anywhere) but still wrong. **MAJOR**. | S | done (2026-05-27) | Fixed in `StructuredDataSearchService.java`: replaced string-concat with `Filters.and(in("_id", objectIds), Document.parse("{" + userQuery + "}"))`. Dead helpers `makeMongoQueryId`/`makeMongoQueryArray` removed. 2 new ArgumentCaptor tests added. Pairs with MONGO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-001 тАФ both die when SD1 ships. |
| MONGO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-004 | **No backend-side array-wrap fallback in `StructuredDataService.createStructuredData:53`** (`Document.parse(payload.getPayload())`). BUG-E v15.12 wraps client-side in the importer; any non-importer client POSTing a JSON array as SD payload still 500s with the BSON-array exception. Defensive fix: detect `payload.trim().startsWith("[")` тЖТ wrap as `{items: [...], _wrapped: "v15.12-bug-e"}` server-side. Closes the BUG-E class permanently. **MAJOR**. | S | done (2026-05-27) | Sibling: `MFFD-SD-BACKEND-WRAP-FALLBACK` (preexisting). Fixed in `StructuredDataService.java` + 3 new tests in `StructuredDataServiceTest.java`. |
| MONGO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-005 | **No `$jsonSchema` validators on any of 21 collections.** Cheap wins available on the singleton-schema collections: `userAvatars` (4 fields), `_shepard_files`, `_shepard_videos`, and the bookkeeping shape inside every `FileContainer*` (`{createdAt, name, md5, fileSize, FileMongoId}`). Per-container SD collections must stay polymorphic by design. Supports the FAIR R1 rigour the platform is reaching for. **MAJOR**. | S | done (2026-05-27) | warn-mode validators on 3 singleton collections (`userAvatars`, `_shepard_files`, `_shepard_videos`) shipped in `MongoSchemaInitializer.java` (`@ApplicationScoped` + `@Observes StartupEvent`, idempotent `collMod`/`createCollection`). `_shepard_videos` confirmed as singleton-schema doc collection (same FileService bookkeeping shape, fixed name unlike `FileContainer*`). per-container `FileContainer*` deferred тАФ dynamically-named UUID collections, different scope. TODO: flip `validationAction` to `"error"` after confirming existing data clean. 25 unit tests in `MongoSchemaInitializerTest.java`. |
| MONGO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-006 | **`FileService.deleteFileContainer:237-240` sequential per-doc GridFS delete loop.** N round-trips to delete N files in a container. Bulk variants exist in driver 5.1+ (`bucket.delete(List<ObjectId>)`). For the canonical MFFD `FileContainer7693e977тАж` (34 files) this is 34 round-trips on every cleanup. **MINOR**. | XS | done (2026-05-27) | Driver 5.1.x does not expose `delete(List<ObjectId>)`; shipped pre-fetch-then-delete: cursor materialised into `List<ObjectId>` via `.map().into()` in one pass, then iterated for deletes тАФ separates cursor round-trips from write ops. A future `fs.files.deleteMany($in)` + `fs.chunks.deleteMany($in)` bypass (O(2) round-trips) tracked separately. Tests: `deleteExistingFileContainerTest` (single-file), `_multiFile` (3 files, all deletes verified), `_emptyContainer` (0 deletes, drop still runs). |
| MONGO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-007 | **`FileMongoId` stored as STRING but `fs.files._id` is ObjectId** across `_shepard_files`, `_shepard_videos`, every `FileContainer*` collection. Java side casts at every read (`new ObjectId(...)`) so correctness holds, but any Mongo aggregation `$lookup` join from a shadow collection into `fs.files` silently returns empty unless the join expression pre-casts. Future analytics / cleanup / orphan-scan jobs will trip on this. Mitigations: (a) store as ObjectId; (b) document the convention loudly; (c) add a `$lookup`-with-`$convert` helper. **MINOR**. | S | done (2026-05-27) тАФ convention documented; migration to native ObjectId storage deferred (needs V## data migration across all shadow collections). | Convention comment added above `FILEID_ATTR` in `FileService.java`; `$lookup`-with-`$convert` helper note added to `MongoSchemaInitializer.java` class-level Javadoc. |
| MONGO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-008 | **`StructuredDataService.createStructuredData:60-61` silently strips underscore-prefixed user keys.** `var forbidden = toInsert.keySet().stream().filter(k -> k.startsWith("_")).toList(); forbidden.forEach(toInsert::remove);` тАФ user payload `_my_field` is data-lost without warning. Should: (a) log a `Log.warn` on every strip; (b) restrict to known-conflicting keys (`_id`, `_meta`) instead of all `_*`; (c) reject the payload with 400 + field-list if any conflict. **MINOR**. | XS | ЁЯдЦ hourly-bot-shipped-beta (PR #1511) | Cheap fix; the silent-data-loss class is the worst kind of API foot-gun. |
| MONGO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-009 | **No Mongo connection-pool config.** Driver defaults apply (`maxPoolSize=100`, `minPoolSize=0`, `maxIdleTimeMS=тИЮ`, `serverSelectionTimeoutMS=30s`). Document defaults explicitly in `application.properties` + tune from Prometheus metrics per PERF2b's `mongo_latency_high` rule. **GAP**. | S | тЬЕ **done (2026-05-27)** | Defaults documented as commented-out block in `application.properties` after the `connection-string` line; operator now sees defaults and PERF2b guidance without any active override. |
| MONGO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-010 | **No TTL indexes anywhere.** Nothing self-prunes. SM1 retention and PRE-MUT-SNAP* both need this; today their snapshots / orphan-grace data would grow without bound in Mongo. Audit row is the dependency-flag for those two designs. **GAP**. | M | queued | Cite SM1 + PRE-MUT-SNAP1. |
| MONGO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-011 | **`quarkus.mongodb.connection-string=mongodb://mongo@mongodb:27017` carries no DB name; `MongoClientWrapper.init()` silently falls back to literal `"database"`.** An admin who overrides the URI and forgets the DB segment lands writes into the wrong DB without error. Fix: log loudly at startup, or refuse start when DB name absent (the prod URI already has it; this would only affect future overrides). **GAP**. | XS | done (2026-05-27) | Shipped: `shouldWarnAboutFallback()` static helper + `LOG.warn` in `init()` when resolved name is fallback AND no explicit `quarkus.mongodb.database` key is set. Tests in `MongoClientWrapperTest`. |
| MONGO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-012 | **No per-collection / per-container Mongo size cap.** A single 532 MB `Confluence-space-export-151906-2.html.zip` upload (2026-05-22) is 60% of the entire Mongo substrate. Add: (a) admin alert when any container exceeds `shepard.mongo.container.max-bytes` (default 1 GiB); (b) `shepard.mongo.file.max-bytes` upload-rejection cap (default 2 GiB). Pair with SM1a's 1-year default retention. **GAP**. | S | тЬЕ **done (2026-05-27)** | (b) shipped: `shepard.mongo.file.max-bytes=2147483648` (2 GiB default). Guard added in `FileService.enforceFileSizeCap()` тАФ called from all GridFS write paths (`createFile(..long..)`, `createFileWithSha256(..long..)`). All REST callers (`FileRest`, `FileBundleReferenceRest`, `FileReferenceV2Rest`) updated to pass temp-file length. `VideoStreamReferenceService` also guards using same config key. Throws `InvalidRequestException` (HTTP 400) before any GridFS write. Two-layer model documented: set `quarkus.http.limits.max-body-size` to also block at the HTTP layer. (a) per-container admin alert deferred to SM1a. Test: `createFile_exceedsMaxBytes_throwsInvalidRequestException` in `FileServiceTest`. |
| MONGO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-013 | **3├Ч duplicate `lumen-hotfire.mp4` blobs in `_shepard_videos`** (8.6 MB each ├Ч 3 = 26 MB redundant). Same MD5, distinct ObjectIds тАФ each upload created a fresh GridFS blob with no dedup. Stop-gap: deduplicate by MD5 + reuse the existing blob if present. Long-term: SHA-256-content-addressable storage is the FS1/Garage trajectory, but the GridFS path inherits the dup-tolerant behaviour today. **MINOR**. | S | тЬЕ **done (2026-05-27)** | Shipped: `VideoStreamReferenceService.storeWithDedup()` buffers stream тЙд 100 MiB, computes MD5, checks `_shepard_videos` for existing document with same digest, reuses existing OID if found. Large files (> 100 MiB) bypass buffering and stream directly. Tests: `storeWithDedup_duplicateMd5_reusesExistingBlob` + `storeWithDedup_newMd5_uploadsNewBlob` in `VideoStreamReferenceServiceTest`. |
| MONGO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-014 | **6 empty per-container Mongo collections (24 KB wasted) тАФ `StructuredDataContainer839614f2`, `тАж54ec30b6`, `тАж4702ed7d`, `тАж4786abf3`, `тАж6931e4d4`, `тАж4277ad7c`, `FileContainerecc172da`, `FileContainer8a3e519e`.** Each is a placeholder that was created but never written to. Either the container-create endpoint doesn't roll back on subsequent failure, or the data shape permits create-and-never-use. Investigate the create path for missing transactional bookkeeping. **MINOR**. | XS | done (2026-05-27) тАФ **two root causes confirmed, both WAI at current scale, one structural gap logged.** (1) **Normal create-and-never-use:** Mongo collection is created immediately on container create (`createStructuredDataContainer()` / `createFileContainer()` call `mongoDatabase.createCollection()` as their first step), so any container created but never written to will leave an empty collection. This is the expected lifecycle тАФ the 8 empty collections are containers that were created (correctly) but had no data uploaded to them. (2) **Missing rollback on create failure:** `StructuredDataContainerService.createContainer()` creates the Mongo collection first, then writes the Neo4j node (`structuredDataContainerDAO.createOrUpdate`), then calls `permissionsService.createPermissions()`. Neither the Mongo write nor the Neo4j write are wrapped in a shared transaction (no `@Transactional` on any of these methods). If the Neo4j write or permissions write fails after the Mongo collection was already created, the collection becomes a permanent orphan. **Delete path is correctly wired** тАФ `deleteContainer()` always drops the Mongo collection. **Fix recommendation (not yet implemented):** Add Mongo collection cleanup to `createContainer()` catch block (try Mongo-create + Neo4j-create, drop Mongo collection on Neo4j failure). Alternatively, accept accumulation and add a `/v2/admin/mongo/orphan-sweep` endpoint for periodic admin cleanup. Fix is ~10 lines in each service; tracked for next maintenance window. | Audit-trail-followup. |

## PLUGIN-{SPATIAL,TABLES,HDF5}-AUDIT-2026-05-24-* тАФ plugin design audit findings

Source: [`aidocs/agent-findings/plugin-design-audit-2026-05-24.md`](agent-findings/plugin-design-audit-2026-05-24.md). Three plugins audited in parallel: spatial (PL1b + PV1c + A1c shipped; perf + frontend gaps), HDF5 (A5a/b/d shipped; A5c/A5e queued; frontend gap), tables (no row + no design doc yet тАФ file SSOT doc first).

### Spatial

| ID | Item | effort | status | notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| PLUGIN-SPATIAL-AUDIT-2026-05-24-001 | **PM1f sidecar migration тАФ declare `postgis` in `SpatiotemporalPluginManifest.sidecars()` + remove from central `infrastructure/docker-compose.yml`.** Closes the `feedback_plugins_declare_sidecars.md` gap. Cross-ref `file-s3` reference impl (`FileS3PluginManifestSidecarsTest`). Bundle into the same PR as PLUGIN-HDF5-AUDIT-2026-05-24-001 (matching shape; cross-cutting finding #1). | S | done (2026-05-27) тАФ sidecar declared in manifest; compose removal deferred to SidecarsAssembler milestone | Audit ┬зSpatial.E + cross-cutting ┬з1. |
| PLUGIN-SPATIAL-AUDIT-2026-05-24-002 | **`V1.1.0__indexes.sql` тАФ BRIN on `time` + GIN(`measurements jsonb_path_ops`).** Two cheapest perf wins per `aidocs/data/82 ┬з2.1+┬з2.3`. Additive index creation via `CREATE INDEX CONCURRENTLY`; zero migration risk. | XS | done (2026-05-27) | Audit ┬зSpatial.G + `aidocs/82 ┬з4` recommendation. `plugins/spatiotemporal/src/main/resources/db/spatial/migration/V1.1.0__indexes.sql` ships `spatial_data_points_time_brin` (BRIN, pages_per_range=32) + `spatial_data_points_measurements_gin` (GIN jsonb_path_ops); both `IF NOT EXISTS` for idempotency. Note: `CREATE INDEX CONCURRENTLY` cannot run inside a Flyway transaction; operators with large live tables may run indexes manually with CONCURRENTLY before upgrade тАФ `IF NOT EXISTS` guard will skip on migration run. |
| PLUGIN-SPATIAL-AUDIT-2026-05-24-003 | **MVT vector-tile endpoint + MapLibre frontend viewer.** New JAX-RS `GET /v2/spatial-data-containers/{appId}/tiles/{z}/{x}/{y}.mvt` returning `ST_AsMVT()` bytes; `SpatialDataMapView.vue` consuming via MapLibre GL JS vector source. Closes the frontend gap (no `*spatial*` components exist today). | M | queued | Audit ┬зSpatial.G + `aidocs/82 ┬з3`. |
| PLUGIN-SPATIAL-AUDIT-2026-05-24-004 | **Collapse separate `postgis` container into TS Postgres** (`postgis` extension + `shepard_spatial` schema). Cross-ref `POSTGRES-MULTITENANT-SCHEMA-DECISION`. Reclaims ~256MB and unlocks cross-substrate SQL JOINs (spatial-data ├Ч TS measurements ├Ч table-container rows). Gated on the in-flight `pgbouncer-audit` pool-sizing decision. | M | queued | Audit ┬зSpatial.C + cross-cutting ┬з3. |
| PLUGIN-SPATIAL-AUDIT-2026-05-24-005 | **`GeoQueryCapability` declaration on `PayloadKind` (additive, default-no-op).** Lets downstream consumers (search, MCP tools, OGC export) target spatial-supporting kinds generically without reflecting on repository classes. Defer until a second consumer materialises; file as a forward-pointer. | S (design) | parked | Audit ┬зSpatial.B + cross-cutting ┬з2. Carried forward by SPATIAL-V6-013 (no scope change). |
