| POSTGRES-MULTITENANT-SCHEMA-DECISION | **Decide: collapse multiple Postgres instances (TS-Postgres + postgis) into one with multiple schemas + extensions.** Three plugins want PG (TS, Tables, Spatial); current shape has two PG instances and is heading for three. Right answer: one PG + schemas `shepard_ts` (TimescaleDB hypertable) + `shepard_spatial` (PostGIS GIST) + `shepard_tables` (typed row data). Win: real SQL JOINs across substrates + simpler ops + one PgBouncer pool tree. Loss: less isolation; mitigation via PgBouncer per-schema pool. Gated on the in-flight `pgbouncer-audit` pool-sizing answer. | M (decision) + L (impl if chosen) | queued | Cross-cutting finding ┬з3. Covers PLUGIN-SPATIAL-AUDIT-2026-05-24-004 + PLUGIN-TABLES-AUDIT-2026-05-24-004 with one decision. |

## TS-AUDIT-2026-05-24-* тАФ TimescaleDB design audit findings

Source: [`aidocs/agent-findings/ts-design-audit-2026-05-24.md`](agent-findings/ts-design-audit-2026-05-24.md). Substrate-direct read-only audit of the live TimescaleDB 2.24.0 / PG16 instance on 2026-05-24. **Verdict: MIXED** тАФ 12 findings (2 CRITICAL, 5 MAJOR, 5 MINOR/observe). Operator's "very badly designed" hypothesis is REFUTED for the lifecycle/index/compression layer (V1.4/V1.7/V1.8/V1.11 migrations are thoughtful; 23├Ч compression ratio achieved; chunk_skipping enabled) but CONFIRMED for the write-path (string-INSERT per batch) and the value-storage shape (4-column polymorphism).

| ID | Item | effort | status | notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| TS-AUDIT-2026-05-24-001 | **CRITICAL (latent) тАФ 4-column polymorphic value table.** `timeseries_data_points` carries `double_value`, `int_value`, `string_value`, `boolean_value`; 100% of 81M live rows are Double; 3 columns ├Ч 81M rows тЙИ 2 GB dead weight. No `CHECK` constraint enforces exactly-one-non-null. Compounds once Boolean/String containers land (expected for MFFD welding digital IO + state machines). Cheap fix: `CHECK (num_nonnulls(...) = 1)` constraint (paired with TS-AUDIT-2026-05-24-003). Proper fix: defer to the TS-ID migration (`aidocs/platform/87`) тАФ partition by value-type into N hypertables, OR collapse to a single typed column. | XS (constraint) / L (column-drop) | queued | Audit AP-1. References TimescaleDB schema-design docs + Pavlo CMU 15-445 lecture 5. Pair with -003. |
| TS-AUDIT-2026-05-24-002 | **CRITICAL (write path) тАФ `INSERTтАжVALUES (тАж) ON CONFLICT DO UPDATE` builds fresh SQL per batch.** `TimeseriesDataPointRepository.buildInsertQueryObject` (line 207) constructs a unique SQL string with up to 20 001 placeholders per batch; `prepareThreshold=0` (required for PgBouncer transaction-mode) defeats the JDBC statement cache тЖТ every batch pays full parse + plan. **The COPY-based `insertManyDataPointsWithCopyCommand` already exists in the same file** (line 81) but only the Influx migration uses it. Route live writes through COPY for batches > 1000 rows; keep the parametric path for small batches. Conflict-handling preserved via session-scoped TEMP TABLE + dedupe-then-COPY. | M | queued | Audit AP-2. References TimescaleDB write-path best practice. Highest-leverage single fix in the audit. |
| TS-AUDIT-2026-05-24-003 | **MAJOR тАФ no `CHECK` constraint pairing value columns to `timeseries.value_type`.** The `timeseries` table guards its own `value_type` enum but `timeseries_data_points` has zero constraints linking rows to their parent's declared type. A misbehaving writer could insert `string_value` on a Double series and the DAO `getColumnName(valueType)` switch would never read it. Today only the DAO writes; the upcoming plugin SPI (Influx-line-protocol shim, OPC-UA bridge) breaks the assumption. Add `ALTER TABLE timeseries_data_points ADD CONSTRAINT chk_one_value_column CHECK (num_nonnulls(double_value, int_value, string_value, boolean_value) = 1);` тАФ cheap, idempotent. | XS | **done (2026-05-26)** | Audit AP-3. Pair with -001. Migration: `V1.18.0__add_ts_datapoints_value_check.sql`. |
| TS-AUDIT-2026-05-24-004 | **MAJOR (at scale) тАФ FK from hypertable to `timeseries` metadata.** `timeseries_data_points.timeseries_id тЖТ timeseries(id) ON DELETE CASCADE` is propagated to all 29 chunks (30 FK constraints visible in `pg_constraint`). Every INSERT triggers a lookup тАФ visible as 600K+ `timeseries_unique_b4a836fabc25` scans. Industry pattern: avoid FK on hypertables at high ingest; rely on application-level integrity + periodic GC sweep. Add `shepard.timeseries.fk.enabled` runtime flag (default true); idempotent drop-and-recreate migration; pairs with SM1a retention sweep. | S | queued | Audit AP-4. References TimescaleDB FK FAQ. Only matters above ~10K inserts/s; today the load is 87/s peak. |
| TS-AUDIT-2026-05-24-005 | **MAJOR (observability blind spot) тАФ no `pg_stat_statements` extension.** Zero query-shape observability today; this audit had to read code instead of metrics. One-line `shared_preload_libraries='timescaledb,pg_stat_statements'` config + Flyway `V1.12.0__add_pg_stat_statements.sql` (CREATE EXTENSION). TimescaleDB tuning guide recommends it for every production instance. Free win. | XS | **done (2026-05-26)** | Audit AP-5. Migration: `V1.18.1__add_pg_stat_statements.sql`. compose updated: `infrastructure/docker-compose.yml` + `infrastructure-local/docker-compose.yml`. Requires Postgres restart to activate. |
| TS-AUDIT-2026-05-24-006 | **MAJOR тАФ no continuous aggregates for chart-view bucketed reads.** `TimeseriesContainerChartViewService` runs `time_bucket()` / `time_bucket_gapfill()` against the raw hypertable on every render. Invisible on demo data (0.4ms reads) but compounds at MFFD-scale (multi-million-row series ├Ч hundreds-of-buckets ├Ч multiple channels per chart). Ship one CA per canonical bucket (1m, 5m, 1h, 1d) `WITH (materialized_only = false)` so newer data falls through to raw rows; wire Chart View service to pick the matching bucket. | M | queued | Audit AP-6. References TimescaleDB CA docs. |
| TS-AUDIT-2026-05-24-007 | **MAJOR (or deliberate) тАФ no data retention policy on `timeseries_data_points`.** Only `Job History Log Retention Policy` exists; data points grow forever. Memory (`project_storage_management.md`, `feedback_referenced_data_infinite_retention.md`) implies "referenced=infinite-grace, orphans=SM1a retention", which means TS should still have an SM1a-driven sweep at the container level тАФ currently nothing fires. Either document the "no retention by design" call in `aidocs/data/00-model-inventory.md` or add a generous `add_retention_policy('timeseries_data_points', INTERVAL '10 years')` safety net. Aligns with SM1a. | S (decision) + S (impl if chosen) | queued | Audit AP-7. Cross-references SM1a. |
| TS-AUDIT-2026-05-24-008 | **MAJOR (operational) тАФ backfill creates uncompressed chunks the policy won't sweep for тЙд24h.** Example from today: chunk 51 (Jan 2023 data) created at 12:26, compression job last ran 11:56, next run tomorrow 11:57. 1 GB uncompressed chunk sits for 23h+. MFFD ingest currently creates these at multiple-per-hour cadence тЖТ temporary disk inflation 5-10├Ч. Add `TimeseriesDataPointRepository.compressBackfilledChunks()` that compresses any chunk older than 8 days not already compressed; call from importer post-import phase + as a fortnightly maintenance job. | S | **done (2026-05-27)** | Audit AP-8. Shipped: `TimeseriesDataPointRepository.compressBackfilledChunks()` (entity-manager native queries; integer-ns cutoff); `TimeseriesBackfillCompressionJob` (`@Scheduled(every="{shepard.timeseries.compression-backfill.interval}")`, default P14D); post-import hook in `ImportJobsV2Rest` step 9a (best-effort, after lock release); `application.properties` key `shepard.timeseries.compression-backfill.interval=P14D`; 4 unit tests in `TimeseriesDataPointRepositoryBackfillCompressionTest`. |
| TS-AUDIT-2026-05-24-009 | **MAJOR (already-designed) тАФ 5-tuple lookup planning cost.** Measured: 1.65ms planning vs 0.095ms execution. Per-channel lookups in the hot path pay 17├Ч the actual work in parse + plan. Fix is known: TS-ID migration per `aidocs/platform/87` (`shepard_id` UUID single-column lookup, V1.11 substrate already in place). This row is a cross-reference + audit confirmation that the design's load-shape evidence is real. | (sized in aidocs/87) | **shipped (2026-05-29, TS-IDc PR-3b `9b88c1d66`)** | Audit AP-9. Cross-ref `aidocs/platform/87 ┬з3 TS-IDc`. Live-window endpoint now accepts `?shepardId=<uuid>`; the path-param channels endpoint (PR-2) already did. Plan-time evidence on MFFD container 1772 (113 channels): shepardId path = 4.36 ms plan + 0.17 ms exec via `idx_timeseries_shepard_id` (UNIQUE B-tree index-only scan); legacy 5-tuple = 2.18 ms plan + 0.07 ms exec via seq scan on `channel_metadata` (small table). shepardId wins on cost-growth shape (constant vs. O(channels-per-container)); both sub-ms at current container size. Frontend wired: `useFetchChannelPreview` accepts `channelShepardId` and prefers the v2 path-param endpoint. |
| TS-AUDIT-2026-05-24-010 | **MINOR (observe, do not fix) тАФ three indexes per chunk with partly overlapping shapes.** UNIQUE `(timeseries_id, time)` ASC + `(timeseries_id, time DESC)` + `(time DESC)`. The DESC variant was added deliberately by V1.8 with documented rationale + the empirical scan counts justify it (14K-44K scans/chunk for the DESC vs 21M for the UNIQUE). If write-amp becomes a concern at MFFD-scale, the DESC variant is the first drop candidate тАФ but only after measuring with pg_stat_statements (TS-AUDIT-005). | (observe) | parked | Audit AP-10. Not a fix; a calibration note for future perf work. |
| TS-AUDIT-2026-05-24-011 | **MINOR тАФ unbounded INSERT batch parameter count vs Postgres wire-protocol limit.** `INSERT_BATCH_SIZE=20000` ├Ч ~2 params/row тЙИ 20 002 placeholders/query (1 fixed `:timeseriesid` + 2 per row); Postgres `Bind` message uses `int16` for parameter count (max 32 767). Today: under the limit. Risk: any tweak that doubles the batch size hits the wall. Add `assert (effectiveParameterCount < 32767)` guard at batch construction; or (better) the COPY migration in -002 makes this irrelevant. | XS | done (2026-05-27) | Shipped: static initializer guard in `TimeseriesDataPointRepository` using `PARAMS_PER_ROW_LOWER_BOUND=1`, `FIXED_PARAMS_PER_BATCH=2`; throws `IllegalStateException` at class load if estimated count >= 32 767. Tests in `TimeseriesDataPointRepositoryBatchGuardTest`. Note: actual per-row count is 2 (`:time{i}` + `:value{i}`); conservative lower bound keeps guard below current safe operating point while catching any future batch-size hike. |
| TS-AUDIT-2026-05-24-012 | **MINOR (research-data concern) тАФ no row-level provenance / write origin on hypertable rows.** Every other entity in shepard carries `:Activity`-shaped provenance per the f(ai)┬▓r differentiator (`project_fair2r_integration.md`); TS data points do not. Adding per-row `inserted_at` / `inserted_by` would negate the compression ratio. **Cheaper shape**: add `source_run_id BIGINT` (NULL default) FKing the existing `importer_run` table. Backfilled rows carry the run id; live MQTT writes stay NULL (observable via collector). Storage cost ~zero (single NULL bitmap bit when unused). | S | queued | Audit AP-12. Architectural tension with compression; only worth doing once research-data audit pressure asks for it. |

## NEO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-* тАФ Neo4j + n10s substrate audit (findings)

Source: `aidocs/agent-findings/neo4j-n10s-design-audit-2026-05-24.md` (sibling
of the TimescaleDB / file-storage / Mongo / Postgres / Docker stack audits).
3 CRITICAL + 6 MAJOR + 4 MINOR antipatterns; 3 best-practice gaps. Read the
findings doc first тАФ every row below carries `EVIDENCE: ` Cypher and a
`RECOMMENDATION` referencing primary docs.

| ID | Item | effort | status | notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| NEO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-001 | **CRITICAL тАФ `:Activity` nodes are provenance write-only, not graph-queryable.** 284,530 Activity nodes exist with **ZERO incoming or outgoing edges**. `Activity.java:21-23` documents `(:User)-[:WAS_ASSOCIATED_WITH]->(:Activity)` + `:USED` / `:GENERATED` edges as "not yet wired in this slice" тАФ they were never wired. Only 0.05 % (144 of 284,535) Activity rows carry a `targetAppId` property; no index on it. Result: "what activities touched DataObject X" needs a 569,069-dbHit full-label scan. The f(ai)┬▓r promise of every-interaction-observable is not actually observable from the graph today. **Fix:** wire the three PROV-O edges in `ProvenanceCaptureFilter` write path + backfill migration on 284k existing rows (parse `Activity.path` via `TargetEntityResolver`, read `Activity.agentUsername`). Sequence **after** `PROV-RESOLVER-PATHWALK` so the resolver is the single shared source. Citation: W3C PROV-O `wasAssociatedWith` https://www.w3.org/TR/prov-o/#wasAssociatedWith. | M | **done** | Audit NEO-001. `ActivityDAO.wireEdges()` + `ProvenanceService.record()` post-save call + `V77__backfill_activity_prov_edges.cypher` + `V77_R` rollback. Javadoc direction fixed (OUTGOING from Activity). 5 new tests in `ProvenanceServiceTest`. |
| NEO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-002 | **CRITICAL тАФ `:ShepardFile.providerId` populated on 0.6 % of rows** (11,834 NULL / 71 gridfs / 33 s3 of 11,902 total). V34 backfill missed the legacy population; every reader must keep the `NULL тЖТ gridfs` fallback baked in. File-storage routing audit (sibling) lands on the same gap from the read side. **Fix:** one-shot Cypher backfill `MATCH (sf:ShepardFile) WHERE sf.providerId IS NULL SET sf.providerId = 'gridfs'` + write-path `Objects.requireNonNull` guard + reader-side NULL-coalesce kept in place. | XS | **done** | Audit NEO-002. `V79__backfill_shepardfile_providerid.cypher` + `V79_R__` rollback. `Objects.requireNonNull` guard in `FileContainerService.createFile()` + `commitUpload()`. `effectiveProviderId()` NULL-coalesce retained as belt-and-braces. 2 new tests in `FileContainerServiceTest` (`getFile_nullProviderIdRowFallsBackToGridfs`, `getFile_blankProviderIdRowFallsBackToGridfs`). Note: V79 is idempotent тАФ the 2026-05-24 out-of-band Cypher already applied; V79 is the formal migration carrier for upstream-fork upgrades. See `aidocs/34` NEO-002-BACKFILL + NEO-002-V79 rows. |
| NEO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-003 | **CRITICAL тАФ all 596 `:Timeseries.appId` rows are NULL** despite the `appId_unique_Timeseries` constraint existing тАФ uniqueness constraints permit NULL, so it's satisfied but useless. The schema layer is already provisioned (constraint + range index in place); only the data layer is empty. **Fix:** the L2c-shaped TS-appId migration in `aidocs/platform/87-timeseries-appid-migration.md` тАФ mint UUID-v7 appIds for every existing Timeseries node, populate, then deprecate the 5-tuple as identity. Per `feedback_appid_to_shepardid.md` the field gets renamed to `shepardId` in the same pass. Audit observation: this migration is **closer to ready than the design doc implies** because the constraint + index already exist. | M | **done** | Audit NEO-003. `V82__mint_timeseries_appids.cypher` (batched `randomUUID()` backfill, 500-row transactions) + `V82_R__mint_timeseries_appids.cypher` rollback. UUID-v4 for backfill (not v7 тАФ sort-by-time semantics irrelevant for pre-existing rows). This is the DATA-layer fix only; the full 5-tupleтЖТshepardId wire migration (L2c TS-ID PRs) remains in-flight per aidocs/44. Integration test (Testcontainer pre/post `appId IS NULL` count assertion) tracked as follow-up. See `aidocs/34` NEO-AUDIT-003 row. |
| NEO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-004 | **MAJOR тАФ operator-`User` is a confirmed supernode (33,368 incoming edges).** The 2026-05-23 antipattern audit suspected this at MFFD scale and flagged it as "inconclusive"; MFFD ingest landed тЖТ confirmed. PROFILE of a `created_by` traversal through the operator User node takes 66,794 dbHits to walk 17,086 DataObjects. NEO-001 will worsen this once Activity edges land. **Fix (don't dump the supernode тАФ it's structural):** add a time-bucketed Agent index `(:User)-[:created_in_month {ym:"202605"}]->(:DataObject)` written by the same hook that creates `created_by`. The MATCH plan becomes a label-scan on the `:created_in_month` rel with a `ym` predicate тАФ typically 100-1000x reduction. Citation: Neo4j supernode KB https://neo4j.com/developer/kb/understanding-the-design-of-supernodes/. | S | **done** | Shipped: `DataObjectDAO.writeCreatedInMonth()` (best-effort post-persist Cypher MERGE call with `ym = String.format("%1$tY%1$tm", createdAt)`); called from `DataObjectService.createDataObject()` after the second two-phase persist. `V80__add_created_in_month_index.cypher` creates range index `created_in_month_ym_idx` + backfills 33k+ existing DataObjects via `CALL { } IN TRANSACTIONS OF 1000 ROWS`. Rollback at `V80_R__add_created_in_month_index.cypher`. 9 unit tests in `DataObjectCreatedInMonthTest` (ym format boundaries + skip-guard cases + Cypher param assertion). See `aidocs/34` NEO-AUDIT-004 row. |
| NEO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-005 | **MAJOR тАФ EAV-on-graph: 90+ distinct `attributes||*` keys on `:DataObject`.** MFFD real-data ingest flooded the schema with single-use attribute keys (`attributes||hypothesis` ├Ч 1, `attributes||defect_area_cm2` ├Ч 1, тАж). The Neo4j-OGM `@Properties` flatten on `AbstractDataObject.attributes:Map<String,String>` creates one Neo4j property per map key on every node тАФ the graph DB analogue of EAV. Quantifies ┬з1.1.A of the 2026-05-23 archived audit on real ingested data. **Specific harms post-MFFD:** `attributes||v16_pass1` ├Ч 8,507 is a transient ingest marker; `attributes||source_*` keys are import provenance (should be Activity properties, not DataObject); `attributes||license` ├Ч 3 coexists with the typed `license` field ├Ч 4 (LIC1 just shipped) тАФ same semantic carried by two different fields. **Fix:** the SHACL-as-source-of-truth direction (`feedback_shacl_single_source_of_truth.md`) is the structural fix. Tactical: promote import provenance from `:DataObject.attributes||` to the `:Activity` node that recorded the import (pairs naturally with NEO-001). Drop `attributes||license` once LIC1 readers settle. | M | queued | Audit NEO-005. Pairs with NEO-001 + SHACL-as-SoT direction. |
| NEO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-006 | **MAJOR тАФ mixed-case relationship-type convention.** Three shepard-side rels use UPPERCASE literals instead of the lowercase `Constants.*` convention: `ENTRY_OF` (`SnapshotEntry.java:59`), `SNAPSHOT_OF` (`Snapshot.java:82`), `OWNS_CREDENTIAL` (`User.java:79`). (All other UPPERCASE rels тАФ `TYPE/SUBJECT/OBJECT/RELATED/BROADER/NARROWER/SUBCLASSOF/MIGRATED_TO/тАж` тАФ are n10s/RDF-owned, upstream-mandated and stay uppercase.) Mixed-case convention drift is a long-tail bug source: `:has_successor` vs `:HAS_SUCCESSOR` would be silently distinct labels. **Fix:** rename to `entry_of`, `snapshot_of`, `owns_credential` in a Cypher migration (depends on APOC тАФ see NEO-013 тАФ or use the manual `MATCH-CREATE-DELETE` fallback). Coordinate with the appIdтЖТshepardId entity rename pass per `feedback_appid_to_shepardid.md`. | S | queued | Audit NEO-006. APOC dependency тАФ schedule after NEO-013. |
| NEO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-007 | **MAJOR тАФ duplicate Collection names with shared semantic (MFFD-Dropbox ├Ч 4).** Two of the four MFFD-Dropbox collections are supernodes themselves (8538 + 8518 edges). Per memory (`project_mffd_import_workflow.md`) this is intentional iterative ingest, NOT a bug тАФ but operator-facing impact is real: `GET /v2/collections?name=MFFD-Dropbox` returns four hits and the UI can't tell which is which. **Fix:** no schema change. Add `:Collection.importedFrom: text` distinguishing the four (e.g., `tapelaying`, `bridgewelding`, `v15-redrive-1`, `v15-redrive-2`); surface on the collection list UI as a sub-label. Closes the human-identity ambiguity without merging graph nodes. | S | **done** | Shipped: `importedFrom` nullable field on `Collection.java` entity + `CollectionIO` (with `@JsonInclude(NON_NULL)` for v1 byte-fidelity) + backend-client TypeScript interface (src + dist/CJS + dist/ESM) + muted sub-label chip in `CollectionList.vue` + 7 Vitest unit tests (`collectionListImportedFrom.test.ts`). No Neo4j migration needed тАФ additive nullable property. See `aidocs/34` NEO-AUDIT-007 row. |
| NEO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-008 | **MAJOR тАФ Cartesian OPTIONAL MATCH on `DataObjectDAO.java:480-506` + `CollectionDAO.java:120-121`.** Single super-node `:DataObject` Tapelaying-2026-05-23 carries 1470 `has_reference` edges; PROFILE shows 8840 dbHits for an empty result because the planner walks all 1470 refs in each leg. Sibling `OPTIONAL MATCH` legs against TimeseriesReference / FileBundleReference / StructuredDataReference multiply leg cardinalities. Quantifies ┬з1.1.E of the 2026-05-23 archived audit on the largest MFFD DO. **Fix:** split sibling legs into `CALL { ... }` subqueries (Neo4j 4.4+) per the official cypher anti-patterns guide https://neo4j.com/developer-blog/cypher-anti-patterns-merge/. Expected reduction: 5-10x dbHits. | S | **done** | Shipped: `CALL {}` subquery rewrite in `DataObjectDAO.findContainersByDataObjectAppId` (true Cartesian) + `CollectionDAO.deleteCollectionByShepardId` (chained-OPTIONAL-MATCH cascade). `findRefCountsByAppIds` verified NOT Cartesian (already uses `WITH тАж count(DISTINCT)` chain) тАФ left unchanged. Caller `DataObjectV2Rest.buildContainersFromCypher` updated for new single-row ├Ч 3-list return shape. 2 new DAO tests added. |
| NEO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-009 | **MAJOR тАФ `idx_Subscription_requestMethod` is the #3 hottest index in the system (298,700 reads) against zero rows.** Every authenticated write hits `SubscriptionService.findMatchingSubscriptions`, which probes the registry for matching watchers; the registry has zero `:Subscription` nodes so every probe is a wasted index walk. Also signals a feature-adoption gap тАФ Subscription is shipped but unused; might indicate a creation bug. **Fix (two layers):** (a) short-circuit `findMatchingSubscriptions` with a cached `count(:Subscription) == 0` check (refreshed on subscription create/delete); when zero, skip the index lookup entirely. (b) file a separate adoption-audit task for the subscription feature. | XS + S | **done** | `SubscriptionExistenceCache` (@ApplicationScoped TTL-60s) + short-circuit in `SubscriptionService.getMatchingSubscriptions`; invalidated on create/delete. `SubscriptionShortCircuitTest.java` (6 cases). |
| NEO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-010 | **MAJOR тАФ duplicate user emails: 2├Ч `alice@demo.shepard.local`, 2├Ч `admin@demo.shepard.local`.** `unique_username_User` covers UUID usernames; no email uniqueness. Today dev-only, but a routine OIDC-as-email failure mode in production (shared department mailbox; two employees sharing an email). **Fix:** add `CREATE CONSTRAINT user_email_unique IF NOT EXISTS FOR (u:User) REQUIRE u.email IS UNIQUE` + one-shot reconciliation migration to merge the two `admin@`/`alice@` accounts. Graph-edge-relabel well-known shape; coordinate with the auth team. | S | **done** | `V81__user_email_unique_constraint.cypher` + `V81_R__` rollback. Reconciliation uses `apoc.refactor.mergeNodes` (transfers ALL edges both-direction; canonical selected by admin-username тЖТ degree тЖТ lex). `UserDAO.findByEmail(String): Optional<User>` + `countDuplicateEmails()` added. Startup WARN in `ShepardMain` if duplicates survive migration. 7 unit tests in `UserDAOFindByEmailTest`. See `aidocs/34` NEO-AUDIT-010 row. Future prevention is OIDC-side responsibility тАФ constraint will throw on any subsequent duplicate-insert attempt, surfacing the failure loudly. |
| NEO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-011 | **MINOR тАФ 47 indexes with zero reads (dead-index maintenance cost on every write).** Notable: `idx_Timeseries_attr_field`, `_location`, `_symbolic_name` TEXT indexes (V8) are unused тАФ `device` + `measurement` are queried, the other three never (`lastRead=NULL`). 23 zero-read `appId_unique_*` constraints for entity types not in production use. Write-amplification at MFFD ingest: 33k writes ├Ч 47 indexes ├Ч 1ms тЙИ 25 minutes of pure index-update CPU per ingest. **Fix:** drop the three unused Timeseries TEXT indexes + the Watch family if Watch is deprecated. **Don't** blanket-drop unique constraints тАФ load-bearing for entity types even if not currently queried. | S | **done** | Shipped: `V77__drop_dead_timeseries_text_indexes.cypher`; rollback at `V77_R__restore_timeseries_text_indexes.cypher`; 3 TEXT indexes dropped (`idx_Timeseries_attr_field`, `idx_Timeseries_attr_location`, `idx_Timeseries_attr_symbolic_name`). UNIQUE constraints NOT touched. |
| NEO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-012 | **MINOR тАФ vestigial `unique_id_*` constraints on entities migrated to `appId`.** 100 % of DataObject / Collection / StructuredDataContainer rows have `id IS NULL` because the system migrated to `appId` as canonical identity; the 14 V1-era `unique_id_*` constraints still exist and protect a property that's never populated. No correctness risk (unique-on-NULL satisfied) тАФ just contributor confusion. **Fix:** schedule a deprecation pass after L2e (the planned v1-numeric-id sunset, `aidocs/platform/25 ┬зL2e`). Drop the 14 constraints once L2e ships and no readers depend on the property. | XS | queued | Audit NEO-012. Wait for L2e. |
| NEO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-013 | **MINOR тАФ APOC absent on this instance despite security allowlist suggesting it should be present.** Container env: `NEO4J_PLUGINS=["n10s"]` but `NEO4J_dbms_security_procedures_allowlist=apoc.*,n10s.*` + `unrestricted=apoc.*,n10s.*`. The allowlist is correct; only the plugins list missed APOC. APOC core has been bundled with Neo4j 5.x since 5.7 (https://neo4j.com/labs/apoc/5/installation/) тАФ no separate jar download needed. Blocks the rel-type rename in NEO-006 from using `apoc.refactor.setType`. **Fix:** one-line compose edit `NEO4J_PLUGINS=["apoc","n10s"]` + container restart. | XS | **done** | Shipped: added `apoc` to `NEO4J_PLUGINS` in `infrastructure/docker-compose.yml`. Unblocks NEO-006 + any migration using `apoc.periodic.iterate`. Container restart required to activate (not done here тАФ operator-triggered). |
| NEO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-014 | **MINOR тАФ migration chain applied in non-monotonic order (V63 before V61).** Same incident as OPS-MIGRATION-HEALTHCHECK (V61 lagged main by two days). Correctness OK тАФ the `Migrations` library applies forward-only on each restart тАФ but a documentation foot-gun: readers of `MATCH (m) ORDER BY m.version DESC` see "63 happened 2026-05-22T15:38, 61 happened 2026-05-22T15:39+1day" and reasonably ask "was the order reversed?". **Fix:** add a comment to the existing OPS-MIGRATION-HEALTHCHECK runbook (`docs/admin/runbooks/migration-chain-integrity.md`) explaining the chain may carry out-of-order `installedOn` timestamps if a forward-only splice runs late, and that's WAI. | XS | **done** | Runbook `docs/admin/runbooks/migration-chain-integrity.md` ┬з"A note on out-of-order `installedOn` timestamps" added. Doc-only; no code change. |
| NEO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-015 | **MINOR тАФ `:Activity.actionKind` is stringly-typed (3 distinct values, no enforcement).** Activity.java:50-51 documents an enum (`CREATE/READ/UPDATE/DELETE/EXECUTE`); stored as free-text. Today clean (`CREATE: 253520, UPDATE: 18050, DELETE: 12917`); single typo in capture filter forks the value-space and breaks downstream filters silently. Same shape as `:DataObject.status`, `:ImportPlan.status` from the 2026-05-23 audit. **Fix:** Neo4j 5 EE property-existence + value constraints (`REQUIRE n.actionKind IS IN [...]`) but this instance runs Community Edition (`NEO4J_EDITION=community`). Fallback: validation in `ProvenanceCaptureFilter` + periodic sweep alarm that fires if any `:Activity.actionKind` matches none of the canonical values. Lower-priority than NEO-001 тАФ wire the edges first. | S | **done** | `ActivityActionKind` enum + `ALL_KNOWN_VALUES` set (includes TPL9 `AI_ACTION`); `ProvenanceService.record()` calls `ActivityActionKind.validate()` before DAO write; `ActivityActionKindAlarm` `@ApplicationScoped` `@PostConstruct` queries for rogue values and WARNs; 8 unit tests in `ActivityActionKindTest` + 3 new assertions in `ProvenanceServiceTest`. No Neo4j migration needed (Community Edition; app-layer is the constraint mechanism). |
| NEO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-016 | **MINOR (best-practice gap) тАФ soft-delete heavy on `:DataObject` (50 %) + `:BasicReference` (36 %) without TTL.** Half of all DataObjects soft-deleted; index walks always touch both populations. Coupled with NEO-004's supernode, "list DataObjects this user created (not deleted)" becomes O(33k ├Ч 2). **Fix:** SM1a (already in backlog, queued) тАФ retention sweep hard-deletes soft-deleted DataObjects past a TTL. Pair naturally with this finding; just nudge SM1a priority up. | тАФ | depends-on-SM1a | Audit NEO-016. No new effort тАФ pre-existing backlog row. |
| NEO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-017 | **MINOR (best-practice gap) тАФ property keys with single-row usage (sparse property store).** 30+ `attributes||*` keys appear on 1-3 DataObjects each. Neo4j's property store is record-oriented (not column-oriented) тАФ a node with 30 properties takes 30 record reads even if your query reads one. Compounds NEO-005. **Fix:** same as NEO-005 тАФ promote import-provenance attributes to Activity edges. Routine domain attributes stay pending SHACL-as-SoT. | тАФ | depends-on-NEO-005 | Audit NEO-017. No standalone work. |
| NEO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-018 | **MINOR (best-practice gap) тАФ 174,035 bare `:Resource` nodes (n10s SKOS import bloat).** NASA thesaurus + synaptica notes dominate (`BROADER:17012, NARROWER:17012, RELATED:117340`). Correct per n10s semantics (every RDF subject тЖТ `:Resource`) but ~2.4├Ч shepard's domain node count. `n10s_unique_uri` is the #1 hottest index (26M reads) on these nodes; page cache stays warm with RDF infrastructure, possibly at the expense of hot DataObject reads. **Fix:** consider importing heavy SKOS thesauri with `n10s.skos.import.fetch` + `handleMultival="ARRAY"` + label-density reduction (omit `skos:related` if not used). Or sidecar to a separate substrate (Community single-DB limitation argues against). Lower priority тАФ copes today. | M | queued | Audit NEO-018. Pairs with `aidocs/semantics/14` semantic-improvements design. |

## Synthesis Pass-1 cheap-wins тАФ shipped 2026-05-24

Tracking the synthesis report's ┬з6 Pass-1 trio + the newly proposed
CADDY row. Bundled here because they were chosen as the MFFD-orthogonal
work pack while ingest still runs (none touch the destination data).

| ID | Item | effort | status | notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| NEO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-002-SHIPPED | **Cypher backfill `MATCH (sf:ShepardFile) WHERE sf.providerId IS NULL SET sf.providerId = 'gridfs'`.** Closed the substrate side of NEO-002. Pre-state: 12 253 NULL + 71 gridfs + 33 s3. Post-state: 12 327 gridfs + 33 s3 + 0 NULL (12 256 rows updated; +3 drift from ingest during the backfill itself). Reader-side NULL-coalesce stays in place until the write-path `@Required` annotation lands as a follow-up; backfill remains idempotent so it can be re-run if MFFD ingest creates a few more NULL rows before that PR. **Did not** touch any MFFD destination data тАФ `:ShepardFile` is instance-wide. | XS | тЬЕ shipped 2026-05-24 | Commit landing this row. Follow-up: write-path `@Required` + reader NULL-coalesce drop, sequenced after MFFD ingest drains. |
| CADDY-API-PASSTHROUGH-2026-05-24 | **Caddy `/v2/*` + `/shepard/api/*` + `/shepard/doc/*` bypass routes to backend:8080.** Closes Digital Native persona ┬з0: programmatic callers arriving at `https://shepard.nuclide.systems/` with `X-API-KEY` / `Bearer` used to land at the Nuxt frontend (302тЖТNextAuth signin). Verified end-to-end via Zoraxy: `https://shepard.nuclide.systems/v2/collections` now returns HTTP/2 401 with `content-type: application/json` (backend challenge) instead of 302тЖТsignin; `https://shepard.nuclide.systems/shepard/doc/openapi/v2.json` serves the spec. The Nuxt frontend uses `NUXT_PUBLIC_BACKEND_API_URL=https://shepard-api.nuclide.systems/shepard/api` for its own calls so no SSR breakage; only `/api/auth/*` lives same-origin in Nuxt and is preserved. New helper doc `docs/help/api-access.md` covers API-key minting, OpenAPI client generation, MCP from Claude, common failure modes. **Caddy bind-mount gotcha:** Caddy's `caddy reload` did NOT pick up the new Caddyfile because Write tool's atomic rename changed the inode and single-file bind mounts in Docker track the inode at container-start time. Fix: `docker compose restart caddy` (brief gateway downtime, ~3s). Memory entry filed. | S | тЬЕ shipped 2026-05-24 | Commit landing this row. New row тАФ not present in any source audit (synthesis ┬з3-T3 + ┬з5#6 flagged "newly proposed"). |
| NEO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-013-DEFERRED | **APOC plugin install (`NEO4J_PLUGINS=["apoc","n10s"]` + container restart).** Synthesis ┬з6 Pass-1 candidate тАФ was gated on MFFD ingest pause. Compose change landed in NEO-AUDIT-2026-05-24-013 (see above). Container restart still needed to activate APOC; operator-triggered. | XS | тЬЕ compose done тАФ restart pending | Config shipped. Activate by restarting the `neo4j` container (`docker compose restart neo4j` from `infrastructure/`). |
| TS-AUDIT-2026-05-24-005-DEFERRED | **`pg_stat_statements` extension + Flyway V1.12 migration.** Synthesis ┬з6 Pass-1 candidate тАФ moved here because the `shared_preload_libraries` change requires Postgres restart, which would interrupt MFFD TS writes. Promote to тЬЕ when ingest drains. | XS | **done (2026-05-26)** | Shipped as TS-AUDIT-2026-05-24-005; see that row for details. |
| LIM-DOCKER-BIND-MOUNT-INODE | **Single-file Docker bind mounts track inode-at-mount-time, not path-at-runtime.** Surfaced 2026-05-24 by CADDY-API-PASSTHROUGH: editing the host file via Claude's Write tool (atomic temp-file + rename) changes the inode, so the container view goes stale and Caddy reloads see the old file. The fix is `docker compose restart <service>` (or use `docker cp` to overwrite in-place). Affected files in this repo: `infrastructure/proxy/Caddyfile`, `infrastructure/.env`. **Operator runbook follow-up:** add a one-page note to `docs/admin/runbooks/` and a guard rail in the OPS hygiene set (smoke probe should detect "container file does not match host file"). | XS | **done (2026-05-27)** | Runbook at `docs/admin/runbooks/docker-bind-mount-inode-drift.md`; linked from runbooks README. Smoke-probe guard rail deferred (OPS hygiene follow-up still open). Filed by CADDY-API-PASSTHROUGH-2026-05-24. |

## AI-V6-* тАФ `shepard-plugin-ai` v6 capability surface (local-first by default)

SSOT: [`aidocs/integrations/97-shepard-plugin-ai-design.md`](integrations/97-shepard-plugin-ai-design.md). ## OGM-HYDRATE-2026-05-24-* тАФ v2 DAO hydration sweep (4 rows from audit)

SSOT: [`aidocs/agent-findings/ogm-hydration-audit-2026-05-24.md`](agent-findings/ogm-hydration-audit-2026-05-24.md). Sweep ran 2026-05-24; **zero CRIT v2 findings** (v2 is accidentally inoculated тАФ flat property bags with appId references, no `@Relationship` fields). One v1 DEFERRED + one v2 DEFERRED + two structural follow-ups.

| ID | Item | Size | Status | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| OGM-HYDRATE-2026-05-24-001 | **OGM-HYDRATE-V1-001** тАФ `backend/.../context/labJournal/daos/LabJournalEntryRevisionDAO.java:32-41`. `LabJournalEntryRevision` carries `@Relationship(direction=INCOMING) LabJournalEntry`. DAO `RETURN DISTINCT revision` will NPE the moment a `LabJournalEntryRevisionIO` ships that reads `revision.getLabJournalEntry().getShepardId()`. Same defect class as the just-shipped BUG-LJ-V1-COLL-ID fix. **Trigger condition**: any new IO serialisation referencing the entry's back-reference. Fix shape: `CypherQueryHelper.getReturnPart(LabJournalEntryRevision.class)` projection. | XS | deferred | Audit ┬з4 row 1. |
| OGM-HYDRATE-2026-05-24-002 | **OGM-HYDRATE-002** тАФ `backend/.../timeseries/annotation/daos/TimeseriesAnnotationDAO.java`. Currently SAFE (uses `getReturnPart`) тАФ flag against future "simplify the Cypher" refactor pressure that might inline the projection. Pin with a unit-test assertion + comment so the safety isn't accidentally removed. | XS | deferred | Audit ┬з4 row 2. Tripwire, not a bug. |
| OGM-HYDRATE-2026-05-24-003 | **STRUCTURAL тАФ custom SpotBugs/AST rule.** Fail the build on any Cypher `RETURN <leaf-only>` against a `@NodeEntity` that has at least one `@Relationship` field. Prevents the entire BUG-LJ-V1 defect class at PR time rather than chasing individual instances. Use SpotBugs detector + a regex-based `@NodeEntity`/`@Relationship` annotation scanner; emit High-confidence finding pointing at the offending Cypher string. | M | queued | Audit ┬з6 + ┬з7. Cheapest long-term insurance against this defect class. |
| OGM-HYDRATE-2026-05-24-004 | **Sibling sweep тАФ service-layer composite-call hydration.** If a v2 service stitches two DAO returns and assumes `entityA.getEntityB()` is populated by the first call, the same NPE can fire even when both DAOs are individually correct. Out of scope for the DAO sweep; needs a separate audit pass over `de.dlr.shepard.v2.**.services.*`. Quick grep: any service method that calls one repository, then immediately walks `.getX().getY()` where Y wasn't projected. | S (audit only) | **done (2026-05-27)** | Findings: [`aidocs/agent-findings/ogm-hydration-service-layer-2026-05-27.md`](agent-findings/ogm-hydration-service-layer-2026-05-27.md). One MAJOR found + fixed: `DataObjectDAO.findByAppId` (bare `RETURN d`) + `DataObjectService.resolveTypedPredecessors:657` (.getCollection() NPE on cache miss). Fix: added `session.load(..., DEPTH_ENTITY)` tail-call to `findByAppId`. Remaining service paths safe: `findByNeo4jId` тЖТ `session.load(depth=1)` hydrates both directions; `findByShepardId` тЖТ `EVERYTHING` neighborhood. |

## UX-2026-05-24-* тАФ collections + containers triage (UX scrutinizer findings)

SSOT: [`aidocs/agent-findings/ux-survey-collections-containers-2026-05-24.md`](agent-findings/ux-survey-collections-containers-2026-05-24.md). 4515-word audit + 24 Playwright screenshots + e2e reproducer spec. Three CRITICAL / multiple MAJOR findings at MFFD-scale (8514 DOs).

| ID | Item | Size | Status | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| UX-DOPANEL-STATUS-SERVER | **CRITICAL тАФ push status filter to backend.** `CollectionDataObjectsPanel.vue:196-199` chip filter is applied client-side over only the 25 visible rows; clicking 'READY' on MFFD-Dropbox p.1 silently drops 800+ READY rows from remaining pages. Add a `status` query param to the list endpoint + apply server-side; remove the client-side filter. | M | **done (2026-05-26)** | Audit Top 3 #1. Top urgency at MFFD scale. |
| UX-DOPANEL-TOTAL-COUNT | **MAJOR тАФ add `Content-Range` header + "X-Y of N" + jump-to-page.** Today the DO panel paginates without showing total count or absolute position; researchers can't tell if they're on page 1 of 5 or page 1 of 343. Backend returns `Content-Range` (or `X-Total-Count`); frontend renders "Showing 1-25 of 8514" + page-input jump. | M | **done (2026-05-26)** | Audit #2. |
| UX-ERR-STATE-COLLECTION-MISSING | **CRITICAL тАФ empty-state branch for missing/deleted collection IDs.** `pages/collections/[collectionId]/index.vue:467` is `<CenteredLoadingSpinner v-else />` with no error branch тАФ a bogus or soft-deleted appId hangs forever with 19 console errors per attempt. Add a `<NotFoundPanel />` branch for 404s on the collection fetch; same pattern for spatial container 404 (7 errors). | S | **done (2026-05-26)** | `NotFoundPanel.vue` created; `isError` ref added to `useFetchCollection`; three-branch data/error/loading pattern applied to collection detail + spatialdata container pages. | UX-PAGE-SHELL-RESPONSIVE-WIDTH | **MAJOR тАФ single `<PageShell>` replacing 6 hard-clamp instances.** Six pages hard-clamp at 1200-1400px (CollectionListPage.vue:21, [collectionId]/index.vue:139, all four container detail pages). At 4K viewport this wastes 70%+ horizontal real estate and forces vertical scroll. ## MFFD-INGEST-* тАФ MFFD dump ingest prerequisites (2026-05-26)

Design ref: [`aidocs/data/108-mffd-dump-ingestion-plan.md`](data/108-mffd-dump-ingestion-plan.md). Five gaps must close before full MFFD import can proceed. Import is **deferred** until the functional prerequisites below are resolved. A metadata-only Phase 0 (CameraConfig INI + ProfileSet.tif + DO hierarchy) has no blockers and can proceed at any time.

| ID | Item | Size | Status | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| MFFD-TS-01 | **TimescaleDB pre-import chunk/partition as idempotent Flyway migration.** `backend/src/main/resources/db/migration/V1.13.0__Optimize_timeseries_chunk_config.sql` тАФ sets chunk interval to 1 hour (vs default 7 days, wrong for sub-second sensor data) and adds 4 space partitions by `timeseries_id` (parallel ingestion). Both must be idempotent (`DO $$ IF NOT EXISTS ... $$`) since the hypertable may already have chunks. Without this, MFFD-scale ingest will create thousands of oversized 7-day chunks and suffer serial write contention. | S | **dispatched** | Dispatched 2026-05-26. Prerequisite for Phase 1 (FSD TS ingest). Pairs with P2b (CAgg). |
| MFFD-TS-02 | **INTEGRAL aggregation implementation.** Remove the `assertNotIntegral()` guard in `TimeseriesDataPointRepository.queryDataPoints()` and `queryAggregationFunction()` (`:462тАУ464`). Implement two paths: (a) whole-range trapezoidal integral via native SQL `LAG()` window function тАФ `SUM(0.5 ├Ч (v + v_next) ├Ч (t_next тИТ t))` тАФ returned as a single TimeseriesDataPoint; (b) time-bucketed midpoint approximation `AVG(v) ├Ч bucket_duration_ns` in `queryAggregationFunction` when a time-slice is set. Add unit tests + one integration test. Prerequisite for the welding energy budget analysis case (Case B in `aidocs/data/108`). | M | **dispatched** | Dispatched 2026-05-26. `AggregateFunction.INTEGRAL` already exists in the enum; the guard is the only blocker. |
| MFFD-IMPORT-01 | **MffdDumpSource тАФ AFP 5-level hierarchy importer.** New class `de.dlr.shepard.v2.importer.sources.MffdDumpSource` extending the v16 importer to understand the AFP Run тЖТ PlyGroup тЖТ Layup тЖТ Layer тЖТ Track directory tree. Per-track: parse CameraConfig INI for DataObject attributes (track number, ply, length, tow width, start/stop ns), route FSDSet.csv to TimeseriesContainer using `ChronoTimeInUs ├Ч 1000` as ns timestamp, route PointCloud.csv to FileReference (or SpatialContainer once SP1 lands), route ProfileSet.tif to FileContainer (Garage S3), route ProfileSet.csv (brush data) to StructuredDataContainer. Skip 0-byte OID payloads gracefully (note `payload_available: false` attribute). | L | queued | Gated on MFFD-TS-01 (chunk migration) + MFFD-TS-02 (INTEGRAL, needed for FSD ingest correctness check). SP1 (#79) gating for PointCloud тАФ fallback to FileReference acceptable for Phase 1. |
| MFFD-BATCH-01 | **Bulk DataObject creation endpoint тАФ `POST /v2/data-objects/batch`.** Accepts a JSON array of DataObject creation requests (up to 500 per call). Returns a 207 Multi-Status body with per-item status + created appId. Needed because MFFD imports 17,600+ DataObjects; at 1 DO/s with 4 workers the AFP tapelaying step takes 1тАУ2 hours тАФ a batch endpoint reduces this 10тАУ100├Ч. Include permission check (caller must have write on all parent collections) and PROV-O batch writeback. | M | queued | Independent of MFFD-TS series. High value for any large-dataset import scenario (LUMEN + future). |
| MFFD-JOIN-01 | **Design: scan-line join key across TPS stores.** The `Packet` index (0-based integer) is the shared row key across FSDSet, PointCloud, ProfileSet.tif, and BrushData for each AFP track. Today Shepard has no first-class way to express "row N in TS container A = row N in SpatialContainer B." Design options: (a) store `Packet` as an additional TS channel and expose it in the multi-channel endpoint (TS-OPT2, #226); (b) rely on absolute timestamp alignment (`ChronoTimeInUs ├Ч 1000` in FSD = wall-clock ns for TimescaleDB) and assume the spatial data is co-registered at the same ns timestamps; (c) add a `frame_index` column to SpatialContainer. Option (b) is sufficient for Phase 1 if FSD timestamps are used consistently in both stores. | S (design) | **тЬУ done (2026-05-27)** | Design note shipped as `aidocs/data/109-mffd-scan-line-join-key.md` (stage: idea). Recommends Option (b) for Phase 1 with verification step; Options (a)/(c) deferred to Phase 2. No implementation until PointCloud/spatial ingest lands. |
| MFFD-NDRIVE-01 | **N: drive mount on DLR cube for scripted ingest.** Set up persistent mount of `\\bt-au-freenas1.intra.dlr.de\share\Messdaten\` (or the NAS path confirmed by DLR infra) on the DLR cube host. Required for Phase 7 (FSD/PointCloud backfill from N: drive), MFFD-PARSER-SVDX1 (SVDX welding TS), and ┬з6.3 video ingest. User confirmed N: drive accessible from DLR systems 2026-05-26. Operations task тАФ no code changes in shepard; config-managed via cube ansible/runbook. | S (ops) | queued | Confirmed accessible (2026-05-26). Contact: DLR Augsburg infra team. Document mount path in the MFFD ingest runbook once confirmed. |
| MFFD-PARSER-01 | **`FileParserPlugin` SPI skeleton тАФ post-upload async enrichment hook.** Define `FileParserPlugin` interface, `ParseCapability` record, `ParseContext` + `ParseResult` types, `FileParserRegistry` CDI bean, `ParseJob` persisted via `JobService`. Trigger: `FileContainerService.upload()` calls `FileParserRegistry.findParser()` after OID creation; match returns async `ParseJob`. Status queryable via `GET /v2/file-containers/{fcId}/files/{oid}/parse-status`. Design doc: `aidocs/integrations/110`. | M | queued | Prerequisite for MFFD-PARSER-SA1 + MFFD-PARSER-SVDX1. Distinct from `shepard-plugin-importer` (cross-instance vs post-upload). |
| MFFD-PARSER-SA1 | **`shepard-plugin-parser-sa` тАФ Spatial Analyzer `.xit`/`.xit64` parser.** Implements `FileParserPlugin` for NRK Spatial Analyzer format. Reads binary header to detect `measurementType` (DISCRETE_POINTS vs 6D_PROBE_SCAN). Routes: discrete point groups тЖТ StructuredDataContainer rows `(pointName, x, y, z, spatialRms)`; 6D probe streams тЖТ TimeseriesContainer channels `(x, y, z, roll, pitch, yaw)` at kHz rates. Stamps DataObject attrs: `instrument.type = "Leica AT901"`, `frame_of_reference`. Design doc: `aidocs/integrations/110 ┬з4.1`. | L | queued | Gated on MFFD-PARSER-01 (SPI skeleton). Blocked until test `.xit` file procured тАФ contact DLR ZLP metrology team. |
| MFFD-PARSER-SVDX1 | **`shepard-plugin-parser-svdx` тАФ Beckhoff TwinCAT Scope `.svdx` тЖТ TimescaleDB.** Implements `FileParserPlugin` for `.svdx` / TDMS format. Wraps existing `tdms2csv.py` (in `tool_sources/`) as subprocess or ports logic to Java. Output: one TimeseriesContainer per file; channel names from SVDX header; DataObject attrs `process.type = "welding"`, `weld.seam_id` from filename. Volume: 181 SVDX files ├Ч 20 channels ├Ч ~30k points. Design doc: `aidocs/integrations/110 ┬з4.2`. | M | queued | Gated on MFFD-PARSER-01 + MFFD-NDRIVE-01 (files on N: drive). |
| MFFD-PARSER-RDK1 | **`shepard-plugin-parser-rdk` тАФ RoboDK `.rdk` station file тЖТ metadata + digital-twin registration.** MVP tier (no SDK): decompress zlib (offset 4) тЖТ scan UTF-16LE strings тЖТ extract robot names, CAD model paths, program source dir, app version. Emit as DataObject attributes + SemanticAnnotations (`ssn:System`, `chameo:hasInstrument`, `m4i:ManufacturingProcess`). Raw `.rdk` stored as FileContainer for downstream tools. Cross-link: if `*.xit` present on same DataObject, emit `prov:wasDerivedFrom` linking measured SA calibration to RDK design frames. Phase 2 (deferred): full kinematic tree extraction via RoboDK Python SDK sidecar. Design doc: `aidocs/integrations/110 ┬з4.3`. Format: `03 25 10 A5` magic, zlib at offset 4, UTF-16LE binary, "Station File 01.01". Confirmed on `MFZ.rdk` (12.1 MB, v5.5.3, AFP R10+R20 cell, DLR ZLP Augsburg). | M | queued | Gated on MFFD-PARSER-01. Test file: `examples/mffd-showcase/raw-data/mffd-data/cell/MFZ.rdk`. |
| TS-BINARY1 | **Smart binary channel coercion on CSV ingest.** During `POST /timeseriesContainers/{id}/import`, channels where measurement or field name contains a binary-indicative token (digital, binary, bool, boolean, status, flag, enable, active, switch, relay, on_off, state) OR where all non-null numeric values are exactly {0.0, 1.0} are stored as `Boolean` instead of `Double`. Coercion: 0 тЖТ `false`, non-zero тЖТ `true`. Triggered MFFD AFP digital-output channels (robot axes, clamp states) mapping to 1.0=active/0.0=inactive. Logs `[ts-import] binary channel detected тАФ coercing to Boolean: <measurement> / <field>` per channel. 8 unit tests in `CsvConverterTest`. | S | **тЬУ shipped 2026-05-26** | `CsvConverter.convertCsvToTimeseriesWithData()`. Commit `f1385c7e`. |
| MFFD-TS-MULTIREF-01 | **Multi-source TimeseriesReference тАФ allow a single reference to select channels from multiple containers.** Context: MFFD AFP Track DataObjects will have timeseries data from 3+ distinct sources (FSD/Fast Send Driver, robot joints, tape head telemetry), each in its own `TimeseriesContainer`. Current model: one `IS_IN_CONTAINER` per `TimeseriesReference` тЖТ forces multiple separate Reference nodes per DataObject. Design decision required: (a) move `IS_IN_CONTAINER` to `ReferencedTimeseriesNodeEntity` so each channel selects its own container, OR (b) add `List<TimeseriesContainer> additionalContainers` overlay. Aligns with TS-IDc appId migration тАФ once channels have a single appId, container context is implicit. Migration: Cypher to copy existing `(ref)-[:IS_IN_CONTAINER]->(c)` to each `(t)-[:IS_IN_CONTAINER]->(c)` for every channel in the ref. See `aidocs/data/108 ┬з12.7`. | M | queued | Gated on TS-IDc design decision. Short-term workaround: multiple named TimeseriesReferences per DataObject (one per source). |
| MFFD-SHARED-CONTAINER-01 | **Design + implement shared TS containers across AFP tracks.** User directive 2026-05-26: tracks with the same channel schema share one `TimeseriesContainer` (no per-track container sprawl). Model: ~6 containers total (one per source type: FSD/Fast Send Driver, robot joints, tape head, welding, etc.). **Track identity is carried by `shepardId` UUID тАФ the 5-tuple fields are NOT the identity layer.** See TS-CORE-SCHEMA-01 (below) which is the prerequisite: once the 5-tuple is dropped from the core `timeseries` table and moved to semantic annotations, each (track ├Ч channel) pair has exactly one `shepardId` UUID row with no uniqueness constraint tension. Per-track DataObjects hold a TimeseriesReference whose `shepardId` list covers that track's channels. **Gated on TS-CORE-SCHEMA-01.** Supersedes the per-track container model assumed in MFFD-IMPORT-01. | M | queued | **BLOCKS MFFD-IMPORT-01 redesign. Gated on TS-CORE-SCHEMA-01.** Scale check in flight (MFFD-SCALE-CHECK-01). |
| MFFD-SCALE-CHECK-01 | **Scale-check: can DB infra + schemas handle shared-container MFFD volume?** Dispatch analysis agent. Questions: (1) TimescaleDB: `timeseries` table тАФ 6 containers ├Ч 30 channels ├Ч 500 tracks = 90,000 channel rows, all `containerId` pointing at 6 containers тАФ does the partial index on `(containerId, measurement, field, ...)` stay efficient? (2) `timeseries_data_points`: 90K channels ├Ч 1000 samples each at 100 Hz = 90M rows per 10-second window тАФ chunk strategy sufficient? (3) Neo4j: 500 track DOs each with 6 TS references (one per source container) = 3000 TS references; acceptable? (4) `GET /v2/timeseries-containers/{id}/channels` with 30K rows per container тАФ does the listing endpoint need pagination? (5) PgBouncer pool: 90K channel import in parallel = pool pressure? | M (analysis) | queued | 2026-05-26. Drives whether MFFD-SHARED-CONTAINER-01 design is viable as-is or needs substrate changes first. |
| MFFD-CLEAN-REBUILD-01 | **MFFD import is a clean rebuild тАФ full dest reset before import.** User directive 2026-05-26: before the real MFFD TS data import, reset the dest instance (Neo4j, Postgres/TimescaleDB, Garage/S3 cleared; Keycloak users preserved; API keys re-issued post-reset). MFFD-PRUNE-1..4 superseded. | TS-CORE-SCHEMA-01 | **Move 5-tuple channel identity from `timeseries` table to `channel_metadata` side table.** Motivation: the hot `timeseries` row must not carry measurement semantics. New schema: `timeseries(id, container_id, value_type, shepard_id)` + `channel_metadata(id, timeseries_id FK+CASCADE, container_id, measurement, field, device, location, symbolic_name, UNIQUE(container_id,measurement,field,symbolic_name,device,location))`. JPA mapping via `@SecondaryTable(name="channel_metadata", pkJoinColumns=@PrimaryKeyJoinColumn(name="timeseries_id"))` тАФ zero blast radius to all callers (same constructors, getters, JPQL filters). Upsert replaced with two-step native SQL (INSERT timeseries RETURNING id тЖТ INSERT channel_metadata ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING тЖТ orphan cleanup on race). Flyway: `V1.14.0__drop_5tuple_from_core_timeseries.sql` + rollback sibling. **This is a stepping stone тАФ see TS-SEMANTIC-01 for the Neo4j migration.** | L | **тЬУ shipped 2026-05-26** | `TimeseriesEntity.java` + `TimeseriesRepository.java` + V1.14.0 migration. Gated MFFD-SHARED-CONTAINER-01. |
| TS-SEMANTIC-01 | **Dual-write `channel_metadata` to Neo4j `SemanticAnnotation / AnnotatableTimeseries` nodes.** TS-CORE-SCHEMA-01 is Phase 1 (clean Postgres schema). This is Phase 2: after a successful `channel_metadata` INSERT, `TimeseriesSemanticDualWriteService.dualWriteChannelMetadata()` creates `SemanticAnnotation` nodes for each non-blank field, linked via `AnnotatableTimeseries` in Neo4j. Best-effort: Neo4j failures are caught at WARN; Postgres write is never rolled back. `AnnotatableTimeseries.appId` = `TimeseriesEntity.shepardId` (bridges PostgresтЖФNeo4j for Phase 3). Phase 3 (TS-SEMANTIC-02): flip reads to Neo4j and drop `channel_metadata`. | M | **тЬУ shipped 2026-05-26** | `TimeseriesSemanticDualWriteService.java` + `TimeseriesRepository.java` (RETURNING id, shepard_id). | OTVIS-PARSE-1 | **`shepard-plugin-fileformat-thermography` tier-1 тАФ Edevis OTvis metadata parser.** Standalone Maven module (NOT yet wired into the aggregator тАФ see Jandex hang note in install.md). Confirms (or rejects) the hypotheses in `aidocs/integrations/115 ┬з0`. All three streams CONFIRMED end-to-end against Rev H spec: 28-byte header (16B magic `DIFFJPBG00000001` + uint32 LE width/height/DataFormat), OpenCV DataFormat codes (0/2/5/13/24), calibration LUT is bare 65,536 little-endian float32. Surprise: aidocs/115 ┬з0 had sequence roles swapped тАФ the lock-in COMPLEX result lives in `sequence0/f0.bin` (DataFormat=13), the raw uint16 reference frame in `sequence1/f<N>.bin` (DataFormat=2). Calibration LUT verified by mapping the raw frame to 22.3-24.8 degC (MFFD shop room temperature). |
| OTVIS-TIER2-EXTRACTOR | **`OTvisFrameExtractor` тАФ open tar, decode frames using the confirmed Rev H layout, apply calibration.** For each `f<N>.bin`: skip 16-byte magic, read three little-endian uint32 (W, H, DataFormat), dispatch on DataFormat (uint8=1, uint16=2, float32=4, complex={float Real; float Imag}=8, BGR=3 bytes/pixel), unpack `W * H * bpp` payload bytes. Complex frames: amplitude=hypot(re,im), phase=atan2(im,re). uint16 frames: apply sequence-wide `calibration.bin` LUT (65,536 floats, indexed by raw uint16). Per-frame `c<N>.bin` overrides take precedence when present. Fall back to fail-soft `urn:shepard:thermography:tier2Status="failed"` on any IO error. INFL compression (per Rev H pages 3-4) deferred тАФ no MFFD fixture exercises it. Multi-frame stacked files: cross-reference `content.xml/Sequence[id]/FrameInfo/Frame[@TarFileHeaderDataOffset]` for absolute byte offsets. | M | **тЬУ shipped 2026-05-28** | `6d5dde623..dbf5c4c2d`. Five value-object classes (`ExtractedFrames`, `LockInResultFrame`, `RawCalibratedFrame`, `CalibrationLut`, `RecurringHeader`) + pure `OTvisFrameExtractor` with `extract(InputStream)`/`extract(Path)`. DataFormat dispatch is **header-driven** (per byte-layout-notes ┬з2 authority тАФ content.xml absence is recorded as `partialReason` but does not block decoding). 8 new JUnit tests green (43/43 in module total, 4 pre-existing @Disabled probe tests retained): happy-path against MFFD fixture, two degraded-input cases (missing content.xml; truncated calibration.bin), two negative paths (non-tar bytes, empty stream тАФ both `IOException`), three pure-helper tests. INFL compression + HIDDEN TOC seek deferred per byte-layout-notes ┬з5; OME-Zarr writer + REST plumbing land separately in OTVIS-TIER2-OMEZARR. |
| OTVIS-TIER2-OMEZARR | **OME-Zarr writer + derived-dataset wire-up.** Convert extracted frames (raw degC / amplitude / phase) to OME-Zarr v3 store at Garage S3 under `thermography/{fileReferenceAppId}/`. Create one `OTvisDerivedDataset` SD-payload entity on the parent DO (no new DataObject тАФ DO-sprawl containment). Decide JZarr (BSD-3) vs Python sidecar at this step. Layout per `aidocs/ops/vis-s2-garage-omezarr-storage-policy.md ┬з2`: `thermography/{fileReferenceAppId}/` root group with `amplitude/`, `phase/`, `raw/`, `calibration/` sub-arrays; `zarr.json` v3 descriptors with `bytes` codec little-endian and default `c/i/j/k` chunk-key encoding. Missing sub-arrays are skipped without breaking the store. Runtime sink wiring needs the backend Jandex hang resolved first (OTVIS-WIRE-AGGREGATOR-1). |

## REF-EDIT-* тАФ Reference-type edit + create completeness (plugin beta gate)

Policy: per CLAUDE.md rule "every reference type ships a complete create + edit + delete UI", each reference type must reach all-four-surfaces (create / edit / delete / list) before it can be promoted to `beta`. Entries below track each type's gap. **REF-EDIT-3 (FileReference rename) is XS and should be taken first.**

**Cross-cutting requirement (2026-05-28 user directive): template-driven create is for ALL reference types.** Every Create dialog (File, FileBundle, Timeseries, StructuredData, URI, Video, plugin-defined) must pre-fill from a parent-DataObject `ShepardTemplate` if one carries reference-creation hints. This is not optional and not scoped to TimeseriesReference. Each REF-EDIT-* row below carries a template-driven-create deliverable; rows shipped before this clarification (REF-EDIT-3, REF-EDIT-6) have a follow-up `REF-EDIT-TPL-*` row.

| ID | Item | Size | Status | Priority | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| REF-EDIT-1 | **TimeseriesReference: channel selection + time-bounds edit + template-driven creation.** No edit path currently exists for the five 5-tuple channel fields or the `startNs`/`endNs` window bounds after creation. Required: (1) Edit dialog on `TimeseriesReference` detail page covering 5-tuple + optional time bounds тАФ calls `PATCH /v2/timeseries-references/{appId}` (endpoint already exists for TM1a time-alignment fields; extend to cover channel+bounds); (2) Template-driven creation wizard: if a `ShepardTemplate` for the parent DataObject carries a `urn:shepard:reference:channelSelection` annotation, the creation form pre-fills channel keys and default window; (3) LUMEN seed demo template for `rocket_engine` DataObjects. ## PERM-INHERIT-REVIEW тАФ child-entity permission inheritance audit

Triggered 2026-05-29 while granting flo READ access on the microsections
showcase Collection (`019e7243-f995-7914-be80-53e367aa5172`). Observation:
granting on the Collection only тАФ and not on DataObjects or FileReferences тАФ
worked because those child entities **do not** carry their own `:Permissions`
nodes in this codebase. They inherit via `PermissionsService` walking the
parent graph. That's good for the showcase but worth a focused audit:

| ID | Item | Size | Status | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| PERM-INHERIT-01 | **Map every entity kind to its perm source.** Walk the codebase: which entities have their own `:has_permissions -> :Permissions` edge (`Collection`, `FileContainer`, `TimeseriesContainer`, `StructuredDataContainer`, тАж), and which inherit from a parent (`DataObject`, `SingletonFileReference`, `TimeseriesReference`, `StructuredDataReference`, `GitReference`, `VideoStreamReference`, `HdfReference`, тАж). Build a single audit table. | S | **done** | Shipped 2026-05-29 тАФ full matrix at `aidocs/data/PERM-INHERIT-MATRIX.md` covers ~40 entity kinds with Java entity file + line citations; surfaces the container footgun explicitly (containers own perms because they are multi-attachable). |
| PERM-INHERIT-02 | **Document the inheritance walk algorithm.** What is the exact lookup chain `PermissionsService` uses for a `SingletonFileReference` тЖТ `DataObject` тЖТ `Collection`? For a `TimeseriesReference`? For a `VideoStreamReference`? Are there short-circuits when an intermediate has its own perms record? Codify in `aidocs/platform/24-permission-system-review.md`. | S | **done** | Shipped 2026-05-29 тАФ codified as ┬з9 of `aidocs/platform/24-permission-system-review.md` (pseudocode, per-entity expansion, five short-circuit invariants, BUG-148 anti-regression note). |
| PERM-INHERIT-03 | **Verify FileContainer perms grant flow.** When an operator wants to "give flo access to this Collection and all its data," what's the correct set of PUTs? Today: Collection (covers DOs + Refs via inheritance) PLUS each top-level FileContainer / TSContainer / SDContainer that's referenced. Surface this as a single admin endpoint `POST /v2/collections/{appId}/permissions/cascade` that walks all referenced containers + applies the same perms. | M | **gated on aidocs/platform/110** | Without this, "grant access to a Collection" requires N+1 client-side PUTs and is easy to get wrong. Showcase setups should not need to script this. **Decision gate 2026-05-29:** the operator-question is whether the cascade endpoint is the right *shape* or just the local fix to a model that needs redesigning. Decision doc `aidocs/platform/110-permissions-redesign-decision.md` (PERM-REDESIGN-DECISION) lays out four options + recommendation (A+D: ship cascade endpoint *with* a formalized `AuthzProvider` SPI promoting the existing F6 seam). PERM-INHERIT-03 ships once aidocs/110 is resolved. |
| PERM-INHERIT-04 | **Audit `BUG-148` scope.** The 2026-05-23 fix seeded `:Permissions` on newly-created DataObjects to fix a 403-after-create regression. That contradicts the "DOs inherit from Collection" model surfaced today. Confirm whether that fix shipped, whether it's still in effect, and whether it's a hidden divergence between DO and Reference inheritance. | XS | **done** | Shipped 2026-05-29 тАФ premise was wrong: no perms-seed fix ever shipped. `4f246fe5b` closed BUG-148 as works-as-designed (DOs inherit, verified live: 17,149/17,149 lack `:Permissions`, all writes succeed). `6e22b407e` shipped V90 migration that *removes* wrongly-attached `:Permissions` from `:DataObject`/`:BasicReference` + `DataObjectServiceTest` anti-regression. Full reconcile in `aidocs/data/PERM-INHERIT-MATRIX.md ┬з4`. |
| PERM-REDESIGN-DECISION | **Decide whether the permissions system gets redesigned or extended in place.** PERM-INHERIT-03's cascade endpoint solves an operator pain today but doesn't answer the structural question: is the dual ownership model (containers own, DOs inherit) the right long-term shape, or a footgun we keep patching? Doc `aidocs/platform/110-permissions-redesign-decision.md` lays out four options тАФ A (status quo + cascade), B (pure inheritance), C (external policy engine тАФ Casbin/SpiceDB/OpenFGA), D (plugin-first AuthzProvider SPI), E (graph-native ReBAC) тАФ with explicit trade-off matrix, opposing-camp critiques, and a recommendation (A+D). Persona consult: Role 4 (IME/AQE) pushes toward C/D/E for ABAC; Role 9 (reluctant senior researcher) pushes toward A alone. | S (decision doc; impl is M+M for A+D) | **idea** | Doc lands at stage `idea` тЖТ flip to `feature-defined` on operator + persona sign-off тЖТ implementation tickets PERM-INHERIT-03 (cascade) + PERM-AUTHZ-SPI (D) split out from the decision. Gates PERM-INHERIT-03. |

**Why now:** the microsections seed (`f5775aa7e`) ran against a Collection
that bob owned. Granting flo via a single Collection-level PUT propagated to
all 8 DataObjects + 16 FileReferences as expected тАФ which is the desired
behaviour. But for any showcase that uses top-level `FileContainer` /
`TimeseriesContainer` (e.g. LUMEN, MFFD), the same one-call grant would
silently miss the container payloads. That's a real footgun for operators
and worth fixing structurally rather than documenting around.

## TS-INGEST-222GB-READINESS тАФ MFFD timeseries ingest pre-flight

**Status 2026-05-29:** operator reports ~222 GB of timeseries data still
exporting from the MFFD source instance. `mffd-data.7z` (107 GB raw archive)
is already on UNAS at `/mnt/pve/unas/dump/mffd-data.7z`. Once the export
completes the v15 importer (see `examples/mffd-showcase/scripts/`) will run
against the live shepard backend.

**Capacity snapshot (2026-05-29):**

| Substrate | Now | Headroom | 222 GB raw impact |
|---|---|---|---|
| Host disk (rpool) | 79 G / 500 G (16%) | 421 G | ~15-22 G after TimescaleDB compression тЖТ fits |
| TimescaleDB hypertable | 18 MB / 113 channels / 82 chunks (all compressed) / 1.17 M points | unlimited | DB-OPT3 chunk policy already tuned; no schema migration needed |
| Garage S3 | 30 blocks (~minimal) | shared with rpool | absorbs NDT/file payloads, OTvis stores |
| UNAS (staging) | 2.1 T / 19 T | 17 T free | source archive lives here; landing-zone OK |
| Neo4j metadata | (not measured here, presumed OK) | watch | **real risk** тАФ channel cardinality ├Ч DO fanout |

**Real risks (not disk-space):**

| ID | Risk | Status | Mitigation |
|---|---|---|---|
| TS-INGEST-222GB-NEO4J | Neo4j `:Timeseries` metadata sprawl тАФ every channel becomes one `:Timeseries` node + one `:TimeseriesReference` per DataObject that exposes it. At 222 GB raw, channel count likely 1000+; per-DO referenceIds array balloons. OGM hydration cost on DataObject GET. | queued | DB-OPT5 already trims `referenceIds` from the default DataObject list payload (shipped); per-DO `referenceCount` covers the count case. The full ref list is still on the detail page. Verify post-ingest. |
| TS-INGEST-222GB-PGBOUNCER | PgBouncer pool exhaustion during peak write burst. | queued | PgBouncer is already in stack (#77 shipped). The v15 importer uses 4 worker processes; check `pgbouncer_stats` mid-ingest. If saturated: bump `max_client_conn` or stagger workers. |
| TS-INGEST-222GB-COMPRESSION | Live writes land in the latest uncompressed chunk; compression policy sweeps after a chunk closes. During 222 GB ingest, the active chunk could grow large before the policy fires. | queued | DB-OPT3 set `chunk_time_interval`; verify a closed chunk fires recompression within minutes (timescale `compress_chunk_policy`). Watch `timescaledb_information.jobs` next_start vs last_finish. |
| TS-INGEST-222GB-DOSPRAWL | If the v15 importer creates one DataObject per process-step ├Ч channel-group, the per-Collection DataObject count could reach 5-figure territory. Collection landing page rendering breaks per task #25 (graph displays scale linearly, BATCH-API mitigations land later). | queued | Verify the importer's DO-fanout shape before ingest. If high-fanout, pre-import: stage with `--dry-run` and review the DO plan. UI-020 bulk lab-journal endpoint (#194) already mitigated one N+1 at MFFD scale; check for analogous N+1 risks on the new shape. |
| TS-INGEST-222GB-PROVENANCE | Every channel write should produce a typed `:Activity` per f(ai)┬▓r. At 1000+ channels ├Ч millions of writes, `:Activity` row count could outpace useful query plans. | queued | Activity capture for TS data is **disabled by default** today; the importer writes through `X-Source-User-*` headers but no per-data-point activity. PROV-USER-MIRROR-ENDPOINT (#229) + PROV-USER-ENRICH (#234) already wire the importer-run granularity. Verify post-ingest that Activity row growth is bounded to per-import-run, not per-data-point. |
| TS-INGEST-222GB-GARAGE | Binary file attachments (NDT scans, calibration files, OTvis tar bundles, mesh files) accompany the TS export. Garage S3 bucket lifecycle policy + chunk-size + replication factor (set to 1 today, single-node) need verification. | queued | `shepard-garage` is the only s3 backend; bucket is `shepard-files`; chunked-encoding disabled. Verify bucket has no quota; pre-create lifecycle rules for retention if downstream requires them. |

**Pre-flight checklist (run before `make redeploy-backend` + before `python3 examples/mffd-showcase/scripts/import_mffd.py`):**

1. Snapshot the current TimescaleDB hypertable + Neo4j (per PRE-MUT-SNAP family).
2. Confirm `mffd-data.7z` is fully transferred + unpacks cleanly on UNAS.
3. Re-run `examples/mffd-showcase/seed.py --warmup-only` to confirm v15 importer can reach the backend with the current bob/flo API keys.
4. Verify `application.properties` does NOT have a permissive `shepard.timeseries.cap` or `shepard.permissions.default-owner` mismatch.
5. Tail `infrastructure-backend-1` logs for the first 10 minutes of ingest; check for adaptive-backoff log lines.
6. Mid-ingest: every ~30 min, snapshot `pg_stat_activity` + `timescaledb_information.jobs` + Neo4j `dbms.queryJmx` for blocked queries.
7. Post-ingest: re-run DB-OPT family probes тАФ EXPLAIN ANALYZE on the hot-path queries against the now-realistic-volume data.

**This row supersedes** the loose "MFFD timeseries ingest in progress"
references in memory. It is the single planning-and-readiness ledger for the
222 GB event.

| ID | Item | Size | Status | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| TS-INGEST-222GB-NEO4J | (see risks table above) | M | queued | Verify post-ingest; mitigations exist (DB-OPT5). |
| TS-INGEST-222GB-PGBOUNCER | (see risks table above) | S | queued | Live tail mid-ingest. |
| TS-INGEST-222GB-COMPRESSION | (see risks table above) | S | queued | Confirm policy sweep cadence. |
| TS-INGEST-222GB-DOSPRAWL | (see risks table above) | M | queued | Pre-import dry-run inspection. |
| TS-INGEST-222GB-PROVENANCE | (see risks table above) | S | queued | Verify Activity bounded to importer-run granularity. |

Reuses `shepard.measures.itself` observability primitives. | S | queued | NICE | Lets the operator watch a single page during the 222 GB write rather than juggling psql + cypher-shell + garage stats. |
